Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Introduction to Sam'iyyat: Belief in the Unseen
Opening and closing lines establishing Sam'iyyat and its authority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what Sam'iyyat are and why it is obligatory for every Muslim to believe in the matters of the afterlife and unseen that are conveyed by revelation.

Core Idea
Sam'iyyat are beliefs that come only from revelation and are as certain as necessary knowledge.

The third section of the creed deals with matters that cannot be known by reason alone—only through divine revelation. These are called Sam'iyyat (hearing-based matters). The poet begins by stating that belief in these is necessary, and concludes by affirming that everything the Prophet brought becomes like necessary knowledge. This lesson introduces the category and its foundational principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening line
Read the first line 'القسم الثالث: السمعيات' and its translation. Notice that the author classifies this as the third section of Aqeedah.
This establishes the context for the rest of the beliefs.
2
Understand the obligation
Focus on the phrase 'ويلزم الإيمان' (it is necessary to believe). Ask yourself: why must we believe these things? How do we come to know them?
3
Read the final lines
Read the last two lines about everything the Prophet brought becoming like necessary knowledge (الضروري). This explains the epistemic status of Sam'iyyat.
4
Reflect on the overall message
Consider how the opening and closing lines frame the entire list. The poet is saying that these beliefs are not optional but are as certain as basic logical truths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
ويلزم الإيمان بالحساب * والحشر والعقاب والثواب
والنشر والصراط والميزان * والحوض والنيران والجنان
والجن والأملاك ثم الأنبيا * والحور والولدان ثم الأوليا
وكل ما جاء عن البشير * من كل حكم صار كالضروري
وينطوي في كلمة الإسلام * ما قد مضى من سائر الأحكام
The third section: Sam'iyyat (hearing-based matters)
And it is necessary to believe in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, and the Reward,
and the Resurrection, the Path (Sirat), and the Balance, and the Basin, the Fires, and the Gardens,
and the Jinn, the Angels, then the Prophets, and the Hoor, the Boys (wildan), then the Saints (awliya),
and everything that came from the Bringer of Glad Tidings (the Prophet) of every ruling became like the necessary knowledge,
and it is contained in the word of Islam what has passed of all the other rulings.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the sam'iyyat – matters known only through revelation that must be believed. The poet lists: belief in the Reckoning (hisab), the Gathering (hashr), punishment and reward; the Resurrection (nashr), the Bridge (sirat), the Scale (mizan), the Basin (hawd), Hell (niran), Paradise (jinan); the unseen creatures: jinn, angels; then prophets, the celestial maidens (hur), and youths (wildan), and the saints (awliya). The last line states that everything the Prophet (al-bashir) brought from rulings becomes like necessary knowledge (daruri) for the believer, and that the word of Islam encompasses all these rulings.

Key Terms
السمعيات
الضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only a few afterlife events must be believed, and that matters like the Basin (Hawd) or saints (Awliya) are optional.
Correction: The passage explicitly lists all these items as necessary (ويلزم) to believe, and the last line states that everything the Prophet brought becomes like necessary knowledge, leaving no room for omission.

Checkpoint
What does the poet say about the rulings brought by the Prophet (al-bashir)?
A) They are optional for believers.
B) They become like necessary knowledge (daruri).
C) They are only for scholars.
D) They are only about the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Sam'iyyat are beliefs that come only from revelation, and every believer must affirm them with the same certainty as basic logical truths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just recited a list of unseen realities that your Prophet brought. Which of these do you find hardest to truly internalize in your daily life? Does your heart feel certain about these, or do doubts creep in? What step will you take today to strengthen your conviction in even one of these?
?
The passage says these beliefs are 'like necessary knowledge'—as certain as knowing that fire burns. Do you treat them with that level of certainty? If not, what is holding you back from that conviction, and what will you do to change that starting today?
?
Imagine standing before the Sirat (the Path) tomorrow based on your current actions. Would you be confident to cross it? What specific change in your life will you make so that you can face that moment with hope?

Eschatological Events: Reckoning to Gardens
Specific enumeration of eschatological beliefs from Reckoning to Gardens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the specific eschatological events that every Muslim must believe in: the Reckoning, Gathering, Punishment, Reward, Resurrection, Bridge, Balance, Basin, Hell, and Paradise.

Core Idea
Belief in the afterlife includes specific events: Reckoning, Gathering, Resurrection, Bridge, Balance, Basin, Hell, and Paradise.

After introducing Sam'iyyat, the poet immediately lists the key events of the Day of Judgment and the afterlife. These are not abstract concepts but concrete realities that every Muslim must affirm. This lesson focuses on those events from the Reckoning to the Gardens.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list
Read the second line: 'ويلزم الإيمان بالحساب * والحشر والعقاب والثواب'. Notice that belief in each of these is mandatory.
2
Continue the list
Read the third line: 'والنشر والصراط والميزان * والحوض والنيران والجنان'. These are more events and realms.
The order is not necessarily chronological but covers major eschatological realities.
3
Reflect on each term
Consider the meaning of each term: Reckoning (حساب), Gathering (حشر), Punishment (عقاب), Reward (ثواب), Resurrection (نشر), Bridge (صراط), Balance (ميزان), Basin (حوض), Fires (نيران), Gardens (جنان).
These are all based on Quran and Sunnah.
4
Connect to obligation
Remember that the verb 'ويلزم' applies to each of these. They are not optional.

A) The Reckoning (Hisab)

Key Takeaway
Belief in the afterlife includes specific, named events and realms that every Muslim must affirm as part of their faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The poet says belief in these events is necessary (ويلزم). Which of these events do you find most difficult to truly internalize as real? Why, and what is one step you can take this week to strengthen your certainty in it?
?
If you knew that the record of your deeds would be shown to you today, what would you wish you had done differently this past week? What can you do right now to start changing that?
?
Imagine standing on the Path (الصراط) — a bridge over Hell. What attachment to this world might cause you to slip? What can you let go of today to lighten your crossing?

Unseen Beings and Prophetic Authority
Enumeration of unseen beings and concluding principle on prophetic teachings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in unseen beings (jinn, angels, prophets, houris, wildan, awliya) and the authority of the Prophet's teachings are obligatory parts of Islamic creed.

Core Idea
Belief in jinn, angels, prophets, houris, boys, and saints is as necessary as belief in the afterlife.

The poet continues the list of Sam'iyyat by including beings that are not normally perceived: jinn, angels, prophets, houris, wildan, and awliya. He then concludes with a general principle: everything the Prophet brought is as certain as necessary knowledge. This lesson focuses on these beings and the final statement on prophetic authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth line
Read 'والجن والأملاك ثم الأنبيا * والحور والولدان ثم الأوليا'. Identify each category.
2
Understand each term
Briefly consider what each term refers to: Jinn (الجن), Angels (الأملاك), Prophets (الأنبيا), Houris (الحور), Wildan (الولدان), Awliya (الأوليا).
3
Read the final line
Read 'وكل ما جاء عن البشير * من كل حكم صار كالضروري'. Understand that this affirms the absolute authority of the Prophet's teachings.
4
Connect to Islam
Read 'وينطوي في كلمة الإسلام * ما قد مضى من سائر الأحكام'. Realize that all these beliefs are contained within the word 'Islam'.

?

?
When you are alone and no one sees, does your belief in the jinn, angels, and the ever-present awareness of Allah shape your actions, or do you forget the unseen witnesses? How will you remind yourself today?
?
The poem says the entire word of Islam contains all these beliefs. Is there any category—like belief in the saints (awliya) or the houris—that you have neglected or doubted? What step will you take to affirm it fully?

The Third Section: Matters of the Unseen
The author enumerates the articles of belief in samiyyat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of samiyyat (matters of the unseen) and the obligation of faith in the specific articles enumerated by the author.

Core Idea
Belief in the unseen matters transmitted by revelation is an essential part of Islam.

In this lesson, we examine the third and final section of the poem, which deals with al-samiyyat—the articles of faith that are known only through revelation. The author lists key eschatological events and beings that every Muslim must believe in, emphasizing that these are not optional but integral to the word of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic verses and the translation. Notice the list format and the poetic rhyme.
The asterisks separate verses.
2
Categorize the listed items
Group the items into events (reckoning, gathering, punishment, reward, resurrection, path, balance, pond, fires, gardens) and beings (jinn, angels, prophets, houris, boys, saints).
This helps in memorization and understanding the breadth of samiyyat.
3
Reflect on the final lines
The last two lines declare that everything from the Prophet (al-bashir) is like necessary knowledge (daruri) and that these rulings are contained in 'the word of Islam.' This shows that belief in samiyyat is mandatory.
The phrase 'like the necessary' means it is certain and obligatory to accept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
ويلزم الإيمان بالحساب * والحشر والعقاب والثواب
والنشر والصراط والميزان * والحوض والنيران والجنان
والجن والأملاك ثم الأنبيا * والحور والولدان ثم الأوليا
وكل ما جاء عن البشير * من كل حكم صار كالضروري
وينطوي في كلمة الإسلام * ما قد مضى من سائر الأحكام
The third section: the matters of the unseen (samiyyat). And faith in the reckoning, the gathering, the punishment, and the reward is required; and the resurrection, the path, the balance, the pond, the fires, the gardens, the jinn, the angels, then the prophets, the houris, the boys, then the saints; and everything that came from the bringer of good tidings, of every ruling, became like the necessary; and it is contained in the word of Islam: what has passed of all the rulings.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of the articles of belief in the third section of the poem, called 'al-samiyyat' (the matters heard/transmitted from revelation). The author states that faith is required in a list of eschatological events and beings: the reckoning (ḥisāb), the gathering (ḥashr), punishment (ʿiqāb) and reward (thawāb), the resurrection (nashr), the path (ṣirāṭ), the balance (mīzān), the pond (ḥawḍ), the fires (nīrān), the gardens (jinnān), the jinn, the angels, then the prophets (anbiyā), the houris (ḥūr), the boys (wildān), then the saints (awliyā). He then states that everything that came from the Prophet (al-bashīr) regarding any ruling has become like necessary knowledge (ḍarūrī) in terms of certainty, and it is encompassed within the word of Islam—all that has passed of the various rulings. The passage thus defines the scope of samiyyat and emphasizes that these transmitted beliefs are integral to Islam.

السَّمْعِيَّات
الحساب
الحشر
العقاب
الثواب
النشر
الصراط
الميزان

النيران
الجنان
الجن
الأملاك
الأنبيا
الحور
الولدان
الأوليا
البشير
الضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Belief in samiyyat is optional or merely symbolic.
Correction: The passage shows that faith in these unseen matters is obligatory and essential to the word of Islam.

Checkpoint
In the samiyyat section, which of the following is NOT explicitly listed as an article of faith?
A) The balance (mīzān)
B) The pond (ḥawḍ)
C) The throne (ʿarsh)
D) The path (ṣirāṭ)

Key Takeaway
Belief in the samiyyat—the unseen matters conveyed by revelation—is a required component of faith in Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in the reality of every item listed in this passage—the balance, the pond, the path—as firmly as you believe in your own existence? Or do you merely nod along? What would change in your daily life if you took each one seriously?
?
The poet says every ruling from the Prophet became 'like the necessary.' Is there any ruling from him that you have been treating as optional or negotiable? How will you begin to realign your heart with that truth starting today?
?
The passage ends by saying these beliefs are contained in the word of Islam. If you stripped away all that you believe about the unseen, would your 'Islam' still be the same? What does that reveal about the state of your faith?

Ru'ya in the Afterlife: Paradise and the Resurrection
Imam Dardeer discusses the locations of ru'ya in the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two occasions when believers see Allah in the afterlife and the majority view that disbelievers do not see Him.

Core Idea
Believers see Allah in Paradise and at the Resurrection, but disbelievers remain veiled.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary addresses the question of when and where the beatific vision (ru'ya) occurs in the afterlife. He affirms that believers will see Allah in the Garden of Eternity, and also on the Plain of Resurrection based on the Sunnah. A minority opinion suggesting disbelievers might see Allah as torment is mentioned but rejected by the majority. The passage clarifies the Sunni position that only believers enjoy this vision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two locations
Read the passage and highlight where ru'ya occurs: Jannat al-Khuld and arsat al-qiyama.
Note that 'arsa' means an open courtyard.
2
Understand the majority view
Pay attention to footnote (7) which states the majority consensus that disbelievers do not see Allah.
This corrects the minority view mentioned in the main text.
3
Consider the attributes of majesty
Notice the phrase 'sifat al-jalal' – seeing Allah in His majestic attributes is possible for all who see Him.
This concept will be developed in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقولي: في جنة الخلد، وأمّا في عرصات القيامة ففي السُّنَّةِ ما يقتضي وقوعها فيها للمؤمنين أيضًا وهو الصحيح، بل قيل: وللكُفَّار () ليكونَ الحِجْبُ عليهم حشرة، ولا مانعَ مِنْ أَنْ يَرَوه في صِفاتِ الجلال.
(٦) جمع «عرصة» وهي كل موضع واسع لا بناء فيه، والمراد به هنا مواقف القيامة. [القاموس المحيط ١٩٦/٣]
(۷) لكن الصحيح الذي عليه الجمهور أن المنافقين والكفار لا يرونه اتفاقاً. [سباعى، ص ٤١٥]
And my saying: In the Garden of Eternity, and as for the courtyards of the Resurrection, there is in the Sunnah what indicates its occurrence there for the believers as well, and that is the correct view. Rather it is said: And for the disbelievers, so that the veil would be a torment upon them, and there is no impediment to them seeing Him in the attributes of majesty.
(6) Plural of 'arsa, which is any wide place with no building in it, intended here as the stations of the Resurrection.
(7) But the correct view on which the majority is that the hypocrites and disbelievers do not see Him, by consensus.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage classifies the location of ru'ya in the afterlife. The author first states that ru'ya occurs in the Garden of Eternity (Jannat al-Khuld). He then adds that, according to the Sunnah, it also occurs in the courtyards (arsat) of the Resurrection for believers, and this is the correct view. A minority opinion is mentioned that even disbelievers might see Allah at that time as a form of torment (hijab), but the author does not affirm this. In fact, footnote (7) clarifies that the majority holds that hypocrites and disbelievers will not see Allah by consensus. The passage also notes that seeing Him in the attributes of majesty (sifat al-jalal) is possible. The footnotes explain the meaning of 'arsat and reaffirm the Sunni position that only believers see Allah in the afterlife.

Key Terms
جنة الخلد (Jannat al-Khuld)
عرصات القيامة (arsat al-qiyama)
حجاب (hijab)
صفات الجلال (sifat al-jalal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think disbelievers will see Allah in the afterlife as a form of punishment.
Correction: The majority Sunni view, affirmed by Imam Dardeer, is that disbelievers and hypocrites will not see Allah at all; the veil is a torment, not the vision itself.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where does ru'ya occur besides the Garden of Eternity?
A) Only in Paradise.
B) In the courtyards of the Resurrection.
C) In Hell for the disbelievers.
D) Only in the attributes of majesty.

Key Takeaway
Believers will see Allah in both Paradise and at the Resurrection, while disbelievers will not see Him, in accordance with the majority Sunni position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to see your Lord in Paradise and at the Resurrection, or have you become comfortable with veils of distraction that keep you from Him? What will you change today to ensure you are among those who see Him?
?
If you knew that at the Resurrection you would be veiled from Allah like the disbelievers, would that thought terrify you into repentance? How would your actions today be different if you truly feared that veil?
?
The veil is described as a torment for the disbelievers—while you still have breath, are you living in a way that seeks to remove any veil between you and Allah, or are you building veils through negligence? What is one step you can take right now to draw closer to Him?

Unseen Matters
beginner
5 min
Seeing Allah in Dreams: Heart-Vision Not Eye-Vision
Imam Dardeer discusses dream-vision as heart-vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true dream-visions of Allah are heart-based spiritual experiences, not physical sight, and that the righteous have experienced this without compromising Allah's transcendence.

Core Idea
Dream vision of Allah is heart-vision, not eye-vision.

The possibility of seeing Allah in dreams is a delicate topic. The majority of Sunni scholars affirm it for the righteous, but they insist it is a vision of the heart, not the eyes. This passage by Imam Dardeer establishes that distinction and provides important context to protect against misunderstanding and false claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice the footnote markers—they contain further scholarly discussion.
2
Identify the author's core claim
Look for the phrase 'a type of witnessing that occurs with the heart, not with the eye.' This is the central thesis: dream-vision is spiritual, not physical.
3
Note the majority view and supporting story
The footnote mentions that most scholars permit it, citing consensus and the anecdote of Imam Ahmad seeing Allah in a dream ninety-nine times. This reinforces the legitimacy of such visions for the righteous.
4
Understand the warning about false visions
The footnote also warns: if the seen one appears with created attributes or commands contrary to Sharia, it is the devil. This safeguards against deception.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why the author stresses 'bi al-qalb la bi al-ayn'. This protects Allah's transcendence—He is not seen with physical eyes in this world, even in dreams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما رؤيته تعالى في المنام (۱) فقد وقعت لكثير مِنَ الصالحينَ مِنْ سَلَفَ الأُمة وخلَفَهم، ولا خَفَاءَ فِي أَنها نَوعُ مُشاهدة تكونُ بالقَلْبِ (۲) لا بالعين.
(۱) الرؤية المنامية الله تعالى فيها خلاف والجمهور على الجواز بل حكى القاضي عياض عليه الاتفاق، ونقل أن الإمام أحمد رآه تسعاً وتسعين مرة، وقال: إن رأيته في تمام المائة لأسألنه، فلما رآه قال: بما يتقرب إليك المتقربون، قال: بتلاوة كلامي، فقال أبفهم أو بغير فهم؟ فقال: بفهم وبغير فهم. ولكن قد يُرى تعالى في المنام بصفة الحوادث ويأمر بما يخالف الشرع كإسقاط التكليف، وحينئذ فالمرئي الشيطان، ومن أطاعه وفعل بمقتضاه فهو ضال مضل قد خسر الدنيا والآخرة. [حاشية الصاوي على الجوهرة ص ٢٦٤] وقيل بالمنع، وعليه القاضي أبو بكر، لأن المرئي في المنام خيال ومثال، وذلك محال على القديم، واختلف فيها أيضا في اليقظة، هل وقعت لغيره ؟ و الصواب المنع لخبر مسلم [كتاب الفتن وأشراط الساعة، باب ذكر ابن صياد]: تعلموا أنه لن يرى أحد منكم ربه عز وجل حتى يموت).
(۲) لأن البصر في حال النوم مقبوض ، وغمض الأجفان المانع من الرؤية مشاهد محقق. [سباعي، ص ٤١٦]
And as for seeing Him, exalted, in a dream (1), it has occurred for many of the righteous among the predecessors and successors of the ummah, and there is no hiddenness that it is a type of witnessing that occurs with the heart (2), not with the eye.
(1) Dream vision of Allah, exalted, there is disagreement about it, and the majority permit it, rather Qadi Iyad reported consensus on it. And it is narrated that Imam Ahmad saw Him ninety-nine times and said: If I see Him in the hundredth, I will ask Him. When he saw him, he said: By what do those who draw near to You draw near? He said: By reciting My speech. He said: With understanding or without understanding? He said: With understanding and without understanding. But one may see Him, exalted, in a dream with the attribute of created things and he may command something contrary to the Sharia, such as dropping of obligation. In that case, the seen one is the devil. Whoever obeys him and acts according to it is misguided and misguiding, having lost this world and the afterlife. [Hashiyah al-Sawi on al-Jawhara, p. 264] And it is said that it is prohibited, and Qadi Abu Bakr holds this, because what is seen in a dream is an image and a likeness, and that is impossible for the Eternal. And there is disagreement about it in wakefulness, whether it occurred for other than him? And the correct view is prohibition due to Muslim's report [Book of Tribulations and Portents of the Hour, Chapter on Mention of Ibn Sayyad]: 'Know that none of you will see his Lord until he dies.'
(2) Because the sight during sleep is closed, and the closing of the eyelids, which prevents vision, is a witnessed reality.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of seeing Allah in dreams. The author states that it has occurred for many righteous people throughout the ummah, both early and later generations. He clarifies that this vision is a type of witnessing (mushahada) that occurs with the heart, not with the physical eye. The footnotes provide additional detail: the majority of scholars permit it, with some even claiming consensus. An anecdote about Imam Ahmad seeing Allah in a dream is cited. However, the footnote also warns that if the seen one appears with attributes of created things or commands something contrary to Sharia, it is the devil. A minority prohibition (by Qadi Abu Bakr) is noted, based on the impossibility of image/form in relation to Allah. The footnote also discusses the possibility of seeing Allah while awake (for other than the Prophet), citing a hadith that no one will see his Lord until he dies. The author's main point remains: dream-vision is possible and heart-based, not an eye-vision.

Key Terms
رؤية منامية (ru'ya manamiyya)
مشاهدة (mushahada)
بالقلب (bi al-qalb)
بالصر (bi al-basar)
خيال (khayal)
مثال (mithal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that seeing Allah in a dream means seeing Him with the physical eyes, or that such visions imply Allah has a form.
Correction: Imam Dardeer explicitly states it is a heart-vision, not eye-vision. The footnote also warns that if a form appears, it is the devil, not Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does one see Allah in a dream?
A) With the physical eye.
B) With the heart, not the eye.
C) Only in the form of a creation.
D) It is impossible for anyone.

Key Takeaway
Seeing Allah in dreams is a heart-vision that affirms the possibility of spiritual closeness without compromising Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your dream contradicts what you know of Islam, will you have the courage to reject it, even if it feels spiritual? What does this lesson teach you about humility before revelation?
?
When you long to see Allah, do you seek it only in dreams, or do you actively recite His speech as Imam Ahmad learned? What step will you take today to draw near to Him through His words?
?
Have you ever attributed a dream to Allah without checking it against the Sharia? How can you ensure you follow the guidance of this lesson and not be deceived by the devil?

The Prophet's Vision of Allah on the Night of Isra'
Imam Dardeer states the relied-upon view on the Prophet's vision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relied-upon Sunni view that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) saw Allah with his physical eyesight on the Night of Isra'.

Core Idea
The Prophet saw Allah with his eyes, not only his heart.

In this lesson, Imam Dardeer settles a debated issue: did the Prophet see Allah on the Night of Isra' with his eyes or just his heart? He presents the majority view of Ahl al-Sunna, which affirms direct visual sighting. This distinction is important for understanding the limits of prophetic experience and the nature of Allah's transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text slowly, noticing the key term 'al-mu'tamad' (the relied-upon view) and 'bil-basar' (with eyesight).
The footnote provides a scholarly context.
2
Understand the two views
Identify the two positions: the majority view (Ibn Abbas) that the Prophet saw with eyesight, and the alternative view (Aisha, Ibn Mas'ud) that he saw with the heart.
The author clearly prefers the first.
3
Grasp the theological significance
Reflect on why this matters: affirming vision without direction or limitation is consistent with Allah's transcendence while honoring the Prophet's special status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمُعْتَمَدُ أنَّ النبيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم راه ليلةَ الإسراءِ بالبَصَرِ لا بالقلب فقط (٣).
(٣) هذا ما ذهب إليه ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما، وعليه جمهور أهل السنة، ومقابله ما ذهبت إليه السيدة عائشة رضي اللها من أنه رأى ربه بقلبه وهو المشهور عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه. [سباعي، ص ٤١٥]
And the relied-upon view is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, saw Him on the night of Isra' with his eyesight (basar), not with the heart only (3).
(3) This is the view of Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, and upon it is the majority of Ahl al-Sunna. Opposed to it is the view of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, that he saw his Lord with his heart, and it is the famous view from Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage states the definitive position (al-mu'tamad) regarding the Prophet's vision of Allah on the night of Isra' and Mi'raj: the Prophet saw Allah with his physical eyesight (basar), not only with his heart. The footnote clarifies that this is the view of Ibn Abbas and the majority of Ahl al-Sunna. The alternative view, attributed to Aisha and Ibn Mas'ud, is that the Prophet saw Allah with his heart. The author presents the former as the relied-upon position, emphasizing that the physical eyesight was involved, though without implying direction or limitation, as per the earlier discussion.

Key Terms

الإسراء (al-Isra')
قلب (qalb)

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that affirming vision with the eyes implies Allah is located in a direction or is like created objects.
Correction: The Sunni position affirms vision without spatial direction or physical limitation, as Allah is not confined to place.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon view is that the Prophet saw Allah with his physical eyesight on the Night of Isra', not only with his heart.

Sam'iyyat and Belief in al-Hisab
Dardeer introduces the third division of theology (sam'iyyat) and defines belief in al-hisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the category of sam'iyyat in Islamic theology and the obligation to believe in al-hisab (the accounting).

Core Idea
Sam'iyyat are truths known only through revelation, and belief in them is obligatory.

This lesson introduces the third division of theology, sam'iyyat, which are matters known only through revelation. After covering ilahiyyat and nubuwwat, Imam Dardeer now turns to sam'iyyat, specifically the obligation of belief in the accounting (al-hisab). The passage clarifies that while reason cannot discover these truths, revelation makes them binding, and denial of them leads to disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three divisions of theology
Read the passage and note the three categories: ilahiyyat (divine matters), nubuwwat (prophecies), and sam'iyyat (transmitted matters).
This sets the context for the new material.
2
Define sam'iyyat
Understand that sam'iyyat are matters that cannot be known by reason alone; they require revelation. Reason does not affirm nor negate them.
This is a key distinction from the first two divisions.
3
Learn the meaning of al-hisab
The passage gives both a linguistic meaning (counting) and a terminological meaning (Allah stopping His servants in the gathering place for their deeds).
The definition involves divine speech, which is eternal and not composed of letters or sound.
4
Understand the obligation of belief
Belief in the sam'iyyat, including al-hisab, is obligatory upon every responsible person. Denial is kufr because it entails rejecting Allah and His Messenger.
This shows the serious nature of these beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
-٥ - ويلزم الإيمان بالحساب * والحشر والعقاب والثواب
ولما كانت مباحث هذا الفنّ ثلاثة : إلهيّاتٌ ونُبوّاتٌ وسَمْعيّات، وقد تَقَدَّمَ الكلام على بيان الأوَّلين شَرَعَ في الثالث وهو السمعيات (۱) فقال:
(وبلزم) أي: يجب على المكلفين (الإيمان) أي: التصديقُ (بالحساب)) وهو لغة: العدُّ، واصطلاحًا: توقيفُ الله عباده في المحشر على أعمالهم، فعلا أو قولا أو اعتقادًا، تفصيلا بأن يكلِّمهم الله تعالى بكلام قديم، لَيسَ بحَرفٍ ولا صوت (۳)، صَوت(۳)،
(۱) السمعيات هي الأمور التي لا تعرف إلا من السمع، وليس للعقل فيها مجال، أي أن العقل لا يقول بإثباتها ولا بنفيها، بل مدار ذلك على السمع. والسمعيات جميعها جائزة عقلا واجبة سمعا، ودليل وجوبها أنها أمور ممكنة عقلا أخبرنا بها الصادق على ما نطقت به النصوص، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو حق يجب شرعا قبوله، وهذا مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة وجمهور المعتزلة، ولا يحتاج الإيمان بما ذكر إلى بيان كيفية الحقيقة، فإن العقول تعجز عن مثل ذلك، وهو مما نقله الأئمة متواترا، فمن أنكر شيئا من السمعيات فهو كافر ، إذ يلزمه تكذيب الله ورسوله في خبريهما، وكذلك كل ما علم من الدين بالضرورة. [حاشية السباعي، ص ١٣٦]
الإيمان بالحساب
(۲) والإيمان بالحساب يجب وجوب الأصول من أنكره كفر لثبوته كتابا وسنة وإجماعا، ففي :الكتاب سَرِيعُ الْحِسَاب ﴾ [البقرة: ۲۰۲]، وفي السنة: (حاسبوا أنفسكم قبل أن تحاسبوا) سنن الترمذي، ح ٢٦٤٧]، وأجمع المسلمون عليه. (۳) لأن الحروف والأصوات كلها مخلوقة وكلامه تعالى غير مخلوق. وقال الفخر الرازي: أو بأن يسمعهم صوتا يدل على كلامه تعالى، وهذا الصوت يخلقه الله تعالى في أذن كل واحد من المكلفين ولكن هذا الصوت لا ينسب إلى الله تعالى إلا من جهة أنه مخلوق ،له لا أنه صفة قائمة بذاته، ولا أن هذا الصوت هو كلامه القديم.
The third section: the sam'iyyat. And necessary is belief in the accounting, and the gathering, and the punishment, and the reward. Since the topics of this art are three: divine matters (ilahiyyat), prophecies (nubuwwat), and transmitted matters (sam'iyyat), and the discussion on the first two has preceded, he began on the third, which is the sam'iyyat (1) and said: 'And binding is belief in the accounting' – i.e., obligatory upon the legally responsible – 'belief' i.e., affirmation of the accounting. It is linguistically counting, and terminologically: Allah's stopping His servants in the gathering place (mahshar) for their deeds, whether actions, words, or beliefs, in detail, by Allah Almighty speaking to them with eternal speech, not composed of letters or sound (3). (1) The sam'iyyat are the matters that are only known from revelation (sam'), and reason has no scope in them, i.e., reason does not affirm nor negate them, rather the criterion is revelation. All sam'iyyat are rationally possible and obligatory by revelation, and the proof of their obligation is that they are rationally possible matters informed to us by the truthful one (the Prophet) according to what the texts state, and everything that is so is true and must be accepted legally. This is the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and the majority of the Mu'tazila. Belief in what is mentioned does not require an explanation of the modality of the reality, for intellects are incapable of that, and it is among what the imams have transmitted as mutawatir. Whoever denies any of the sam'iyyat is a disbeliever, for it necessitates the denial of Allah and His Messenger in their reports, and likewise everything known necessarily from the religion. [Hashiya al-Siba'i, p. 136] Belief in the accounting. (2) Belief in the accounting is obligatory with the obligation of the fundamentals; whoever denies it is a disbeliever due to its establishment by the Book, Sunna, and consensus. In the Book: 'swift in reckoning' (Quran 2:202), and in the Sunna: 'Take account of yourselves before you are taken to account' (Tirmidhi, hadith 2647), and the Muslims are unanimous upon it. (3) Because letters and sounds are all created, and His speech is uncreated. And Fakhr al-Razi said: or by making them hear a sound that indicates His speech, and this sound Allah creates in the ear of each legally responsible person, but this sound is not attributed to Allah except in respect that it is created by Him, not that it is an attribute subsisting in His essence, nor that this sound is His eternal speech.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage introduces the third division of theology: sam'iyyat (transmitted matters known only through revelation). The author explains that after discussing ilahiyyat and nubuwwat, he now addresses sam'iyyat, specifically the obligation of belief in al-hisab (the accounting). He defines hisab linguistically and terminologically: it is Allah stopping His servants on the Day of Gathering to inform them of their deeds in detail through His eternal speech, which is not composed of letters or sound. The footnote clarifies that sam'iyyat are matters where reason has no say; they are rationally possible but obligatory only through revelation. Denial of any sam'iyyat is disbelief because it entails denying Allah and His Messenger. The author then emphasizes that belief in the accounting is obligatory as a fundamental principle, and its denial is kufr, citing Quran, hadith, and consensus. A further footnote discusses the nature of divine speech: it is uncreated, not composed of letters or sounds; some theologians suggest God creates a sound to communicate, but that sound is not His attribute.

Key Terms
سمعيات (sam'iyyat: transmitted matters)
حساب (hisab: accounting)
كلام قديم (qadim kalam: eternal speech)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the sam'iyyat are rationally knowable.
Correction: The passage clarifies they are only known through revelation; reason does not affirm nor negate them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the terminological meaning of al-hisab?
A) Counting of numbers
B) Allah stopping His servants in the gathering place for their deeds
C) The gathering of all creatures
D) The punishment of the wicked

Key Takeaway
Belief in al-hisab is a fundamental obligation established by revelation, and denial of any sam'iyyat leads to disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Necessity of Belief in the Reckoning (al-Hisab)
Dardeer defines al-Hisab, explains its necessity and modalities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition, modalities, and necessity of belief in al-Hisab (the Reckoning) as a sam'iyyat matter.

Core Idea
Belief in the Reckoning is obligatory; it is God's detailed accountability beyond literal counting.

Having covered divine matters and prophecies, Imam Dardeer now turns to the sam'iyyat—matters known only through revelation. The first of these is belief in the Reckoning (al-Hisab). This lesson unpacks its definition, varied forms, and the people it includes, all grounded in the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Hisab
Start by reading the passage's linguistic and terminological definition of al-Hisab. Notice the shift from 'counting' to 'God's detailed calling to account'.
The definition ties to Ash'ari theology about God's eternal speech.
2
Examine the modalities of the Reckoning
The passage describes the Reckoning as easy or difficult, secret or public, by favor or justice. Consider how these varieties correspond to deeds.
Remember that the Reckoning applies to both believers and disbelievers, humans and jinn.
3
Identify the easiest form and the exceptions
Note the description of the easiest reckoning: God alone accounting privately. Also note the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without any reckoning.
This shows God's mercy and the special status of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.
4
Reflect on the community's precedence
The passage ends by noting that this ummah, though last, precedes in the Hereafter. Think about how this relates to the concept of al-Hisab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
-٥ - ويلزم الإيمان بالحساب * والحشر والعقاب والثواب
ولما كانت مباحث هذا الفنّ ثلاثة : إلهيّاتٌ ونُبوّاتٌ وسَمْعيّات، وقد تَقَدَّمَ الكلام على بيان الأوَّلين شَرَعَ في الثالث وهو السمعيات فقال:
(وبلزم) أي: يجب على المكلفين (الإيمان) أي: التصديقُ (بالحساب) وهو لغة: العدُّ، واصطلاحًا: توقيفُ الله عباده في المحشر على أعمالهم، فعلا أو قولا أو اعتقادًا، تفصيلا بأن يكلِّمهم الله تعالى بكلام قديم، ليس بحرف ولا صوت.
بأن يُزيل عنهم الحجاب حتى يسمعوه، أو بصوت يخلقه الله تعالى يدلُّ عليه، وقد يكون من الملائكة فقط، وقد يكون منه تعالى ومن الملائكة جميعًا.
وكيفيته مختلفة، فمنه اليسير ومنه العسير، والسر والجهر، والفضل والعدل، على حسب الأعمال، فيغفر لمن يشاء ويعذب من يشاء.
ويكون للمؤمنين والكافرين، إنسًا وجنّا، بعد أخذهم الكتب لقوله تعالى: فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ * فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا * وَيَنْقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُورًا.
وأيسر الحساب محاسبة الله فقط، حتى لا يعلم بذلك إنس ولا جن ولا ملك، يقول له تعالى: هذه سيئاتك قد غفرتها لك، وهذه حسناتك قد ضاعفتها لك. ولا يكون للمعصومين، ويستثنى من يحاسب سبعون ألفا، أفضلهم أبو بكر الصديق رضي الله، فإنهم يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب كما ورد بذلك الحديث.
وهذه الأمة وإن كانت آخر الأمم إلا أنها تقدم في الآخرة في الحساب وغيره.
The third division: the sam‘iyyāt (matters known through revelation).
-5 - And belief in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, and the Reward is necessary.
Since the topics of this art are three: ilāhiyyāt (divine matters), nubūwāt (prophecies), and sam‘iyyāt, and the discussion on the first two has preceded, he began the third, which is the sam‘iyyāt, and said:
(And it is necessary) i.e., it is obligatory upon the legally responsible (belief) i.e., affirmation (in the Reckoning), which linguistically is counting, and terminologically is God’s calling His servants to account in the Gathering-place for their deeds, whether act, word, or belief, in detail — that God Most High speaks to them with eternal speech, not composed of letter or sound.
That He removes the veil from them so that they hear it, or with a sound that God Most High creates indicating it; and it may be from the angels only, and it may be from Him Most High and from the angels all together.
Its modality is varied: among it is easy and difficult, secret and public, favor and justice, according to deeds. He forgives whom He wills and punishes whom He wills.
It is for the believers and the disbelievers, humans and jinn, after they receive their books, according to His statement: "Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be reckoned with an easy reckoning and will return to his people happy." [Quran 84:7-9]
The easiest reckoning is God’s accounting alone, so that no human, jinn, or angel knows of it. He says to him: These are your sins — I have forgiven them for you, and these are your good deeds — I have multiplied them for you. It does not occur for the infallible, and there are exempted from being brought to account seventy thousand, the best of whom is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him, for they enter Paradise without reckoning as the hadith has reported.
And this community, though it is the last of communities, nevertheless precedes in the Hereafter in the reckoning and other matters.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage defines the third division of theological topics — the sam‘iyyāt (matters known only through revelation) — and focuses on the necessity of belief in the Reckoning (al-ḥisāb). The author begins by stating that the topics of this discipline are three: divine matters, prophecies, and sam‘iyyāt. Having already covered the first two, he now addresses the third. He quotes the poetic line: 'Belief in the Reckoning, the Gathering, the Punishment, and the Reward is necessary,' then provides commentary.

He explains that 'it is necessary' means it is obligatory for the legally responsible (mukallafīn). 'Belief' means affirmation (taṣdīq). The Reckoning (al-ḥisāb) is defined linguistically as counting, and terminologically as God stopping His servants in the Gathering-place (al-maḥshar) to call them to account for their deeds — whether acts, words, or beliefs — in detail. This detailed accounting occurs by God speaking to them with eternal speech (kalām qadīm) that is not composed of letters or sound, thereby affirming the Ash‘arī doctrine that God’s speech is not created and not composed of letters and sounds. The hearing of this speech may occur either by God removing the veil so they hear it directly, or by a created sound that God brings into existence to indicate the speech. The speaker may be angels only, or God together with angels.

The author then describes the varied nature of the reckoning: it can be easy or difficult, secret or public, based on favor or justice, according to each person’s deeds. God forgives whom He wills and punishes whom He wills. The reckoning applies to both believers and disbelievers, humans and jinn, after they receive their books (scriptures of deeds). He cites the Qur’anic verse (84:7-9) about the one who receives his book in his right hand and is given an easy reckoning.

The easiest form of reckoning is when God alone accounts with the person, without any human, jinn, or angel knowing. God says: 'These are your sins — I have forgiven them; these are your good deeds — I have multiplied them.' This reckoning does not apply to the infallible (ma‘ṣūmīn, i.e., prophets). Furthermore, seventy thousand people are exempted from being brought to account altogether, the best of whom is Abu Bakr al-Ṣiddīq, and they enter Paradise without any reckoning, as reported in a ḥadīth. Finally, the author notes that this community (the Muslim umma), despite being the last, will precede others in the reckoning and other matters on the Day of Judgment.

Key Terms
الحساب
السمعيات
الإيمان
الكلام القديم
المحشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's speech during the Reckoning consists of letters and sounds.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God's speech is eternal (kalām qadīm) and not composed of letters or sound; any sound heard is a created sound indicating the speech.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the terminological meaning of 'al-ḥisāb' (the Reckoning)?
A) Counting numbers
B) God's calling His servants to account for their deeds in the Gathering-place
C) The punishment of disbelievers
D) The giving of books

Key Takeaway
Belief in al-Hisab is obligatory; it is God's detailed accountability of all deeds, with varied modalities, and includes exceptions of mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Reckoning includes every act, word, and belief—even those you hide from others. Are you living today as if every secret of your heart will be exposed before God? What one hidden sin are you most afraid will be brought to light, and what will you do about it now?
?
The easiest reckoning is when God alone knows and forgives all sins and multiplies good deeds, with no one else aware. Do you truly believe that God’s mercy can cover even your worst failures? If so, why do you still despair or rely on people’s approval instead of His forgiveness?
?
Seventy thousand will enter Paradise without any reckoning—purely by mercy. Do you rely more on your own deeds or on God’s mercy for your salvation? What would change in your daily life if you fully trusted that mercy today?

The Varied Accounting of the Day of Judgment
Imam Dardeer describes the varying types of accounting and the exception of 70,000.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different forms of divine accounting on the Day of Judgment, including who undergoes it, the easiest type, and the exceptional group that enters Paradise without account.

Core Idea
The accounting is just and varied—easy or hard, secret or public—according to deeds.

Imam Dardeer explains that the accounting on the Day of Judgment is not uniform; it differs based on a person's deeds. Some will face an easy account, others a difficult one; some accounts are public, others private. Moreover, the passage highlights the special status of 70,000 believers, led by Abu Bakr, who will enter Paradise without any accounting at all.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to get a sense of the overall description.
Notice the pairs of opposites: easy/difficult, secret/public, bounty/justice.
2
Identify the types of accounting
The passage lists three pairs of opposite types. Find each pair and understand what they mean in context.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The author quotes Surah al-Inshiqaq (84:7-9) to support the easy account. Read the verse and see how it connects.
4
Learn about the easiest account
The easiest form is when Allah alone judges a person, unknown to others. Notice the dialogue between Allah and the person.
This is a secret account.
5
Recognize the exception and the Ummah's status
Seventy thousand, led by Abu Bakr, enter Paradise without any account. Also note that this Ummah is first in the Hereafter despite being last in time.

وكيفيّتُه (٢) مُختلفة، فمنه اليسيرُ ومنه العَسيرُ ، والسِّرُّ والجَهرُ ، والفضْلُ والعدل، على حسب الأعمال، فيغْفِرُ لمن يشاء ويُعذِّبُ مَنْ يشاءُ. ويكون للمؤمنين والكافرين (۳) ، إنسًا وجنّا، بعد أخذهم الكُتُبَ لقوله تعالى: فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتبهُ بيَمِينِهِ * فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَاباً يَسِيراً * وَيَنقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْله (٤) مسروراً. وأيسر الحِسابِ مُحاسبةُ اللهِ فقط، حتى لا يعْلَمَ بذلك إنس ولا جن ولا ملَكٌ، يقولُ له تعالى: هذه سيّئاتُكَ قد غفَرتُها لك، وهذه حسَناتُكَ قد ضاعفتُها لكَ. ولا يكون للمعصومين، ويُستثنى مِنْ يُحَاسَبُ سَبعون ألفا، أفضَلُهم أبو بكر الصِّدِّيقُ رَضَ الله، فإنهم يدخلون الجنةَ بغَيرِ حِساب كما ورَدَ بذلك الحديث. وهذه الأمه وإن كانتْ آخِرَ الأُمم إلا أنها تقدم في الآخرة في الحساب وغيره.
And its manner (2) varies: among it is easy and difficult, secret and public, bounty and justice, according to deeds. He forgives whom He wills and punishes whom He wills. And it is for the believers and disbelievers (3), humans and jinn, after they have taken their books, due to His saying: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged with an easy account, and he will return to his family joyful' (Surah al-Inshiqaq, verses 7-9). And the easiest of accounts is only the accounting by Allah such that no human, jinn, or angel knows of it. He says to him: 'These are your sins, I have forgiven them for you, and these are your good deeds, I have multiplied them for you.' And it is not for the infallible ones, and an exception is made of seventy thousand who will be accounted, the best of them is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, for they will enter Paradise without account as the hadith has come. And this community, although it is the last of communities, yet it will be first in the Hereafter in the account and other matters.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage describes the nature and types of the accounting (al-hisab) on the Day of Judgment. It begins by stating that the accounting varies in several ways: it can be easy or difficult, secret or public, and characterized by bounty or justice, all according to a person's deeds. Then it clarifies that the accounting applies to both believers and disbelievers, both humans and jinn, after they receive their books of deeds. It quotes the Quranic verse from Surah al-Inshiqaq (84:7-9) about the easy account for those who receive their book in their right hand. The passage then explains that the easiest form of accounting is when Allah alone judges a person, such that no other being knows of it. Allah says to that person: 'These are your sins, I have forgiven them; these are your good deeds, I have multiplied them.' The passage notes that this type of accounting is not for the infallible (ma'sumun, i.e., prophets and angels). It then mentions an exception: seventy thousand people, the best of whom is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, will enter Paradise without any accounting at all, as reported in a hadith. Finally, it states that although this community (the Muslim ummah) is the last in time, it will be first in the Hereafter in terms of accounting and other matters.

?

?
Since the accounting varies according to deeds, what kind of account do your current actions deserve—easy or difficult? If you were to be judged right now, would you want it to be public or secret, and why does that reveal about your true state with Allah?

The Reality of al-Hashr and the Three Modes
Definition of al-Hashr and three modes of travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Hashr and the three different ways people will be gathered at the standing-place.

Core Idea
The gathering is real and people come in varied states: riding, walking, or crawling on their faces.

This lesson introduces the third section of matters heard from revelation (sam'iyyat). Imam Dardeer explains the necessity of believing in al-Hashr, the gathering of bodies after resurrection, and describes the diverse modes in which people will be brought to the standing-place.

Guided Path

Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the definition of al-Hashr and the three modes mentioned.
2

The passage presents these as literal physical states.
3

Consider why belief in al-Hashr is obligatory. How does this connect to the broader Islamic creed?

القسم الثالث: السمعيات
بالحشر بعد بعيْهِم مِنْ قُبُورِهم المُسمّى بالنَّشْرِ كما سيأتي.
(و) يجب الإيمان بـ (الحشر) أني حشر الأجسادِ، وهو: سوقها إلى المَوقِفِ، المسمّى ومراتب الناس في الحشر :متفاوتة فمنهم الراكب، ومنهم الماشي على رجليه ومنهم مَنْ يمشي على وَجْهه.
ويكون [؟] في مراتب [؟] مُختلفة على حسَبِ الأعْمالِ: فمنهم مَنْ هو على صورةِ القِرَدَةِ، وهم الزناة. ومنهم على صورة الخنازير، وهم آكلو السُّحْتِ والمَكْس (۳). ومنهم الأعمى، وهو الجائر في الحكم. ومنهم الأصَمُّ والأبكم، وهو الذي يُعجَبُ بِفِعِلِهِ. ومنهم مَنْ يمضُعُ لِسانَه مُدْلعًا على صدره يسيل القيحُ مِنْ فمه، وهم الوعاظ الذين تُخالِفُ أفعالهم أقوالهم. ومنهم المقطوع الأيدي والأرجل، وهم الذين يؤذون الجيران. ومنهم مَنْ يُصلَّبُ على جذوع مِنَ النارِ، وهم السُّعاةُ بالنَّاسِ إلى السُّلْطانِ. ومنهم مَنْ هوَ أَشَدُّ نثنا مِنَ الجيفِ، وهم الذين يُقبلون على الشهَواتِ واللذاتِ ويمنعون حقَّ الله من أموالهم. ومنهم مَنْ يُلبَسُ جُبَّةٌ سابغةً مِنْ قطران لاصقة بجلده، وهم أهلُ الكِبر والعُجب والخيلاء
الإيمان بالحشر
The third section: The Sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation). Concerning al-Hashr after they are raised from their graves, which is called al-Nashr (the spreading), as will come. And it is obligatory to believe in al-Hashr, i.e., the gathering of bodies, which is: driving them to the standing-place, called al-Mawqif. And the ranks of people in the gathering are varied: among them are riders, among them are walkers on their feet, and among them are those who walk on their faces. And they will be [؟] in varying ranks [؟] according to their deeds: among them are those who are in the form of monkeys, and they are the adulterers. And among them are those in the form of pigs, and they are the consumers of illicit earnings and the tax (al-maks) (3). And among them is the blind, and he is the unjust judge. And among them is the deaf and dumb, and he is the one who is pleased with his own action. And among them are those who chew their tongues, protruding on their chests, pus flowing from their mouths, and they are the preachers whose deeds contradict their words. And among them are those with cut-off hands and feet, and they are those who harm their neighbors. And among them are those who are crucified on trunks of fire, and they are those who slander people to the ruler. And among them are those who are more foul-smelling than carrion, and they are those who indulge in desires and pleasures and withhold Allah's right from their wealth. And among them are those who wear a flowing cloak of tar sticking to their skin, and they are the people of pride, vanity, and arrogance. Belief in al-Hashr.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage belongs to the third section of the book on sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation). It addresses the belief in al-Hashr, which is the gathering of bodies after resurrection. The passage defines al-Hashr as the driving of bodies to the standing-place (al-mawqif) after they have been raised from their graves (al-nashr). It then states that people's ranks in the gathering are varied: some ride, some walk on their feet, and some walk on their faces. The passage then lists several categories of people who will appear in specific forms reflecting their sins. These include: adulterers in the form of monkeys; those who consume illicit earnings and taxes in the form of pigs; unjust judges as blind; those pleased with their own actions as deaf and dumb; preachers whose deeds contradict their words with their tongues protruding and pus flowing; those who harm neighbors with cut-off hands and feet; slanderers to rulers crucified on trunks of fire; those who indulge in desires and withhold Allah's right as foul-smelling; and the proud wearing a cloak of tar. The passage concludes with the phrase 'Belief in al-Hashr', emphasizing the necessity of this belief.

Enumeration of nine forms of sinners at the gathering

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Sinners will be resurrected in forms that reflect their sins, from monkeys and pigs to a cloak of tar.

Having established the reality of the gathering, Imam Dardeer now details the particular forms that different sinful groups will take. This vivid description shows the correspondence between one's actions and one's appearance at the resurrection.

For example, adulterers become monkeys – perhaps symbolizing base desires.
3
Appreciate the diversity

The Gathering (al-Hashr) and Its States
Defines al-hashr and enumerates different states of people in the gathering

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-hashr (the gathering) and the various states of people in the gathering based on their deeds.

Core Idea
The gathering is bodily, and people appear according to their actions.

In this passage, Imam al-Dardir begins the section on sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation) by establishing the obligatory belief in al-hashr, the gathering of bodies after resurrection. He then describes the varying ranks of people in the gathering, highlighting that their appearances reflect their deeds. This vivid imagery serves as a warning and a reminder of the consequences of our actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-hashr
Read the Arabic passage carefully and understand the meaning of al-hashr: the gathering of bodies to the standing-place after resurrection.
Note that it is part of the sam'iyyat (revelational matters).
2
Identify the general ranks
Notice that the author mentions three general ranks: riders, walkers, and those who walk on their faces.
This shows that people have varying statuses in the gathering.
3
Study the nine specific categories
The author enumerates nine types of people and their forms according to their sins. For each, identify the sin and the corresponding form.
These include fornicators (monkeys), bribe-takers (pigs), unjust judges (blind), proud preachers (tongue-chewers), etc.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this passage warns against specific sins and emphasizes that deeds manifest on the Day of Judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
(و) يجب الإيمان بـ (الحشر) يعني حشر الأجساد، وهو: سوقها إلى الموقف، المسمى بالنشر بعد بعثهم من قبورهم كما سيأتي. ومراتب الناس في الحشر متفاوتة: فمنهم الراكب، ومنهم الماشي على رجليه، ومنهم من يمشي على وجهه. ويكون في صور مختلفة على حسب الأعمال: فمنهم من هو على صورة القردة، وهم الزناة. ومنهم على صورة الخنازير، وهم آكلو السحت والمكس. ومنهم الأعمى، وهو الجائر في الحكم. ومنهم الأصم والأبكم، وهو الذي يعجب بفعله. ومنهم من يمضغ لسانه مدلعا على صدره يسيل القيح من فمه، وهم الوعاظ الذين تخالف أفعالهم أقوالهم. ومنهم المقطوع الأيدي والأرجل، وهم الذين يؤذون الجيران. ومنهم من يصلب على جذوع من النار، وهم السعاة بالناس إلى السلطان. ومنهم من هو أشد نتنًا من الجيف، وهم الذين يقبلون على الشهوات واللذات ويمنعون حق الله من أموالهم. ومنهم من يلبس جبة سابغة من قطران لاصقة بجلده، وهم أهل الكبر والعجب والخيلاء.
The third section: the sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation). And it is obligatory to believe in al-hashr (the gathering), meaning the gathering of bodies, which is: driving them to the standing-place (al-mawqif), called al-nashr (the spreading) after their resurrection from their graves as will come. And the ranks of people in the gathering are varying: among them are riders, among them are walkers on their feet, among them are those who walk on their faces. And they are in different forms according to deeds: among them are those in the form of monkeys, and they are the fornicators. Among them are those in the form of pigs, and they are the consumers of bribery and illegal tax (al-maks). Among them are the blind, and that is the unjust in judgment. Among them are the deaf and mute, and that is the one who is amazed at his own action. Among them are those who chew their tongues, sticking out on their chests, pus flowing from their mouths, and they are the preachers whose actions contradict their words. Among them are those with cut-off hands and feet, and they are those who harm their neighbors. Among them are those crucified on trunks of fire, and they are those who slander people to the ruler. Among them are those whose stench is worse than that of carrion, and they are those who pursue lusts and pleasures and withhold the right of Allah from their wealth. Among them are those who wear a capacious cloak of tar stuck to their skin, and they are the people of pride, self-admiration, and arrogance.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines al-hashr (the gathering) as part of the sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation) and then describes various states of people in that gathering. The author first explains that belief in al-hashr is obligatory, meaning the gathering of bodies to the standing-place (al-mawqif) after resurrection. He then states that the ranks of people in the gathering are varying: some ride, some walk, and some crawl on their faces. This difference is a sign of their deeds. He then enumerates nine categories of people and their corresponding forms based on their sins: fornicators appear as monkeys, consumers of bribery and illegal taxes as pigs, unjust judges as blind, those amazed at themselves as deaf and mute, hypocritical preachers with contradictory actions as chewing their tongues, those who harm neighbors as amputated, slanderers as crucified on fire, those who indulge in pleasures and withhold charity as foul-smelling, and the proud and arrogant as wearing garments of tar. Each description is a vivid warning against specific sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The preachers whose actions contradict their words are depicted with pus flowing from their mouths. If your words and actions were weighed right now, would they be consistent? What specific step can you take this week to align your practice with what you say you believe?
?
The people of pride, self-admiration, and arrogance wear a cloak of tar that clings to their skin. When you look in the mirror, do you see any trace of 'ujb (self-amazement) or kibr (pride) in your heart? Ask Allah to purify you from these traits and start a daily habit of thanking Him for every good you do.

Types and Places of Punishment
Defines punishment and lists its places and types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the occasions and types of punishment as described in the text.

Core Idea
Punishment varies according to deeds and occurs in the grave and beyond.

The passage begins by affirming that punishment is for sins and disbelief, occurring in the grave, the gathering, and beyond. It then gives examples of the varied forms this punishment can take, depending on the deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic and translation for the definition of punishment and its locations.
Notice that punishment is for both sins and disbelief.
2
Identify the examples
Find the examples of punishment types: snakes, scorpions, beating, and others.
These are not exhaustive but illustrative.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider that punishment varies according to deeds, which is a key Islamic doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعقاب على الذنوب والكفر، في القبر وفي المحشر وبعده بأنواع مختلفة على حسب الأعمال. فمنهم من يعاقب بالحيات أو بالعقارب، ومنهم من يعاقب بالضرب، ومنهم من يعاقب بغير ذلك. ثم مال الكفار إلى النار ويخلدون فيها. وأما أهل المعاصي فقد يغفر لهم فلا يدخلون النار، وبعضهم يدخلها ولكن لا يخلد فيها، بل لا بد من خروجه منها بشفاعة نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما بعد البعث فمحله الروح والجسد قطعًا، وكذا قبله في البرزخ على المشهور بأن يعيد الله الروح إليه، أو إلى جزء منه إن قلنا إن المعذب بعض الجسد، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرقت أجزاؤه أو أكلته السباع أو الحيتان، فإن القادر لا يعجزه شيء، وقيل: إنه يتعلق بالأرواح فقط.
And punishment is for sins and disbelief, in the grave, in the gathering, and after it, in various types according to deeds. Among them are those punished with snakes or scorpions, among them are those punished with beating, and among them are those punished with other than that. Then the destiny of the disbelievers is to the Fire and they will abide therein eternally. As for the people of disobedience, they may be forgiven and not enter the Fire, and some of them enter it but do not abide eternally, rather they must come out of it by the intercession of our Prophet (peace be upon him) or other than him, as will come if Allah wills. And as for after the resurrection, its locus is the soul and the body definitively, and likewise before it in the barzakh according to the well-known view, by Allah returning the soul to it, or to a part of it if we say that the punished is part of the body. And that is not prevented by the fact that the deceased's parts have scattered or that beasts or fish have eaten him, for the Powerful is not incapacitated by anything. And it was said that it attaches only to souls.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage explains the doctrine of punishment (al-iqab) after death. The author states that punishment applies for sins and disbelief and occurs in the grave, the gathering, and after it, with types varying according to deeds. He gives examples: some are punished with snakes, scorpions, or beating. Then he distinguishes between disbelievers, who will dwell in Hell forever, and disobedient believers, who may be forgiven or punished temporarily but eventually exit through intercession. He then addresses the locus of punishment after resurrection, affirming that it is both soul and body, and similarly in the barzakh (the intermediate state) according to the well-known view. The soul is returned to the body (or a part of it) for punishment, and this is not hindered by the body's disintegration. The author notes an alternative view that punishment attaches only to souls. The emphasis is on Allah's power to reanimate and punish even a completely disintegrated body.

Correction: This passage shows punishment occurs in the grave, the gathering, and after, not only in Hell.

Key Takeaway
Punishment applies for sin and disbelief in multiple stages and varies by deed.

?

Fate of Disbelievers and Sinful Believers
Contrasts eternal punishment for disbelievers and temporary for believers with intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different eternal outcomes for disbelievers and sinful believers and the role of intercession.

Core Idea
Disbelievers face eternal hell, while sinful believers may be forgiven or temporarily punished then saved by intercession.

After describing types of punishment, the text turns to the final destinies. It clearly distinguishes between the eternal punishment of disbelievers and the temporary punishment of believers who commit sins, highlighting the possibility of forgiveness and the necessity of intercession for eventual salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on destinies
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the fate of disbelievers and believers.
2
Contrast the two groups
Note that disbelievers remain in Hell forever, while believers who sin may be forgiven or enter temporarily.
The key term is 'خلود' (eternity) for disbelievers.
3
Understand intercession
Recognize that sinful believers are eventually removed from Hell through intercession (shafa‘ah) of the Prophet or others.
This shows Allah's mercy.

Locus of Punishment: Body and Soul
Affirms punishment on body and soul after resurrection and in barzakh, with divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the locus of punishment after resurrection and in the barzakh, and why it is possible even on a disintegrated body.

Core Idea
Punishment after death affects both soul and body, even if the body has disintegrated, because Allah is all-powerful.

The final part of the passage addresses a crucial question: where does punishment take place? The author affirms that after resurrection, the locus is definitely both soul and body, and similarly in the barzakh, by Allah returning the soul to the body. This is possible even if the body has been scattered or eaten, because nothing incapacitates Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on locus
Read the Arabic and translation about the locus of punishment after resurrection and in the barzakh.
2
Understand the well-known view
Note that the well-known view is that punishment is on both soul and body, with the soul returned to the body.
The alternative view is that it attaches only to souls.
3
Appreciate divine power
Consider that even a disintegrated body is not an obstacle for Allah, who is all-powerful.
This refutes any materialistic objection.

Reward (al-Thawab) and Its Varieties
Defines reward and lists its varieties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of reward in Islamic theology, its varieties in the Hereafter and barzakh, and that it is a bestowal of divine favor.

Core Idea
Reward is divine favor, not merely earned merit.

This short but dense passage from Imam Dardir's commentary on al-Kharidah establishes the foundational understanding of reward (al-thawab). It clarifies that reward is not limited to Paradise but includes various forms of bliss in the barzakh and beyond. Moreover, it emphasizes that all reward ultimately flows from Allah's grace (al-ifdal).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the concise definition of reward.
Notice the concise structure: definition, enumeration, and theological conclusion.
2
Identify the varieties of reward
List the different types and locations of reward mentioned: Paradise, other bliss, barzakh, and after it. Note that they vary according to deeds.
This shows reward is not monolithic.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
The passage ends by stating that reward is a divine favor (al-ifdal). Consider how this relates to the concept of God's grace and human merit.
This is a key Ash'ari principle: reward is not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثواب أي: الجزاء على الأعمال بالجنة في الآخرة، وغيرها من أنواع النعيم، وكذا في البرزخ وبعده وأنواعه مختلفة أيضًا على حسب الأعمال، والإفضال من الواحد المتعال.
And reward (al-thawab): that is, the recompense for deeds with Paradise in the Hereafter, and other types of bliss, and likewise in the barzakh and after it, and its varieties are diverse as well according to deeds, and the bestowal of favor is from the One, the Most High.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage defines reward (al-thawab) as the recompense for good deeds, primarily with Paradise in the Hereafter and other types of bliss. The author clarifies that reward occurs in the barzakh (the intermediate state) and after it, and its varieties are diverse according to the deeds performed. Finally, he emphasizes that this reward is a bestowal of favor (al-ifdal) from Allah, the One and Most High, indicating that it is not something earned by mere merit but is an act of divine grace.

Key Terms
الثواب
النعيم
البرزخ
الإفضال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that God is obliged to reward good deeds as a matter of justice, and that reward is limited to Paradise.
Correction: This passage teaches that reward is not only Paradise but also other bliss in barzakh and beyond, and that it is a divine favor (ifdal), not an obligation.

Checkpoint
What is the primary form of reward in the Hereafter according to this passage?
A) Wealth
B) Paradise
C) Power
D) Knowledge

Key Takeaway
Reward is a diverse and gracious gift from Allah, encompassing Paradise and other bliss in this life's afterlife stages, given as divine favor not mere compensation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the rewards you hope for from Allah, do you treat them as a debt He owes you for your good deeds, or as His pure generosity? Examine your heart: do you feel entitled to Paradise based on your actions?
?
The passage teaches that reward includes not only Paradise but 'other types of bliss' and also in the barzakh. Have you ever sincerely longed for Allah's favor in the moments between death and judgment? What does that tell you about your current connection to the afterlife?
?
If reward is entirely a bestowal of favor, not a wage you earn, does that change how you perform your good deeds? Do you act with gratitude or with a sense of transaction? What would it look like to do today's deeds solely as a response to His favor?
