Punishment After Death: Types and Eternal Fate
Dardeer enumerates punishments and contrasts fates of disbelievers and sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different types of punishment in the grave and afterlife, and the eternal fate of disbelievers versus the temporary punishment of sinful believers.

Core Idea
Punishment after death is varied and eternal for disbelievers, but sinning believers may be forgiven or temporarily punished.

In this passage, Dardeer explains the nature of punishment after death, emphasizing that it occurs in multiple stages and forms according to one's deeds. He clarifies that while disbelievers suffer eternal punishment, believers who commit sins may either be forgiven or experience temporary punishment before being saved through intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on punishment
Read the Arabic passage about punishment and its translation carefully. Notice how Dardeer categorizes punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers.
2
Identify the types of punishment
List the different types of punishment mentioned: snakes, scorpions, beating, etc. Understand that they vary according to deeds.
This shows the justice of Allah in matching punishment to sin.
3
Contrast the fates
Compare the eternal punishment of disbelievers with the possibility of forgiveness or temporary punishment for sinful believers. Note the role of intercession.
4
Apply the concept to intercession
Reflect on how intercession (shafa'ah) allows sinful believers to eventually leave Hell, highlighting Allah's mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعقاب على الذنوب والكفر، في القبر وفي المحشر وبعده بأنواع مختلفة على حسب الأعمال فمنهم من يعاقب بالحيات أو بالعقارب، ومنهم من يعاقب بالضرب، ومنهم من يعاقب بغير ذلك، ثم مال الكفار إلى النار ويخلدون فيها، وأما أهل الإيمان من أهل المعاصي فقد يغفر لهم فلا يدخلون النار، وبعضهم يدخلها ولكن لا يخلد فيها، بل لا بد من خروجهم منها بشفاعة نبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى. والثواب أي: الجزاء على الأعمال بالجنة في الآخرة، وغيرها من أنواع النعيم، وكذا في البرزخ وبعده، وأنواعه مختلفة أيضًا على حسب الأعمال، والإفضال من الواحد المتعال. وأما بعد البعث فمحله الروح والجسد قطعًا، وكذا قبله في البرزخ على المشهور بأن يعيد الله الروح إليه، أو إلى جزء منه إن قلنا إن المعذب بعض الجسد، ولا يمنع من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرقت أجزاؤه أو أكلته السباع أو الحيتان، فإن القادر لا يعجزه شيء، وقيل: إنه يتعلق بالأرواح فقط. تنبيه: تنعيم الله للمؤمنين في القبر الإيمان به واجب كشأن عذابه لما ورد في ذلك من النصوص البالغ مجموعها حد التواتر وإن كانت تفاصيلها آحاداً، ولا يختص النعيم بمؤمني هذه الأمة، كما لا يختص بالمكلفين، وكذا لا يختص بالمقبور.
And punishment is for sins and disbelief, in the grave and in the gathering and after it, in various types according to deeds. Among them are those who are punished with snakes or scorpions, and among them are those who are punished with beating, and among them are those who are punished with other than that. Then the destination of the disbelievers is the Fire and they will abide therein forever. As for the people of faith from among the people of sin, they may be forgiven so they do not enter the Fire, and some of them enter it but do not abide therein forever; rather, they must come out of it by the intercession of our Prophet ﷺ or others, as will come later if Allah wills. And reward: that is, the recompense for deeds with Paradise in the Hereafter, and other kinds of bliss, and likewise in the Barzakh and after it, and its types are also varied according to deeds, and the bestowal of favor is from the One, the Most High. And as for after the resurrection, its locus is the spirit and the body definitively, and likewise before it in the Barzakh according to the well-known view: that Allah returns the spirit to it, or to a part of it if we say that the punished one is part of the body. And nothing prevents that from the fact that the dead person's parts have scattered or that beasts or fish have eaten him, for the Powerful One is not incapacitated by anything. And it was said: it attaches to spirits only. A note: Belief in Allah’s granting bliss to the believers in the grave is obligatory, like His punishment, due to the texts that have reached the level of tawatur in their total, even if their details are ahad; and bliss is not specific to the believers of this nation, nor is it specific to the morally responsible, and likewise it is not specific to the buried.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage discusses the Islamic doctrines of punishment (ʿiqāb) and reward (thawāb) after death, in the grave (qabr), and in the Hereafter. The author begins by stating that punishment is for sins and disbelief, and occurs in the grave, the gathering, and after, in various forms corresponding to deeds. Examples include snakes, scorpions, beating, etc. Disbelievers end up in Hell eternally. For sinful believers, some are forgiven and do not enter Hell; others enter temporarily but are eventually removed by intercession of the Prophet or others. Then he defines reward as recompense with Paradise and other bliss, also in the Barzakh (intermediate state) and afterlife, with types varying by deeds. He then addresses the locus of punishment and reward: definitively both spirit and body after resurrection, and before resurrection in the Barzakh according to the well-known view, where Allah returns the spirit to the body or part of it. This is possible even if the body has disintegrated or been eaten, because Allah is all-powerful. The alternative view holds that it attaches only to spirits. The passage concludes with a note affirming that belief in the bliss of the grave is obligatory, based on numerous texts.

Key Terms
العقاب
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sinners, including believers, will be punished eternally.
Correction: The passage clarifies that sinful believers may be forgiven or punished temporarily, and then saved by intercession.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to believers who commit major sins?
A) They are eternally punished in Hell.
B) They may be forgiven or temporarily punished but eventually saved.
C) They are not punished at all.
D) They are punished only in the grave.

Key Takeaway
Punishment after death is just and varied, but believers have hope through forgiveness and intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever committed a sin and assumed it was 'small' and would be forgiven without consequence? How does knowing that punishment is varied and proportional to deeds change your view of your own actions? What one step will you take today to treat every sin as serious?
?
Do you rely on the intercession of the Prophet ﷺ while continuing in sin? What does this passage teach about the need for faith and repentance before that intercession applies? When will you sincerely repent for a sin you have been neglecting?
?
When you consider your own sins, do you despair of mercy or take it for granted? How does the distinction between believers and disbelievers in this passage affect your hope? What will you do this week to act on that hope and turn back to Allah?

Reward and Its Locus: Body and Soul
Dardeer defines reward and explains its locus in body and soul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of reward in the afterlife and Barzakh, and the debate about whether it involves the body, soul, or both.

Core Idea
Reward in Paradise and Barzakh is given to both body and soul, though some hold it is only for souls.

Dardeer now turns to reward (thawab), defining it as recompense with Paradise and other bliss in both Barzakh and the Hereafter. He then addresses the locus of reward and punishment, presenting the well-known view that Allah reunites the soul with the body (or a part) even after disintegration, affirming divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the reward passage
Read the Arabic passage about reward and its translation. Pay attention to how Dardeer defines reward and discusses its locus.
2
Understand the definition of reward
Notice that reward includes Paradise, other bliss, and is given both in Barzakh and after resurrection. Its types vary by deeds.
3
Analyze the locus discussion
Dardeer states that after resurrection, reward involves both spirit and body definitively. Before resurrection (in Barzakh), the majority view is that Allah returns the spirit to the body or part of it. He argues that this is possible even if the body is destroyed.
This emphasizes Allah's power.
4
Contrast the alternative view
Note that some say reward attaches only to spirits. This shows a difference of opinion.

?

?

Does it scare you or comfort you that your very bones and flesh will taste Allah's generosity or justice? What does that reveal about your heart's love for obedience or its attachment to sin?

Obligatory Belief in Grave Bliss
Dardeer asserts the necessity of believing in grave bliss and its general application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the bliss and punishment of the grave is obligatory, supported by numerous textual evidences, and that it applies generally.

Core Idea
Belief in grave bliss is obligatory and attested by abundant prophetic traditions.

This concluding note from Dardeer emphasizes the obligation of affirming the bliss of the grave for believers. He bases this on the many texts that collectively reach tawatur (mass transmission), even if individual details are from ahad reports. He also clarifies that this bliss is not limited to this nation or to the buried.

Guided Path
1
Read the note on grave bliss
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the emphasis on obligation and the basis in textual evidence.
2
Understand tawatur vs. ahad
Dardeer says the overall total of texts reaches tawatur, though details are ahad. This means the general principle is certain, while specifics may be probable.
3
Grasp the universality
Note that bliss is not specific to this nation, nor to the morally responsible, nor to the buried. It applies broadly to believers.

Source Text

Al-Nashr: The Bodily Resurrection
Dardeer defines al-Nashr as bodily resurrection with gathered parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of al-Nashr as the bodily resurrection after gathering the original parts, including the unique role of the coccyx bone.

Core Idea
Al-Nashr is Allah reassembling and reviving the dead, body and soul.

This lesson introduces one of the core eschatological beliefs known through revelation: the resurrection of the dead. Imam Dardeer explains what al-Nashr means, how it happens, and the one part of the body that never perishes. The passage also hints at a debated point about whether the parts cease to exist entirely or only disperse.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of al-Nashr
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that al-Nashr is equated with 'al-baʿth' (resurrection).
The passage includes two opinions about the state of the body parts before gathering.
2
Identify the key elements
Look for: the role of Allah, the gathering of original parts, the exception of the coccyx bone (ʿajb adh-dhanab), and the two opinions on how the parts are gathered.
The coccyx bone is said to never cease to exist, even if all other parts perish.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does the text emphasize bodily resurrection? Why preserve the coccyx bone? This connects to the Islamic view that resurrection is both physical and spiritual.
This counters any notion of purely spiritual resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
٥٥ - والنشر والصّراط والميزان * والحوض والنيران والجنان
(والنشر) وهو البعث، والمراد به إحياء الله الموتى من قبورهم بعد جمع أجزائهم الأصلية (١) ، بأن يجمعها الله بعد تفرقها، وقيل: بعد عدمها بالكلية (٢) ما عدا عَجْبَ الذَّنَبِ (٣) فإنه لا يُعْدَمُ. وقيل: هو الإخراج من القبور بعد الإحياء برد الروح فيه.
أجزائهم الإيمان
(والصراط) وهو لغة: الطريق الواضح، وشرعًا: جسر ممدود على متن جهنم بين الوقف والجنة، لأن جهنم بينها تردها المؤمنون والكفار للمرور عليه إلى الجنة، أدق من الشعرة وأحد من السيف.
The third section: The Transmitted Matters (As-Samiyyat). 55 - And Al-Nashr and As-Sirat and Al-Mizan * and Al-Hawd and An-Niran and Al-Jinan. (An-Nashr) is the resurrection, and what is meant by it is Allah's giving life to the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts, by His assembling them after their dispersal, and it was said: after their complete non-existence except for the coccyx bone, for it does not cease to exist. And it was said: it is the bringing out from the graves after giving life by returning the spirit to it. Their parts... faith? (As-Sirat) is linguistically: the clear path, and in Islamic law: a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell between the standing and Paradise, because Hell is beneath it; the believers and disbelievers will come to it to pass over it to Paradise, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of two eschatological realities: Al-Nashr (the resurrection) and As-Sirat (the bridge). It begins by introducing the third section of the poem: 'As-Samiyyat' (matters known through revelation). Then it defines Al-Nashr as the resurrection, specifically Allah reviving the dead from their graves after gathering their original bodily parts. There are two views: either after dispersal of parts or after complete non-existence, except for the coccyx bone (ʿajb adh-dhanab) which never perishes. Another opinion defines it as removal from graves after reviving by returning the spirit. The phrase 'أجزائهم الإيمان' is unclear but may relate to the parts of the body. Then As-Sirat is defined linguistically as a clear path, and legally as a bridge stretched over Hell, between the standing place and Paradise. All people (believers and disbelievers) will approach it to cross to Paradise; it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.

Key Terms
النشر
البعث
عجب الذنب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is only spiritual and the body is not reassembled.
Correction: The text affirms bodily resurrection, where Allah gathers the original parts of the body. The body is not left in a state of permanent decay.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which part of the body never ceases to exist?
A) The heart
B) The coccyx bone
C) The brain
D) The soul

Key Takeaway
Al-Nashr is the bodily resurrection where Allah reassembles the original parts, with the unique exception of the coccyx bone which never perishes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that the very bones you have now will be gathered and revived. Does that truth shape how you treat your body, or do you live as if this earthly life is all there is? What specific habit can you change today to honor that certainty?
?
If you truly believed that your coccyx bone is indestructible and will be the seed of your resurrection, would you be more mindful of the deeds your body performs? What action can you take this week to align your physical actions with the reality of the Hereafter?
?
The resurrection is not a vague spiritual return—it is a physical, tangible event. When you read the description in this lesson, did you feel a sense of awe or fear? How can you cultivate a living awareness of that day so that it transforms your daily choices, especially in moments of sin?

Al-Sirat: The Bridge Over Hell
Dardeer defines al-Sirat as the bridge over Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Sirat as the bridge over Hell that all people must cross to reach Paradise, and its described qualities.

Core Idea
Al-Sirat is a bridge finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, stretched over Hell.

This lesson covers the second eschatological reality: al-Sirat. Imam Dardeer defines it both linguistically and legally, describing its location, purpose, and extreme narrowness. Understanding this concept helps believers appreciate the gravity of the Day of Judgment and the need for divine mercy.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the definition has two parts: linguistic and legal (sharʿī).
2

The bridge is stretched over Hell, between the standing place and Paradise. All people (believers and disbelievers) will walk on it.
The bridge is the same for everyone, but the crossing experience differs.
3
Reflect on its description
It is described as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. This highlights the difficulty of crossing safely without faith and good deeds.

(An-Nashr) is the resurrection, and what is meant by it is Allah's giving life to the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts, by His assembling them after their dispersal, and it was said: after their complete non-existence except for the coccyx bone, for it does not cease to exist. The Definition of al-Nashr (Resurrection) and the Two Opinions
Dardeer defines al-Nashr and presents two opinions on its nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Nashr as the resurrection of the dead and the two scholarly opinions regarding how Allah reassembles the body.

Core Idea
The resurrection is Allah's reassembly of the body from its original parts, with debate on whether a core remnant persists.

This passage marks the beginning of the section on eschatological matters known through revelation. Dardeer first defines al-Nashr, the resurrection, and then presents two opinions on how Allah brings the dead to life. Understanding these opinions helps clarify Sunni theology on the nature of bodily resurrection.

Guided Path

Third Section: The Sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation)
55. And al-Nashr, al-Sirat, al-Mizan, al-Hawd, al-Niran, and al-Jinan.
(Al-Nashr) is the Resurrection, and what is meant by it is Allah's giving life to the dead from their graves after gathering their original parts, by His bringing them together after their dispersion. Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage opens the third section of the poem on the Sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation). The line lists key eschatological topics: al-Nashr (resurrection), al-Sirat (bridge), al-Mizan (scale), al-Hawd (basin), al-Niran (fires), and al-Jinan (gardens). The commentary focuses first on al-Nashr. It defines it as the Resurrection, meaning Allah gives life to the dead after reassembling their original physical parts. The author then presents two opinions: the first opinion holds that Allah gathers the original parts after they have dispersed; the second opinion holds that the body is brought into existence anew from nothing, except for a small bone called ʿajb al-dhanab (coccyx) which never perishes. A third view is also given: that resurrection is the extraction of the body from the grave after the spirit has been returned. The author does not explicitly favor one view but presents them as accepted possibilities within Sunni theology.

The Nature of al-Sirat and Scholarly Disputes
Dardeer defines al-Sirat and discusses the dispute over its thinness and who crosses it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of al-Sirat and the scholarly dispute about whether it is uniformly thin, varies by deeds, and whether disbelievers cross it.

Core Idea
The Sirat is real, but its width varies by deeds.

Dardeer begins by defining al-Sirat both linguistically and in Islamic law. He then presents a key dispute: is it actually thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword, or is it wide? The preferred view is that it varies based on deeds. Finally, he mentions two opinions on whether disbelievers cross the bridge. This passage gives you a glimpse into how scholars approach matters of the unseen with evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Dardeer uses very concise language.
2
Identify the two definitions
Find where Dardeer gives the linguistic definition and the legal definition of al-Sirat. Note how the legal definition adds specifics about location and function.
The legal definition includes the bridge's placement between al-waqf and Paradise.
3
Understand the dispute about thinness
The passage reports al-Qarafi's rejection of the description 'thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword'. See the author's response: the more apparent view is that it varies by deeds.
This is an example of how scholars critique transmitted descriptions.
4
Consider the two opinions about disbelievers
The passage ends with two views on whether disbelievers cross the Sirat. Reflect on how these views affect the understanding of the afterlife.
The author does not resolve this dispute, leaving it open.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والصراط) وهو لغة: الطريق الواضح، وشرعًا: جسر ممدود على متن جهنم بين الوقف والجنة، لأن جهنم بينها ترد المؤمنون والكفار للمرور عليه إلى الجنة، أدق من الشعرة وأحد من السيف.
وأنكر القرافي تبعًا لشيخه العز كونه أدق من الشعرة وأحد من السيف، بل هو متسع لما ورد ما يدل على ذلك.
والأظهر أنه مختلف في الضيق والاتساع باختلاف الأعمال.
وقيل: إن الكفار لا يمرون عليه، بل يؤمر بهم إلى النار من أول الأمر، وقيل: بعضهم يمر وبعضهم لا.
(And al-Sirat) linguistically is the clear path, and legally: a bridge stretched across the midst of Hell between the Standing (al-waqf) and Paradise, because Hell is between them; the believers and disbelievers come to it to pass over it to Paradise, thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword.
Al-Qarafi, following his teacher al-ʿIzz, denied that it is thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword; rather it is wide due to what has come indicating that.
And the more apparent is that it varies in narrowness and width according to deeds.
And it is said: the disbelievers do not pass over it, but are ordered to the Fire from the very beginning; and it is said: some of them pass and some do not.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage defines al-Sirat (the bridge) in two ways: linguistically as a clear path, and legally (in Islamic terminology) as a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, between the standing place (al-waqf) and Paradise. It is said to be thinner than a hair and sharper than a sword. The author then reports a rejection by al-Qarafi, following his teacher al-ʿIzz ibn ʿAbd al-Salam, who denied that it is actually that thin and sharp, claiming instead that it is wide based on textual evidence. The author states that the more apparent view (al-azhar) is that the bridge varies in narrowness and width according to one's deeds. Finally, two opinions are given about disbelievers: some say they do not cross it at all but are sent directly to the Fire; others say some do cross and some do not. The passage thus presents multiple scholarly positions without definitive resolution.

States of Those Crossing al-Sirat
Dardeer enumerates states of Sirat crossing and obligation to believe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main categories of people crossing the Sirat, their subcategories based on deeds, and why belief in the Sirat is obligatory.

Core Idea
Crossing the Sirat varies by deeds; all believers are eventually saved.

This lesson explores the detailed description of al-Sirat given by Imam Dardeer. He divides those crossing it into groups: some cross instantly, some with difficulty, some fall into Hell. The passage emphasizes that the Sirat is a real, possible event reported by the Prophet, and thus belief in it is mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once slowly, then read the English translation. Notice the vivid imagery used to describe the varying speeds of crossing.
The passage uses similes like 'blink of an eye' and 'lightning'.
2
Identify the three main groups
The passage presents three overarching categories: those safe by deeds (subcategorized by speed), those scratched by hooks but eventually cross, and those who fall into Hell (subcategorized by duration). List them in order.
3
Understand the role of deeds and intercession
Notice how the speed of crossing correlates with the quickness of turning away from sins. Also note that intercession rescues sinful believers from eternal punishment.
This connects to the concept of shafa'ah.
4
Grasp the theological principle of obligation
The passage ends with a general rule: anything reported by the Truthful (the Prophet) that is possible must be believed. The Sirat falls under this category.
This reinforces the importance of sam'iyyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمارون عليه مختلفون: فمنهم سالم بعمله ناج من الوقوع في نار جهنم، وهم على أقسام: فمنهم من يجوزه كلمح البصر، ومنهم من يجوزه كالبرق الخاطف، ومنهم كالريح العاصف، ومنهم كالطير، ومنهم كالجواد السابق، ومنهم من يسعى سعيا، ومنهم من يمشي، ومنهم من يمر عليه حبوا على قدر تفاوتهم في الأعمال الصالحة والإعراض عن المعاصي، فكل من كان أسرع إعراضا عنها إذا مرت على خاطره كان أسرع مرورا.
ومنهم من تخدشه كلاليبه فيسقط ولكن يتعلق بها فيعتدل ويمر ويجاوزه بعد أعوام. ومنهم غير السالم، بل يسقط في نار جهنم، وهم متفاوتون أيضا بقدر الجرائم، ثم منهم من يخلد في النار كالكفار، ومنهم من يخرج منها بعد مدة على حسب ما شاء الله تعالى، وهم عصاة المؤمنين بشفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره من الأخيار.
وهو من الممكنات التي أخبر بها الصادق، وكل ما كان كذلك فيجب الإيمان به.
And those passing over it differ: among them are those safe by their deeds, saved from falling into the Fire of Hell; and they are of categories: among them is one who crosses it like the blink of an eye, among them is one who crosses it like a flash of lightning, among them like the stormy wind, among them like a bird, among them like a swift horse, among them one who runs, among them one who walks, among them one who crawls over it according to the extent of their difference in righteous deeds and turning away from sins. So whoever was quicker in turning away from them when they occur to his mind was quicker in crossing.
And among them are those whom its hooks scratch, so he falls, but then clings to them, so he straightens up, passes, and crosses it after years. And among them are those who are not safe, but fall into the Fire of Hell; and they also vary according to the degree of crimes. Then among them are those who remain in the Fire forever, like the disbelievers; and among them are those who come out of it after a period according to what Allah wills, and they are the disobedient believers, by the intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or other righteous ones.
And it (the Sirat) is among the possible things about which the Truthful (Muhammad) informed; and everything that is so, then it is obligatory to believe in it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage describes the various states of those who cross al-Sirat (the bridge). It first divides them into those who are safe and saved by their deeds, and then further categorizes them by speed of crossing: some cross in the blink of an eye, others like lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, running, walking, or crawling. The speed corresponds to how quickly they turn away from sins when tempted. A second category includes those who are scratched by the hooks (kalalib) of the bridge, fall, but then cling to the hooks and eventually cross after years. A third category are those who are not safe and fall into Hell, their suffering varying with their crimes. Among these, some remain forever (disbelievers), while others (disobedient believers) come out after a period by God's will, through the intercession of the Prophet or other righteous people. The passage concludes with a theological principle: the Sirat is a possible (mumkin) matter reported by the Truthful (Muhammad), so it is obligatory to believe in it. This emphasizes that belief in such reports is required, even if their details are not fully comprehensible.

الكلاليب
الشفاعة

Misconception: All people who fall into Hell remain there forever.
Correction: The passage states that sinful believers exit Hell after a period through intercession, while only disbelievers remain forever.

The Sirat is a real bridge that all people cross after death; belief in it is obligatory because it is a possible matter reported by the truthful Prophet.

The Sirat: A Debate on Its Description
Dardeer reports and refutes the objection to the Sirat being finer than hair.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly debate about the physical description of the Sirat (the bridge over Hell) and the preferred view that its narrowness varies according to deeds.

Core Idea
The Sirat's narrowness is not fixed; it varies by one's deeds.

In this lesson, we examine a specific theological debate about the Sirat, the bridge over Hell. Some scholars objected to describing it as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, arguing that it is actually wide. Imam Dardeer reports this objection and provides a resolution, showing the Sunni method of reconciling textual descriptions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: a main objection followed by a footnote elaboration.
The passage includes footnote markers (1) and (2).
2
Identify the two opposing views
Find the view of al-Qarafi and al-Izz that the Sirat is wide, and the alternative view that it is finer than hair and sharper than a sword.
3
Understand the metaphorical interpretation
The footnote explains that some scholars interpret the 'finer than hair' description as a metaphor for extreme hardship, not a literal physical state.
This interpretation reconciles with hadiths about angels and hooks.
4
Note the author's preferred view
Identify Dardeer's statement that the more apparent view is that the Sirat varies in narrowness and width according to deeds.
This is the key theological stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنكَرَ القرافي تبعًا لشَيخه العِزَّ كَونَه أدقَّ مِنَ الشَّعْرِةِ وَأَحَدَّ مِنَ السَّيْفِ ، بل هو مُتَّسِعُ لِما ورَدَ ما يدل على ذلك. والأظهَرُ أنّه مُختَلَفُ في الصّيقِ والاتساع باختِلافِ الأَعْمالِ. (۱) وأما ما جاء في بعض الروايات أنه أدق من الشعرة وأحد من السيف، فقد نازع في ذلك بعضهم مثل العز بن عبد السلام والقرافي وغيرهما، وقالوا: إن ذلك يؤول بأنه كناية عن غاية الشدة والمشقة، وحينئذ لا ينافي الأحاديث الدالة على قيام الملائكة على جنبيه، وكون الكلاليب فيه. (۲) القائل بذلك الحليمي، وهو ضعيف. نعم يمكن حمله على أثناء المرور لا على ابتدائه.
And al-Qarafi denied, following his teacher al-Izz, that it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword; rather it is wide, because what indicates that has come. And the more apparent is that it varies in narrowness and width according to the difference of deeds. (1) As for what has come in some narrations that it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, some have disputed that, such as al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam and al-Qarafi and others, and they said: That is interpreted as a metaphor for extreme severity and hardship, and then it does not contradict the hadiths indicating the standing of angels on its sides and the presence of hooks in it. (2) The one who said that is al-Halimi, and he is weak. Yes, it can be applied to the time of crossing, not to its beginning.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage presents a theological debate about the physical description of the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). The author reports that al-Qarafi, following his teacher al-Izz ibn Abd al-Salam, objected to the famous reports that the Sirat is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. They argue that the Sirat is actually wide, based on other evidence. The author then states that the more apparent view is that the Sirat varies in narrowness and width according to people's deeds. The passage then provides a footnote (which is part of the text here) that elaborates on the objection. It says that some scholars interpret the 'finer than hair' description as a metaphor for extreme difficulty, not a literal physical state, so it does not contradict hadiths that mention angels standing on its sides and hooks. The footnote also identifies al-Halimi as the one who held the literal view, but considers him weak, and suggests that the literal narrowness may apply only during the crossing itself, not at the outset. The passage thus affirms the Sunni approach of taking descriptive texts as true while leaving the exact nature to Allah, but here it specifically argues against a fixed extreme narrowness.

Key Terms
الصراط
القرافي
العز بن عبد السلام
الشعرة
السيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sirat is physically extremely narrow for everyone.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Sirat varies in narrowness and width according to deeds, and the 'finer than hair' description may be metaphorical or apply only during crossing.

Checkpoint
What is the more apparent view regarding the Sirat's width according to the passage?
A) It is always finer than a hair.
B) It varies in narrowness and width according to deeds.
C) It is wide for all.
D) It is only narrow at the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The Sirat's description is not literal; it varies by deeds, and the 'finer than hair' is either metaphorical or applies only during crossing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Sirat's narrowness varies by your deeds, what have you done today that will widen your path across it? What will you change tonight to ensure your deeds are light?
?
You just learned that some scholars interpreted the Sirat metaphorically. Are you willing to let your faith in the unseen be shaped by such tawil, or do you insist on literalism? What is the state of your heart when you imagine crossing the Sirat?
?
The passage dismisses al-Halimi's literal view as weak. What does this teach you about relying on weak opinions in matters of the afterlife? Are you building your preparation for the Hereafter on solid evidence or on weak narrations that feel more comforting?

Safe Passers of the Sirat and Their Speeds
Dardeer enumerates safe passers and their speeds of crossing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different speeds at which the saved believers cross the Sirat based on their righteousness and the principle that speed of crossing corresponds to speed of turning away from sin.

Core Idea
Crossing the Sirat is not uniform; speed reflects spiritual vigilance.

Dardeer begins by noting a difference of opinion about whether disbelievers cross the Sirat at all. He then focuses on those who do cross and are saved from falling into Hell. Their speeds vary dramatically—from a blink of an eye to crawling—based on their deeds and how quickly they repel sinful thoughts. This passage establishes a direct link between inner piety and the ease of passing the final test.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on disagreement and safe passers
Carefully read the Arabic passage up to the principle about turning away from sin. Notice the initial disagreement about disbelievers crossing, then the list of speeds for the saved.
The passage uses vivid similes like lightning and wind.
2
Identify the eight speeds mentioned
List the eight speeds or modes of crossing: blink of an eye, lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, walking, crawling. The order is from fastest to slowest.
The text says 'among them is one who runs' after the horse; we interpret 'يسعى سعيًا' as running.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that speed of crossing depends on how quickly one turns away from sinful thoughts when they occur to the mind. This connects worldly spiritual practice to the afterlife.
This is the key takeaway: deeds affect crossing speed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيلَ: إِنَّ الكُفَّارَ لا يمُرونَ عليه، بل يؤمَرُ بهم إلى النارِ مِنْ أَوّلَ الأمْرِ، وقيلَ : بعضُهم يمُرُّ وبعضُهم لا. والمارونَ عليه مُختلِفونَ: فمنهم سالم بِعَمَلِهِ نَاجِ مِنَ الوُقوعِ فِي نَارِ جَهَنَّمَ، وَهُم على أقسام: فمنهم مَنْ يجوزُه كلَمْحِةِ البَصَرِ ، ومنهم مَنْ يجوزُه كالبَرْقِ الخاطفِ، ومنهم كالريح العاصف، ومنهم كالطَّير، ومنهم كالجَوادِ السابق، ومنهم مَنْ يسعى سعيًا، ومنهم مَنْ يمشي، ومنهم مَنْ يمُرُّ عليه حبوًا على قدر تفاوتهم في الأعمال الصالحة والإعراض عن المعاصي، فكُلَّ مَنْ كانَ أسْرَعَ إعْرَاضًا عنها إذا مرت على خاطِرِه كَانَ أسرَعَ مُرورًا. ومنهم مَنْ تَخْدِشُه كلاليبه فيسقُطُ ولكِنْ يَتَعَلَّقُ بها فيعْتَدِلُ ويمُرُّ ويُجاوِزُه بَعدَ أعوام. ومنهم غَيْرُ السالم، بلْ يسقُطُ فِي نَارِ جَهَنَّمَ، وهم متفاوتون أيضًا بقدْرِ الجرائم، ثُمَّ مِنْهُم مَنْ يخلُدُ فِي النَّارِ كَالكُفَّارِ، ومنهم مَنْ يَخْرُجُ منها بعدَ مُدَّةٍ على حسَبِ ما شَاءَ الله تعالى، وهم عُصاةُ المؤمنين بشفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أَو غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الأخيارِ. وهو مِنَ المُمكناتِ التي أخبَرَ بها الصادقُ، وكُلُّ ما كان كذلك فيجب الإيمان به.
And it was said: The disbelievers do not pass over it, but are commanded to the Fire from the very beginning; and it was said: Some of them pass and some do not. And those who pass over it differ: among them is one safe by his deed, saved from falling into the Fire of Hell, and they are of categories: among them is one who crosses it like the twinkling of an eye; and among them is one who crosses it like the swift lightning; and among them like the violent wind; and among them like the bird; and among them like the swift horse; and among them is one who walks; and among them is one who crawls, according to their variance in righteous deeds and turning away from sins. For whoever is quicker in turning away from them when they cross his mind, his crossing is quicker. And among them is one whom its hooks scratch, so he falls, but then clings to them, so he balances and passes and crosses over after years. And among them is one not safe, but falls into the Fire of Hell, and they also vary according to the measure of sins. Then among them is one who is eternally in the Fire, like the disbelievers; and among them is one who comes out of it after a period according to what Allah Almighty wills, and they are the sinful believers, by the intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or other righteous ones. And it is among the possible things that the Truthful One has informed about, and everything that is such, it is obligatory to believe in it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage classifies the types of people who cross the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). It begins by noting a difference of opinion: some say disbelievers do not cross at all but are sent straight to Hell, while others say some disbelievers cross and some do not. The author then focuses on those who do cross, describing them as 'those who pass over it'. They are divided into two main groups: those who are safe (i.e., they do not fall into Hell) and those who are not safe (they fall). The safe ones are further divided by speed of crossing: like a blink, lightning, wind, bird, swift horse, someone walking, someone crawling—this speed depends on their righteous deeds and how quickly they turn away from sinful thoughts. The faster one turns away from sin when it occurs to the mind, the quicker the crossing. Then there are those who are scratched by the hooks of the bridge and fall but manage to cling and eventually cross after years. The unsafe ones fall into Hell and are varied according to their sins, with some remaining eternally (disbelievers) and some eventually coming out (sinful Muslims) by intercession. The passage concludes that this is a possible matter informed by the Truthful (the Prophet), so belief in it is obligatory. The author does not specify which opinion on disbelievers crossing is preferred; he just reports them. This passage serves as an eschatological description to encourage good deeds and repentance.

الكفار
المؤمنون
أعمال صالحة
الإعراض عن المعاصي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyone crosses the Sirat at the same speed regardless of deeds.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that speed varies from a blink to crawling based on righteous deeds and turning away from sin.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what determines the speed of crossing for the saved?

B) Their speed of turning away from sins when they occur to the mind.
C) Their physical strength.
D) The number of good deeds only.

Key Takeaway
The speed of crossing the Sirat for the saved is a reflection of how quickly one turns away from sinful thoughts in life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a sinful thought comes to your mind, how quickly do you turn away from it? Are you like the blink of an eye or the crawling? What does your current pace reveal about your spiritual vigilance? What specific change can you make today to increase your speed?
?
The passage links crossing speed to 'the extent of their righteous deeds and turning away from sins'. Which sin do you find hardest to turn away from quickly? What one step will you take this week to cut off that sin faster?
?
Imagine standing on the Sirat, seeing your speed determined by your life's choices. Are you content with the speed you envision? If not, what is the smallest habit you can adopt starting today to accelerate your crossing?

Those Who Fall from the Sirat and the Obligation to Believe
Dardeer describes those scratched by hooks, those who fall into Hell, and the obligation to believe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fate of those who are scratched by the hooks of the Sirat and those who fall into Hell, including the distinction between eternal punishment for disbelievers and temporary punishment for sinful believers, and the obligation to believe in these reports.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a bridge of justice: some cling after falling, some fall into Hell, but intercession can save the sinful believers.

This continuation of Dardeer’s description covers the less fortunate passers of the Sirat. Some are scratched by hooks and fall, but manage to cling and eventually cross after years. Others fall into Hell, varying in punishment: disbelievers are eternal, while sinful Muslims may be released by intercession. The passage concludes by affirming that belief in these eschatological realities is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Read about those scratched by hooks
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'ومنهم مَنْ تَخْدِشُه' and notice that they fall but cling to the hooks and eventually cross after years.
These are not safe initially but become safe after struggling.
2
Understand the two categories of those who fall into Hell
The passage distinguishes between those who fall into Hell and remain eternally (disbelievers) and those who fall but later come out (sinful believers) by intercession.
Intercession is mentioned as a means for the sinful believers to leave Hell.
3
Reflect on the obligation to believe
The final sentence declares that these events are possible matters reported by the truthful Prophet, so it is obligatory to believe in them.
This reminds us that belief in the details of the Hereafter is part of faith.

The Reality of the Sirat
Dardeer affirms the Sirat as real, quotes evidence, and contrasts Sunni and Mu'tazila views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Sirat (bridge) and why it is taken literally while consigning its true nature to Allah.

Core Idea
The Sirat is real, but its true nature is known only to Allah.

Imam Dardeer begins the section on sam’iyyat by affirming the Sirat as a literal reality. He cites Quranic and hadith evidence, and explains that Ahl al-Sunnah accept the texts at face value while consigning the exact nature to Allah, in contrast to the Mu’tazila who allegorize. This lesson clarifies the Sunni stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify evidence for the Sirat
The passage cites a Quranic verse (36:66) and a hadith about the Sirat being set over Hell. Notice how these texts are presented as proof.
The verse is from Surah Ya-Sin.
2
Understand the Sunni principle of 'ithbaat with tafwid'
Ahl al-Sunnah keep the apparent meaning of these texts but entrust the true reality of the Sirat to Allah. This is the key methodological point.
3
Contrast with the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila interpret the Sirat metaphorically. Dardeer explicitly contrasts their view with the Sunni approach.
This shows the importance of literalism in eschatology.
4
Consider the opinion on creation when needed
Some scholars say the Sirat will be created at the time of need. Note that this does not contradict its reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَاطَ ) ، وفي الحديث: (ويُضَرَبُ الصِّراطُ بَينَ ظهراني جَهَنَّمَ، فأكون أنا وأمتي أول مَنْ يجوزُه)، وغير ذلك. قال ابنُ الفاكهاني: وهو موجود والأخبار عنه صحيحة .اهـ. فذهبَ أهلُ السُّنَّةِ إلى إبقائها على ظاهرها مع تفويض عِلم حقيقته إلى الله تعالى خلافًا للمعتزلة. وقال بعضهم: إنه سيوجدُ عِندَ الحاجة إليه.
(والميزان) وهو قبل الصراط، توزنُ به أعمالُ العِبادِ، ودلَّ عليه الكتاب في آيات متعددة، والسنة حتى بلغتْ أحاديثه مبلَغَ التَّواتُرِ، والحملُ على الحقيقةِ مُمكن، فيجب بالميزان الإيمان به وإنْ كُنا لا نعرفُ حقيقةَ جَوهَره، والتأويل بتمام العدْلِ كما ذهَبَ إليه المعتزلة عناد ومُكابرة. والصحيح أنه ميزان لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجمع في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ ) للتعظيم، وأَنَّ خِفَّةَ الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا، وأنَّ الكُفَّارَ توزَنُ أعمالهم كالمؤمنين بدليل قوله تعالى:
The third section: The Sam'iyyat (Revealed Matters). Allah Most High said: 'So they race to the path' (Quran 36:66), and in the hadith: 'The Sirat will be set between the two sides of Hell, and I and my community will be the first to cross it,' and other things. Ibn al-Fakahani said: It exists and the reports about it are authentic. End quote. So Ahl al-Sunnah went to keep them on their apparent meaning while consigning knowledge of its true reality to Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And some said: It will come into existence when needed. (And the Mizan) and it is before the Sirat, by which the deeds of the servants are weighed. The Book has pointed to it in multiple verses, and the Sunnah to the point that its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur. And taking it literally is possible, so belief in the Mizan is obligatory, even if we do not know the true essence of its substance. And interpreting it as perfect justice, as the Mu'tazila held, is obstinacy and stubbornness. And the correct view is that it is a scale for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in His saying 'and We will set up the just scales' (Quran 21:47) is for magnification; and that the lightness or heaviness of what is weighed is in its form in this world; and that the disbelievers' deeds are weighed like the believers' deeds, as evidence from His saying:
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on Sam'iyyat (matters known only through revelation). It affirms the reality of the Sirat (bridge) and the Mizan (scale). For the Sirat, the author cites a Quranic verse and a hadith, then quotes Ibn al-Fakahani confirming its existence and authentic reports. He states that Ahl al-Sunnah take these texts at face value while leaving the exact nature to Allah, opposing the Mu'tazila who allegorize them. Some scholars say the Sirat will be created when needed. Then the author discusses the Mizan, which comes before the Sirat. It is a scale that weighs deeds. Proofs from Quran (multiple verses) and Sunnah (mutawatir hadiths) confirm it. Taking it literally is possible (i.e., it is a real scale with weight), so belief in it is obligatory, even if we do not know its substance. The Mu'tazila interpret it as 'perfect justice' metaphorically, but the author calls this stubbornness. The correct view is that it is a scale for all nations and deeds; the plural in the Quran (mawazin) is for emphasis/magnification. The weight of deeds appears as their form in this world (e.g., good deeds as heavy, bad as light). Disbelievers' deeds are also weighed, just like believers', based on Quranic evidence (the verse is cut off here but implies this). The passage thus defends the Sunni literal approach to eschatological realities.

الصراط
السمعيات
تفويض
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sirat is only metaphorical or does not exist.
Correction: The passage affirms its existence based on authentic revelation; Sunnis take it literally while leaving its true nature to Allah.

Checkpoint
What is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the Sirat according to the passage?
A) They interpret it metaphorically.
B) They take it on its apparent meaning while consigning the true reality to Allah.
C) They deny it as a fable.
D) They only accept the hadith but not the Quranic verse.

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is real; Sunnis affirm it literally and entrust its true nature to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the Sirat, but do you live today with the awareness that you will cross it? How does that affect your choices this hour?
?
The Mu'tazila explained it away because it was hard to accept. What difficult truths about the unseen are you tempted to rationalize instead of submitting?
?
If the true reality of the Sirat is known only to Allah, are you content to trust Him without needing to picture it? Or do you seek to define it for yourself?

The Reality of the Mizan
Dardeer affirms the Mizan as a real scale, cites evidence, refutes Mu'tazila metaphor, and clarifies attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni belief in the Mizan (scale) as a real instrument for weighing deeds, and how it refutes the Mu'tazila metaphorical interpretation.

Core Idea
The Mizan is a literal scale for all nations and deeds, not just a metaphor.

After discussing the Sirat, Imam Dardeer turns to the Mizan. He provides scriptural proofs from Quran and Sunnah, insists on its literal reality, and refutes the Mu'tazila who interpret it as mere justice. He also explains details about its universality and the weighing of disbelievers' deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify evidence for the Mizan
The passage cites multiple Quranic verses and mutawatir hadiths as proof for the Mizan. Notice the emphasis on the abundance of evidence.
2
Understand the obligation to believe despite unknown substance
Dardeer says literal interpretation is possible, so belief in the Mizan is obligatory even if we do not know its substance. This shows the priority of revelation over reason.
3
Contrast with the Mu'tazila metaphorical interpretation
The Mu'tazila interpret the Mizan as 'perfect justice' (metaphor). Dardeer calls this 'obstinacy and stubbornness' (عناد ومكابرة).
This highlights the importance of affirming literal meanings for eschatological realities.
4
Note the details of the Mizan
The Mizan is for all nations and deeds, the plural 'mawazin' is for magnification, the form of weight appears as in this world, and disbelievers' deeds are weighed.
These details are based on Quranic evidence and are part of the Sunni creed.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَاطَ ) ، وفي الحديث: (ويُضَرَبُ الصِّراطُ بَينَ ظهراني جَهَنَّمَ، فأكون أنا وأمتي أول مَنْ يجوزُه)، وغير ذلك. قال ابنُ الفاكهاني: وهو موجود والأخبار عنه صحيحة .اهـ. فذهبَ أهلُ السُّنَّةِ إلى إبقائها على ظاهرها مع تفويض عِلم حقيقته إلى الله تعالى خلافًا للمعتزلة. وقال بعضهم: إنه سيوجدُ عِندَ الحاجة إليه.
(والميزان) وهو قبل الصراط، توزنُ به أعمالُ العِبادِ، ودلَّ عليه الكتاب في آيات متعددة، والسنة حتى بلغتْ أحاديثه مبلَغَ التَّواتُرِ، والحملُ على الحقيقةِ مُمكن، فيجب بالميزان الإيمان به وإنْ كُنا لا نعرفُ حقيقةَ جَوهَره، والتأويل بتمام العدْلِ كما ذهَبَ إليه المعتزلة عناد ومُكابرة. والصحيح أنه ميزان لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجمع في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ ) للتعظيم، وأَنَّ خِفَّةَ الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدُّنيا، وأنَّ الكُفَّارَ توزَنُ أعمالهم كالمؤمنين بدليل قوله تعالى:
The third section: The Sam'iyyat (Revealed Matters). Allah Most High said: 'So they race to the path' (Quran 36:66), and in the hadith: 'The Sirat will be set between the two sides of Hell, and I and my community will be the first to cross it,' and other things. Ibn al-Fakahani said: It exists and the reports about it are authentic. End quote. So Ahl al-Sunnah went to keep them on their apparent meaning while consigning knowledge of its true reality to Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And some said: It will come into existence when needed. (And the Mizan) and it is before the Sirat, by which the deeds of the servants are weighed. The Book has pointed to it in multiple verses, and the Sunnah to the point that its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur. And taking it literally is possible, so belief in the Mizan is obligatory, even if we do not know the true essence of its substance. And interpreting it as perfect justice, as the Mu'tazila held, is obstinacy and stubbornness. And the correct view is that it is a scale for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in His saying 'and We will set up the just scales' (Quran 21:47) is for magnification; and that the lightness or heaviness of what is weighed is in its form in this world; and that the disbelievers' deeds are weighed like the believers' deeds, as evidence from His saying:
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on Sam'iyyat (matters known only through revelation). It affirms the reality of the Sirat (bridge) and the Mizan (scale). For the Sirat, the author cites a Quranic verse and a hadith, then quotes Ibn al-Fakahani confirming its existence and authentic reports. He states that Ahl al-Sunnah take these texts at face value while leaving the exact nature to Allah, opposing the Mu'tazila who allegorize them. Some scholars say the Sirat will be created when needed. Then the author discusses the Mizan, which comes before the Sirat. It is a scale that weighs deeds. Proofs from Quran (multiple verses) and Sunnah (mutawatir hadiths) confirm it. Taking it literally is possible (i.e., it is a real scale with weight), so belief in it is obligatory, even if we do not know its substance. The Mu'tazila interpret it as 'perfect justice' metaphorically, but the author calls this stubbornness. The correct view is that it is a scale for all nations and deeds; the plural in the Quran (mawazin) is for emphasis/magnification. The weight of deeds appears as their form in this world (e.g., good deeds as heavy, bad as light). Disbelievers' deeds are also weighed, just like believers', based on Quranic evidence (the verse is cut off here but implies this). The passage thus defends the Sunni literal approach to eschatological realities.

Key Terms
الميزان
الموازين
العدل
الكفار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mizan is only a metaphor for God's justice.
Correction: The passage insists it is a real scale that weighs deeds literally, and calls the metaphorical interpretation 'obstinacy and stubbornness'.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, what is the Mu'tazila interpretation of the Mizan?
A) It is a real scale with two pans.
B) It is perfect justice.
C) It does not exist.
D) It is only for believers.

Key Takeaway
The Mizan is a real scale that weighs deeds of all people, and must be believed literally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every deed you do, even the smallest, will be weighed on a literal scale? How does that change what you did today? Write down one action you will perform differently tomorrow because you know it will be weighed.
?
The Mu'tazila rejected a literal scale because it seemed impossible to their intellect. Are there any aspects of your faith that you are tempted to re-interpret because they seem difficult to believe? What would it cost you to accept them literally as the salaf did?
?
Dardeer says the deeds of disbelievers are also weighed. If you have non-Muslim family or friends, does this knowledge affect how you view their good deeds? What should your response be to them, knowing that their deeds are weighed but they lack iman?

The Sirat (Bridge): A Sam'iyyat Reality
Sanusi enumerates the Sirat as a sam'iyyat and states the Sunni position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the Sirat (bridge) as a revealed reality whose true nature is delegated to Allah.

Core Idea
The Sirat is real, but its true nature is known only to Allah.

In this passage, the author introduces the Sirat as one of the sam'iyyat — matters known only through revelation. He cites scriptural evidence and explains the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah: affirming its apparent meaning while delegating knowledge of its reality to Allah. This lesson unpacks that position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the quotation marks and the scholar's name.
2
Identify the scriptural evidence
The passage cites a Quranic verse and a hadith. Note that the verse may be a misquotation; focus on the hadith about the Sirat over Hell.
3
Understand the Sunni position
Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the apparent meaning of the texts but delegate knowledge of the true reality to Allah (tafwid). Contrast this with the Mu'tazila who interpret metaphorically.
Tafwid is a key concept.
4
Note the additional opinion
Some scholars said the Sirat will come into existence when needed. This is a secondary detail.
5
Reflect on the lesson's implication
This lesson shows how Sunni creed balances affirming revealed truths without over-speculating on their exact nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات. قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَبَقُوا الصِّرَاطَ﴾، وفي الحديث: (ويُضَرَبُ الصِّراطُ بَينَ ظهراني جَهَنَّمَ، فأكون أنا وأمتي أوَّل مَنْ يجوزُه)، وغير ذلك. قال ابنُ الفاكهاني: وهو موجود والأخبار عنه صحيحة. فذهبَ أهلُ السُّنَّةِ إلى إبقائها على ظاهرها مع تفويض عِلم حقيقته إلى الله تعالى خلافًا للمعتزلة. وقال بعضهم: إنه سيوجدُ عِندَ الحاجة إليه.
The third section: The Audible Matters. Allah said: 'Then they raced to the path'? And in the hadith: 'The Sirat will be set up between the sides of Hell, and I and my nation will be the first to cross it' and other [proofs]. Ibn al-Fakahani said: 'It is real and reports about it are authentic.' So the Ahl al-Sunnah went to maintaining them upon their apparent meaning while delegating knowledge of its reality to Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And some said: It will come into existence when needed.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of creedal matters, the sam'iyyat (audible matters derived from revelation). The author first discusses the Sirat (bridge). He cites the Quranic verse (though apparently corrupted) and a hadith in which the Prophet describes the Sirat being set up over Hell and that he and his nation will cross first. Ibn al-Fakahani is quoted affirming its reality and the authenticity of reports about it. Then the author states the Sunni position: they affirm the Sirat based on its apparent meaning, but without claiming to know its true reality, delegating that knowledge to Allah. This is in contrast to the Mu'tazila who interpret it metaphorically. Some scholars add that it will be created at the time of need. The lesson emphasizes the importance of affirming the unseen realities as transmitted.

تفويض

Misconception: The Sirat is merely a metaphor or parable, not a real physical bridge.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the texts about the Sirat as literally true, but delegate its exact nature to Allah. The Mu'tazilite metaphorical interpretation is rejected.

Checkpoint
What is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the Sirat?
A) They interpret it metaphorically.
B) They affirm its apparent meaning but delegate its reality to Allah.
C) They deny it entirely.
D) They only accept the hadith but not the verse.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah affirm the Sirat as real but delegate its true nature to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet will be the first to cross the Sirat, and his nation will follow. Where do you honestly expect to be relative to him? What have you done today to ensure you are among those who cross safely?
?
You affirm the Sirat as real, but do you live with a sense of urgency about crossing it? What specific habit or attitude do you need to change starting today to prepare for that moment?
?
The Sunni position delegates the 'how' of the Sirat to Allah. Are there areas of your faith where you insist on understanding the mechanism before submitting? Can you name one and commit to accepting it on Allah's word alone?

The Reality of the Balance (Mizan)
Definition and proof of the Mizan, refutation of metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Mizan is a real physical scale, obligatory to believe in, and that interpreting it as mere justice is rejected.

Core Idea
The Mizan is a real scale, not a metaphor—belief in it is obligatory.

In this passage, Imam Dardir establishes the fundamental belief in the Balance (Mizan). He provides evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, insists on literal interpretation, and refutes the Mu'tazila who reduce it to mere justice. This lesson lays the groundwork for understanding this key eschatological reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's direct style and his emphasis on literal interpretation.
The passage is concise yet packed with theological assertions.
2
Identify the proofs
Look for the evidence the author cites from the Quran and Sunnah. He mentions the Book (Quran) and the Sunnah reaching tawatur.
Tawatur means mass transmission, indicating certainty.
3
Understand the refutation
The author rejects the Mu'tazila interpretation of the Balance as mere justice. Note his strong language: 'stubbornness and obstinacy'.
This shows the importance of affirming the literal reality.
4
Reflect on obligation
Despite not knowing the true essence, belief in the Balance is obligatory. This teaches us that faith in the unseen is required.
We affirm what Allah and His Messenger informed us.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والميزان وهو قبل الصراط، توزن به أعمال العباد، ودل عليه الكتاب في آيات متعددة، والسنة حتى بلغت أحاديثه مبلغ التواتر، والحمل على الحقيقة ممكن، فيجب بالميزان الإيمان به وإن كنا لا نعرف حقيقة جوهره، والتأويل بتمام العدل كما ذهب إليه المعتزلة عناد ومكابرة. والصحيح أنه ميزان لجميع الأمم، ولجميع الأعمال، والجمع في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَنَضَعُ الْمَوَازِينَ الْقِسْطَ﴾ للتعظيم، وأن خفة الموزون وثقله على صورته في الدنيا، وأن الكفار توزن أعمالهم كالمؤمنين بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُوْلَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنْفُسَهُم﴾ الآية، وأما من خفت موازينه فأمه هاوية) وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزْنا﴾ أي نافعًا. ولا يكون للأنبياء ولا للملائكة، ولا لن يدخل الجنة بغير حساب؛ لأنه فرح عن الحساب، ولا حساب على من ذكر. وهو على صورة ميزان الدنيا، له كفتان ولسان وتوزن الأعمال بأن تصور الأعمال الصالحة في صورة حسنة نورانية، فتوضع في كفة النور، وهي المعدة للحسنات، وهي عن يمين العرش، مقابلة للجنة، وتصور الأعمال السيئة بصورة قبيحة ظلمانية، فتوضع في كفة الظلمة المعدة للسيئات، وهي عن شمال العرش تجاه النار. وقيل: توزن الصحف المكتوبة فيها الأعمال؛ بناء على أن الحسنات متميزة عن السيئات بكتاب، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة). رواه الحاكم في المستدرك بسنده عن سيدنا عبد الله بن عمر رَضِى الله عَنْهُمَا، يقول: قال رسول الله : (يصاح برجل من أمتي على رءوس الخلائق يوم القيامة، فينشر له تسع وتسعون سجلا كل سجل مد البصر، ثم يقال له : أتنكر من هذا شيئا؟ فيقول : لا يا رب، فيقول: ألك عذر، أو حسنة ؟ فيهاب الرجل، فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول: بلى إن لك عندنا حسنات، وإنه لا ظلم عليك، فيخرج له بطاقة فيها أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمدا عبده ورسوله، فيقول: يا رب ما هذه البطاقة مع هذه السجلات؟ فيقول: إنك لا تظلم، قال: فيوضع السجلات في كفة، والبطاقة في كفة فطاشت السجلات، وثقلت البطاقة).
And the Balance: it is before the Sirat, deeds of servants are weighed with it. The Book has indicated it in multiple verses, and the Sunnah until its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission). Literal interpretation is possible, so belief in the Balance is obligatory even if we do not know the true essence of its substance. Interpretation as mere justice, as the Mu'tazila held, is stubbornness and obstinacy. The correct view is that it is a balance for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in Allah's saying 'And We shall set up the scales of justice' is for glorification, and that lightness and heaviness of the weighed matter is according to its form in this world, and that the deeds of disbelievers are weighed like the believers, as evidence of Allah's saying: 'And those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls' and 'But as for one whose scales are light, his refuge is the abyss' and His saying 'So We will not assign to them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' meaning beneficial weight. And it does not apply to the prophets nor to the angels, nor to those who enter Paradise without account because they are saved from account, and there is no account for those mentioned. And it is in the form of the scales of this world, having two pans and a tongue. Deeds are weighed by representing righteous deeds in a beautiful luminous form, placed in the pan of light, prepared for good deeds, which is on the right side of the Throne, facing Paradise, and evil deeds are represented in an ugly dark form, placed in the pan of darkness, prepared for evil deeds, which is on the left side of the Throne, facing the Fire. And it is said: the scrolls in which deeds are written are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from evil deeds by a book, and the hadith of the card testifies to this. Al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak through his chain from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr, may Allah be pleased with them, that the Messenger of Allah said: 'A man from my nation will be summoned before all creatures on the Day of Resurrection, and ninety-nine scrolls will be spread out for him, each scroll extending as far as the eye can see. Then it will be said to him: Do you deny any of this? He will say: No, my Lord. It will be said: Do you have any excuse or any good deed? The man will be frightened and say: No, my Lord. He will say: But you have good deeds with Us, and no injustice will be done to you. Then a card will be brought out with 'I bear witness that there is no deity but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger.' He will say: My Lord, what is this card compared to these scrolls? He will say: You will not be wronged. Then the scrolls will be placed in one pan and the card in the other, and the scrolls will fly away and the card will be heavy.'
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of the belief in the Balance (Mizan). The author begins by defining the Balance as an instrument placed before the Sirat for weighing deeds. He provides evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, emphasizing that the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir (massively transmitted). The literal interpretation is possible, so it is obligatory to believe in it despite not knowing its true substance. The author then refutes the Mu'tazila who interpret the Balance as a metaphor for justice, calling their position stubborn. Next, he establishes that the Balance is for all nations and all deeds, and that the plural 'scales' in the Quran is for glorification. He affirms that the weight of deeds corresponds to their form in this world. Disbelievers' deeds are also weighed, as indicated by verses. Then he clarifies that prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account are exempt from weighing. After this, the author provides a detailed description of the Balance: it has two pans and a tongue, good deeds are represented as luminous forms placed in the right pan, evil deeds as dark forms in the left pan. Alternatively, some say the scrolls themselves are weighed. He supports this with the famous hadith of the card with the shahada outweighing ninety-nine scrolls of sins. This hadith is quoted in full. The lesson underscores the literal belief in the scales as a real entity and the importance of the shahada.

Key Terms
الميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Balance is merely a metaphor for justice.
Correction: The Salaf affirm it as a real physical scale, and literal interpretation is possible and obligatory.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ruling on interpreting the Mizan as mere justice?
A) It is a valid interpretation.
B) It is a sign of stubbornness.
C) It is the view of the majority.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Mizan as a real physical scale is obligatory, and denying its literal reality is rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe in the Mizan as a real scale, or does your mind subtly reduce it to a metaphor? What evidence from your heart would prove your belief is genuine?
?
If your deeds were weighed today, what would the scale show? Which of your daily habits are you relying on to tip the balance?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected the literal Balance because it didn't fit their rational system. Where in your life do you resist clear teachings because they feel uncomfortable or hard to accept? What will you do about that resistance starting now?

The Scope of the Mizan: Who and What is Weighed
Clarification of whom the Mizan is for and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Mizan applies to all nations and both believers and disbelievers, except for prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account.

Core Idea
The Balance weighs everyone's deeds—except a few special groups.

Imam Dardir now clarifies the scope of the Balance. He affirms it is for all nations and all deeds, including those of disbelievers. He also explains that prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account are exempt from weighing. This lesson broadens our understanding of the Mizan's universality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the phrases indicating universality and exception.
2
Identify the universality
The author says it is for all nations and all deeds. The plural 'scales' is for glorification, not multiple balances.
This counters the idea that only Muslims are weighed.
3
Disbelievers' deeds weighed
The author explicitly states that disbelievers' deeds are weighed, quoting Quranic verses.
Even disbelievers will have their deeds measured, though they may not benefit.
4
Exceptions
Prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account are not weighed because they are beyond account.
They are saved from the stress of weighing.

And the Balance: it is before the Sirat, deeds of servants are weighed with it. The Book has indicated it in multiple verses, and the Sunnah until its hadiths have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission). Literal interpretation is possible, so belief in the Balance is obligatory even if we do not know the true essence of its substance. Interpretation as mere justice, as the Mu'tazila held, is stubbornness and obstinacy. The correct view is that it is a balance for all nations and for all deeds, and the plural in Allah's saying 'And We shall set up the scales of justice' is for glorification, and that lightness and heaviness of the weighed matter is according to its form in this world, and that the deeds of disbelievers are weighed like the believers, as evidence of Allah's saying: 'And those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls' and 'But as for one whose scales are light, his refuge is the abyss' and His saying 'So We will not assign to them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' meaning beneficial weight. And it does not apply to the prophets nor to the angels, nor to those who enter Paradise without account because they are saved from account, and there is no account for those mentioned. And it is in the form of the scales of this world, having two pans and a tongue. Deeds are weighed by representing righteous deeds in a beautiful luminous form, placed in the pan of light, prepared for good deeds, which is on the right side of the Throne, facing Paradise, and evil deeds are represented in an ugly dark form, placed in the pan of darkness, prepared for evil deeds, which is on the left side of the Throne, facing the Fire. And it is said: the scrolls in which deeds are written are weighed, based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from evil deeds by a book, and the hadith of the card testifies to this. Al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak through his chain from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr, may Allah be pleased with them, that the Messenger of Allah said: 'A man from my nation will be summoned before all creatures on the Day of Resurrection, and ninety-nine scrolls will be spread out for him, each scroll extending as far as the eye can see. Then it will be said to him: Do you deny any of this? He will say: No, my Lord. It will be said: Do you have any excuse or any good deed? The man will be frightened and say: No, my Lord. He will say: But you have good deeds with Us, and no injustice will be done to you. Then a card will be brought out with 'I bear witness that there is no deity but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger.' He will say: My Lord, what is this card compared to these scrolls? He will say: You will not be wronged. Then the scrolls will be placed in one pan and the card in the other, and the scrolls will fly away and the card will be heavy.'
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of the belief in the Balance (Mizan). The author begins by defining the Balance as an instrument placed before the Sirat for weighing deeds. He provides evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, emphasizing that the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir (massively transmitted). The literal interpretation is possible, so it is obligatory to believe in it despite not knowing its true substance. The author then refutes the Mu'tazila who interpret the Balance as a metaphor for justice, calling their position stubborn. Next, he establishes that the Balance is for all nations and all deeds, and that the plural 'scales' in the Quran is for glorification. He affirms that the weight of deeds corresponds to their form in this world. Disbelievers' deeds are also weighed, as indicated by verses. Then he clarifies that prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account are exempt from weighing. After this, the author provides a detailed description of the Balance: it has two pans and a tongue, good deeds are represented as luminous forms placed in the right pan, evil deeds as dark forms in the left pan. Alternatively, some say the scrolls themselves are weighed. He supports this with the famous hadith of the card with the shahada outweighing ninety-nine scrolls of sins. This hadith is quoted in full. The lesson underscores the literal belief in the scales as a real entity and the importance of the shahada.

Key Terms
الميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only believers' deeds are weighed in the Mizan.
Correction: Both believers and disbelievers have their deeds weighed, though for disbelievers, the weight may not be beneficial.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, whose deeds are NOT weighed on the Mizan?
A) Disbelievers
B) Prophets
C) Sinners among the believers
D) All humans

Key Takeaway
The Mizan weighs all deeds of all nations, except prophets, angels, and those who enter Paradise without account.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your deeds were placed on the Mizan right now, would the scale tip toward heaviness or lightness? What specific deed this week would you say is the heaviest in sincerity?
?
The author says that disbelievers' deeds are weighed but ultimately have no beneficial weight. Are there deeds in your life that you are proud of but that lack the weight of sincere faith? What would you change to ensure your deeds carry true weight?
?
Prophets and a fortunate few enter Paradise without an account. How does that reality humble you? Are you relying on your own deeds or on the mercy of Allah to be among them? What would it take for you to truly trust His mercy over your deeds?

Physical Description of the Mizan and the Hadith of the Card
Physical description of the Mizan and the weighing process, including the hadith of the card.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical description of the Mizan, how deeds are represented, and the significance of the hadith of the card with the shahada.

Core Idea
The Mizan has two pans and a tongue; one good deed like the shahada can outweigh countless sins.

This lesson provides a vivid description of the Mizan's form and the process of weighing deeds. Imam Dardir mentions that good deeds are represented as luminous forms, evil deeds as dark forms, and cites the famous hadith of the card bearing the shahada outweighing ninety-nine scrolls of sins. This emphasizes the power of sincere faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the description
Read the Arabic and translation. Visualize the two pans, the tongue, and the placement relative to the Throne.
2
Understand the representation of deeds
Deeds are not placed literally; they take on forms: luminous for good, dark for evil.
This shows the spiritual reality behind actions.
3
Study the hadith of the card
Read the hadith carefully. Notice the overwhelming scrolls of sins and the single card with the shahada that outweighs them.
This hadith illustrates the immense value of tawheed.
4
Reflect on the lesson
The hadith teaches that sincere declaration of faith can tip the scales despite many sins.
Encourages reliance on Allah's mercy.
