The Reality and Form of the Balance
Sanusi establishes the Balance with Quranic evidence, describes its form and application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Balance on Judgment Day is a real physical scale with two pans and a tongue, and that it applies only to those under accountability, not to prophets or angels.

Core Idea
The Balance is real, with form and function, and it is for the accountable.

Sanusi begins by affirming the Balance as a sensory reality transmitted in revelation. He cites Quranic verses, then clarifies its scope and physical description. Read on to grasp the essential features of this cosmic scale.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses and note the emphasis on 'weight'
The passage opens with two Quranic verses about scales being light. These establish the reality of weighing deeds. Notice that the third verse says 'no weight' meaning no beneficial weight, which excludes prophets and angels.
The verses are from Surah al-A'raf (7:9), Surah al-Qari'ah (101:8-9), and Surah al-Kahf (18:105).
2
Understand who the Balance applies to
Sanusi clarifies that the Balance is for those who are accountable. Prophets and angels are exempt; they will enter Paradise without account because they are free from sin.
3
Visualize the form – two pans and a tongue
The Balance is described as having two pans (kiffatan) and a tongue (lisan). Righteous deeds become luminous and are placed in the pan of light on the right of the Throne; evil deeds become dark and are placed in the pan of darkness on the left of the Throne.
This physical description emphasizes the reality of the Balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُوْلَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنْفُسَهُم الآية، وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأَتُهُ هَاوِيَةٌ وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نُقِيمُ هُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزْنا﴾ أي نافعًا. ولا يكون للأنبياء ولا للملائكة، ولا لَنْ يَدخُلَ الجنَّةَ بِغَيْرِ حساب؛ لأنه فرحٌ عن الحساب، ولا حساب على منْ ذُكِرَ. وهو على صورةِ ميزانِ الدُّنيا، له كِفْتانِ ولسان وتوزَنُ الأعمالُ بأنْ تُصَوَّرَ الأعمال الصالحة في صورة حسَنةٍ نورانية، فتوضَعَ فِي كِفْةِ النور، وهي المعدة للحسَناتِ، وهي عن يمين العرْشِ، مقابلة للجنَّةِ، وتُصوَّرَ الأعمال السَّيِّئَةُ بصورة قبيحةٍ ظُلْمانيّة، فتوضَعَ فِي كِفْةِ الظُّلْمَةِ المُعَدّةِ للسَّيِّئَاتِ، وهي عنْ شِمال العرش تجاه النّار. وقيل: توزَنُ الصُّحُفُ المكتوبة فيها الأعمال؛ بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات مُتميّزة عن السيِّئاتِ بكتاب، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة. رواه الحاكم في المستدرك بسنده عن سيدنا عبد الله بن عمر و رَضِى الله عَنْهُمَا، يقول: قال رسول الله ﷺ: يصاح برجل من أمتي على رءوس الخلائق يوم القيامة، فينشر له تسع وتسعون سجلا كل سجل مد البصر، ثم يقال له: أتنكر من هذا شيئا؟ فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول: ألك عذر، أو حسنة؟ فيهاب الرجل، فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول: بلى إن لك عندنا حسنات، وإنه لا ظلم عليك، فيخرج له بطاقة فيها أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمدا عبده ورسوله، فيقول: يا رب ما هذه البطاقة مع هذه السجلات؟ فيقول: إنك لا تظلم، قال: فيوضع السجلات في كفة، والبطاقة في كفة فطاشت السجلات، وثقلت البطاقة. القسم الثالث: السمعيات وهناك صنج مثاقيل الذرّ يُعلَمُ بها كَمّيّة التفاوت تحقيقا لتمام العدل فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ * وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًا يَرَهُ
And those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls—the verse. And as for he whose scales are light, his refuge is the Abyss. And His saying, the Exalted: 'And We shall not set up for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' meaning beneficial. And it (the Balance) does not apply to the prophets nor to the angels, nor will they enter Paradise without account; because it (the Balance) is for those who are accountable, and there is no accounting for those who have been mentioned. And it is in the form of the worldly balance: it has two pans and a tongue. And deeds are weighed by transforming righteous deeds into a beautiful, luminous form, which is placed in the pan of light, which is prepared for good deeds, and it is on the right side of the Throne, opposite Paradise. And evil deeds are transformed into an ugly, dark form, which is placed in the pan of darkness, prepared for evil deeds, and it is on the left side of the Throne, toward the Fire. And it is said: the scrolls in which deeds are written are weighed; based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from evil deeds by a book. And the hadith of the card (al-bitaqah) testifies to it. Al-Hakim narrated it in al-Mustadrak on the authority of our master 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr (may Allah be pleased with them both): He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'A man from my community will be summoned before the creatures on the Day of Resurrection, and ninety-nine scrolls will be spread out for him, each scroll extending as far as the eye can see. Then it will be said: Do you deny any of this? He will say: No, my Lord. He will say: Do you have any excuse or any good deed? The man will be stunned and will say: No, my Lord. He will say: Rather, you have good deeds with Us, and there is no injustice upon you. Then a card will be brought out for him on which is written: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger. He will say: My Lord, what is this card compared to these scrolls? He will say: You will not be wronged. Then the scrolls are placed on one pan and the card on the other pan, and the scrolls fly up and the card becomes heavy.' The Third Section: The Sam'iyyat (Revelatory Matters). And there are (other) scales for atomic weights by which the magnitude of disparity is known, to realize perfect justice. So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage defines and describes the Balance (Mizan) on the Day of Judgment as part of the sam'iyyat (revelatory matters). It begins by citing three Quranic verses establishing that deeds are weighed: from Surah al-A'raf (7:9), Surah al-Qari'ah (101:8-9), and Surah al-Kahf (18:105). The author notes that 'weight' here means beneficial weight. Next, we learn that the Balance does not apply to prophets and angels; they will enter Paradise without account because they are free from sin, and the Balance is for those under accountability. The Balance is described as resembling a worldly scale: it has two pans (kiffatan) and a tongue (lisan). The actual weighing of deeds is explained: righteous deeds are transformed into beautiful, luminous forms and placed in a pan of light, which is on the right of the Throne facing Paradise; evil deeds are transformed into ugly, dark forms and placed in a pan of darkness on the left of the Throne facing the Fire. A second opinion is mentioned: that the scrolls containing the deeds are weighed, since good and evil deeds are recorded in separate books. Then the famous hadith of the card (bitaqah) is quoted as evidence: on the Day of Judgment, a man from the Muslim community will have ninety-nine scrolls of sins, each extending as far as the eye can see, but a single card with the testimony of faith outweighs them all, showing the power of tawhid. Finally, the passage adds that there are also scales for atomic weights (sanj mathaqil al-dharr) to measure even the smallest difference, ensuring perfect justice, citing Surah al-Zalzalah (99:7-8).

Key Terms
الميزان
الكفتان
اللسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Balance is only metaphorical or spiritual, not physical.
Correction: The passage clearly states it is on the form of a worldly balance with pans and a tongue, and deeds are physically transformed and placed, affirming its physical reality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who does the Balance not apply to?
A) The righteous believers
B) The prophets and angels
C) The disbelievers
D) The sinners

Key Takeaway
The Balance is a real physical scale with two pans and a tongue, used to weigh the luminous forms of good deeds and the dark forms of evil deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your good deeds were transformed into a luminous form right now, would they be placed on the right side of the Throne? What concrete action have you taken this week that would add weight to that pan, and what action have you neglected?
?
The passage says that the Balance is for the accountable, and you are accountable. How does knowing that each deed becomes a physical, luminous or dark form affect the way you will perform your next prayer or interaction with a family member?
?
You are not a prophet or an angel; you will be weighed. Is there a sin you have been treating as small that, in the darkness of its form, would tip your scale? What will you do today to replace that darkness with light?

The Weighing of Deeds and the Hadith of the Card
Sanusi presents the scroll-weighing view and supports it with a prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that deeds can be weighed in the form of scrolls, and the hadith of the card demonstrates the overwhelming weight of the testimony of faith.

Core Idea
A single declaration of faith outweighs ninety-nine scrolls of sins.

Having described the Balance, Sanusi now addresses an alternative view on how deeds are weighed—whether as transformed forms or as written scrolls. He then supports this with a powerful hadith that illustrates the immense weight of tawhid over a lifetime of sins. Read the hadith carefully to grasp its lesson on divine mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative opinion of weighing scrolls
Some scholars hold that the scrolls containing the deeds are weighed, since good and evil are recorded in separate books. This is based on the fact that deeds are recorded.
This view complements the transformation view; both are possible.
2
Study the hadith of the card
The hadith is cited as evidence: a man with ninety-nine huge scrolls of sins is saved by a single card bearing the testimony of faith. Note the details: the scrolls are placed in one pan, the card in the other, and the card outweighs them.
The hadith is narrated by al-Hakim from Abdullah ibn Amr.
3
Reflect on the lesson: tawhid's weight
The hadith shows that sincere faith, even when accompanied by many sins, can tip the scales towards mercy. It emphasizes the power of the declaration of faith when combined with sincerity.
This does not mean we should sin freely; it highlights Allah's mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأُوْلَئِكَ الَّذِينَ خَسِرُوا أَنْفُسَهُم الآية، وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَفَّتْ مَوَازِينُهُ فَأَتُهُ هَاوِيَةٌ وقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نُقِيمُ هُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزْنا﴾ أي نافعًا. ولا يكون للأنبياء ولا للملائكة، ولا لَنْ يَدخُلَ الجنَّةَ بِغَيْرِ حساب؛ لأنه فرحٌ عن الحساب، ولا حساب على منْ ذُكِرَ. وهو على صورةِ ميزانِ الدُّنيا، له كِفْتانِ ولسان وتوزَنُ الأعمالُ بأنْ تُصَوَّرَ الأعمال الصالحة في صورة حسَنةٍ نورانية، فتوضَعَ فِي كِفْةِ النور، وهي المعدة للحسَناتِ، وهي عن يمين العرْشِ، مقابلة للجنَّةِ، وتُصوَّرَ الأعمال السَّيِّئَةُ بصورة قبيحةٍ ظُلْمانيّة، فتوضَعَ فِي كِفْةِ الظُّلْمَةِ المُعَدّةِ للسَّيِّئَاتِ، وهي عنْ شِمال العرش تجاه النّار. وقيل: توزَنُ الصُّحُفُ المكتوبة فيها الأعمال؛ بناءً على أنَّ الحسنات مُتميّزة عن السيِّئاتِ بكتاب، ويشهد له حديث البطاقة. رواه الحاكم في المستدرك بسنده عن سيدنا عبد الله بن عمر و رَضِى الله عَنْهُمَا، يقول: قال رسول الله ﷺ: يصاح برجل من أمتي على رءوس الخلائق يوم القيامة، فينشر له تسع وتسعون سجلا كل سجل مد البصر، ثم يقال له: أتنكر من هذا شيئا؟ فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول: ألك عذر، أو حسنة؟ فيهاب الرجل، فيقول: لا يا رب، فيقول: بلى إن لك عندنا حسنات، وإنه لا ظلم عليك، فيخرج له بطاقة فيها أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمدا عبده ورسوله، فيقول: يا رب ما هذه البطاقة مع هذه السجلات؟ فيقول: إنك لا تظلم، قال: فيوضع السجلات في كفة، والبطاقة في كفة فطاشت السجلات، وثقلت البطاقة. القسم الثالث: السمعيات وهناك صنج مثاقيل الذرّ يُعلَمُ بها كَمّيّة التفاوت تحقيقا لتمام العدل فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ * وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًا يَرَهُ
And those whose scales are light, they are the ones who have lost their souls—the verse. And as for he whose scales are light, his refuge is the Abyss. And His saying, the Exalted: 'And We shall not set up for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' meaning beneficial. And it (the Balance) does not apply to the prophets nor to the angels, nor will they enter Paradise without account; because it (the Balance) is for those who are accountable, and there is no accounting for those who have been mentioned. And it is in the form of the worldly balance: it has two pans and a tongue. And deeds are weighed by transforming righteous deeds into a beautiful, luminous form, which is placed in the pan of light, which is prepared for good deeds, and it is on the right side of the Throne, opposite Paradise. And evil deeds are transformed into an ugly, dark form, which is placed in the pan of darkness, prepared for evil deeds, and it is on the left side of the Throne, toward the Fire. And it is said: the scrolls in which deeds are written are weighed; based on the fact that good deeds are distinguished from evil deeds by a book. And the hadith of the card (al-bitaqah) testifies to it. Al-Hakim narrated it in al-Mustadrak on the authority of our master 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr (may Allah be pleased with them both): He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'A man from my community will be summoned before the creatures on the Day of Resurrection, and ninety-nine scrolls will be spread out for him, each scroll extending as far as the eye can see. Then it will be said: Do you deny any of this? He will say: No, my Lord. He will say: Do you have any excuse or any good deed? The man will be stunned and will say: No, my Lord. He will say: Rather, you have good deeds with Us, and there is no injustice upon you. Then a card will be brought out for him on which is written: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger. He will say: My Lord, what is this card compared to these scrolls? He will say: You will not be wronged. Then the scrolls are placed on one pan and the card on the other pan, and the scrolls fly up and the card becomes heavy.' The Third Section: The Sam'iyyat (Revelatory Matters). And there are (other) scales for atomic weights by which the magnitude of disparity is known, to realize perfect justice. So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage defines and describes the Balance (Mizan) on the Day of Judgment as part of the sam'iyyat (revelatory matters). It begins by citing three Quranic verses establishing that deeds are weighed: from Surah al-A'raf (7:9), Surah al-Qari'ah (101:8-9), and Surah al-Kahf (18:105). The author notes that 'weight' here means beneficial weight. Next, we learn that the Balance does not apply to prophets and angels; they will enter Paradise without account because they are free from sin, and the Balance is for those under accountability. The Balance is described as resembling a worldly scale: it has two pans (kiffatan) and a tongue (lisan). The actual weighing of deeds is explained: righteous deeds are transformed into beautiful, luminous forms and placed in a pan of light, which is on the right of the Throne facing Paradise; evil deeds are transformed into ugly, dark forms and placed in a pan of darkness on the left of the Throne facing the Fire. A second opinion is mentioned: that the scrolls containing the deeds are weighed, since good and evil deeds are recorded in separate books. Then the famous hadith of the card (bitaqah) is quoted as evidence: on the Day of Judgment, a man from the Muslim community will have ninety-nine scrolls of sins, each extending as far as the eye can see, but a single card with the testimony of faith outweighs them all, showing the power of tawhid. Finally, the passage adds that there are also scales for atomic weights (sanj mathaqil al-dharr) to measure even the smallest difference, ensuring perfect justice, citing Surah al-Zalzalah (99:7-8).

Key Terms
الصحف
البطاقة
التوحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that good deeds are weighed as literal physical objects, but the hadith shows a card, which is a written testimony.
Correction: The hadith indicates that the card with the shahada is what is weighed, supporting the view that deeds in written form are weighed.

Checkpoint
In the hadith, what is written on the card that outweighs the ninety-nine scrolls?
A) The entire Quran
B) The testimony of faith
C) A list of all good deeds
D) A prayer for forgiveness

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the card proves that the testimony of faith, when sincere, can outweigh even the most numerous sins, demonstrating Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your life’s scrolls were laid bare, would your declaration of faith (shahada) be heavy enough to outweigh the record of your sins, or is your faith too light? What will you do today to increase its weight?
?
The man in the hadith had no excuse for his sins. Do you live today relying on Allah’s mercy as a free pass to sin, or does His mercy make you more eager to obey and repent?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you feel the weight of its meaning on your tongue and in your heart, or has it become a routine phrase? What would it take for it to become the most real and heavy reality in your life?

The Scales for Atomic Weights
Sanusi introduces additional scales for atomic weights to measure minute disparities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that there are also scales for atomic weights to measure every tiny deed, ensuring perfect justice as stated in the Quran.

Core Idea
Even an atom's weight of good or evil is weighed.

The passage concludes with a mention of another set of scales—those for atomic weights. These ensure complete justice, as affirmed by the Quran. This reinforces the principle that no deed, however small, is overlooked.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement about atomic weight scales
Sanusi states that there are scales for atomic weights (sanj mathaqil al-dharr) by which the magnitude of disparity is known, to realize perfect justice.
This is in addition to the main Balance.
2
Connect to the Quranic verse
He then quotes Surah al-Zalzalah (99:7-8): 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it.' This verse directly supports the atomic scales.
The verse is the primary proof.
3
Understand the purpose: perfect justice
These scales are to measure even the smallest differences in deeds, ensuring that no one is wronged. Every tiny deed is accounted for.
This emphasizes the completeness of divine justice.

The Prophet's Pool: Attributes and Scholarly Views
Describes the Pool of the Prophet, its attributes, and scholarly opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the attributes of the Prophet's Pool, its confirmation via mutawatir hadith, its timing before the Balance, and the scholarly discussion about its number and relation to al-Kawthar.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Pool is a real, blessed water source for his community, confirmed by many hadiths.

This lesson explains the Pool of the Prophet (ﷺ) as part of the sam'iyyat beliefs. We will see the overwhelming evidence from hadith, its beautiful description, and the scholarly views on whether it is one pool or two, and its relationship to the Kawthar.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Pool's description from authentic hadith
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note the description from the Two Sahihs: size, color, smell, vessels, and the effect of drinking.
The hadith is cited as proof of the Pool's attributes.
2
Learn the correct view about its universality and timing
The passage clarifies that every prophet has a pool, and the Pool occurs before the Balance (mizan). This is presented as the correct view (al-sahih).
3
Explore the disagreement on the number of pools and the role of al-Kawthar
Some scholars say there are two pools (one before the Sirat, one after), others say what is after the Sirat is al-Kawthar (a river in Paradise). The passage prefers the opinion that the pool is before the Sirat.
This shows how different traditions are reconciled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والحوض) أي: حَوضِ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وورد فيه أحاديثُ كثيرةٌ بلغت مبلغ التواتر، وفي الصحيحين: حوضي مسيرة شهر، وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيضُ مِنَ اللبن، وريحه أطيبُ مِنَ المِسكِ، وكيزانه أكثرُ مِنْ نُجومِ السَّماءِ، مَنْ شَرِبَ مِنه لا يَظما أبدا. والصحيحُ: أنَّ لكل نبي حَوضًا، فليسَ مِنْ خُصوصيّاتِ نبينا، وأنه يكون قبل الميزان. وهل هو حوض واحد، أو حوضان، والثاني بعد الصراط؟ قولان. وقيل: الذي بعد الصراط هو الكوثر، وهو نهر في الجنَّةِ لا حَوضُ، وإِنَّا الحَوضُ قَبلَ الصراط، وهو جسم مخصوص يُصَبُّ فيه ميزابانِ مِنْ ماءِ الكَوثَرِ، تَرِدُه أُمِّتُه عليه الصلاة والسلامُ، مَنْ شَربَ مِنه شَربةً لا يظمأُ بعْدَهَا أبدًا.
And the Pool: meaning the Pool of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. Many hadiths about it have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission). And in the Two Sahihs: 'My Pool is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is better than musk, and its drinking vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst again.' And the correct view is that every prophet has a pool, so it is not a particularity of our Prophet, and that it occurs before the Balance. And is it one pool or two pools, the second after the Sirat? Two opinions. And it is said: what is after the Sirat is al-Kawthar, and it is a river in Paradise, not a pool. Rather, the pool is before the Sirat, and it is a specific body into which two pipes from the water of al-Kawthar flow. His community (peace and blessings be upon him) comes to it; whoever drinks from it one drink will never thirst after it ever.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the Pool (Hawd) of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), another sam'iyyat topic. It opens by stating that many hadiths about the Pool have reached tawatur (mass transmission), ensuring certainty. It then quotes a famous reliable hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim describing the Pool: it is a month's journey in length, with equal corners, water whiter than milk, scent better than musk, and vessels more numerous than stars; whoever drinks once will never thirst again. The author then clarifies two points: first, the correct view (al-sahih) is that every prophet has a pool, so this is not unique to our Prophet. Second, the Pool occurs before the Balance (mizan). The passage then discusses a scholarly disagreement: is there one pool or two? Some say there is a second pool after the Sirat (bridge). Others say what is after the Sirat is actually al-Kawthar, a river in Paradise, not a pool, while the pool is before the Sirat. The author prefers that the pool is before the Sirat, describing it as a specific body with two pipes pouring water from al-Kawthar, and the Prophet's community drinks from it and never thirsts again.

Key Terms
الحوض
الكوثر
الصراط
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Pool is only for the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ and occurs after the Sirat.
Correction: The correct view is that every prophet has a pool, and it occurs before the Balance, not after the Sirat.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding the timing of the Pool?
A) It occurs after the Sirat
B) It occurs before the Balance
C) It occurs after the Balance
D) It occurs on the same day as the Sirat

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Pool is a real, blessed water source for his community, proven by many hadiths, occurring before the Balance, and every prophet has one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's Pool is described with water whiter than milk and a scent better than musk. Are you truly longing to drink from it? What are you doing today to ensure you are among those whom the Prophet will welcome there?
?
The hadith says whoever drinks from the Pool will never thirst again. What are you thirsting for in this life—status, wealth, pleasure—that leaves you unsatisfied? How can you shift your longing toward the eternal satisfaction of the Hereafter?
?
Every prophet has a pool, but the Prophet Muhammad's community will have access to his. Does this privilege stir gratitude in your heart? How will you thank the Prophet today through your actions and love for his Sunnah?

The Scales for Weighing Deeds
Dardeer states the purpose of the scales in weighing deeds with perfect justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose and nature of the scales (الصنج) in the afterlife as a means of achieving perfect justice by weighing even the smallest deeds.

Core Idea
The scales of the afterlife measure every atom's worth of good and evil with absolute precision.

Imam Dardeer explains one of the eschatological realities: the scales that will weigh human deeds. This lesson introduces the concept of these scales (الصنج) and their purpose in ensuring complete justice, as affirmed by the Quranic verse from Surah al-Zalzalah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the key terms: الصنج (the scales), المثاقيل (weights), الذرّة (atom).
The verse is Quran 99:7-8.
2
Identify the purpose of the scales
Look for the phrase يُعلَمُ بها كَمّيّة التفاوت تحقيقا لتمام العدل. The scales are to know the exact amount of variance in deeds to achieve complete justice.
This shows the precision of divine justice.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proof
The author quotes the Quran to affirm that every atom's weight of good and evil will be seen. How does this reinforce the purpose?
The verse directly supports the function of the scales.

The Prophet's Basin: Reality, Evidence, and Inclusivity
Dardeer describes the Prophet's Basin, its attributes, and affirms its reality for all prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of the Prophet's Basin as a concrete afterlife event, its scriptural basis from mutawatir hadith, its described attributes, and the correct view that it is not exclusive to Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
The Prophet's Basin is a real, massive pool of heavenly water—not just a metaphor.

This lesson addresses a key eschatological belief: the Basin (Hawd) of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Dardeer presents the overwhelming textual evidence for its existence and describes its extraordinary qualities. He also clarifies that this blessing is not exclusive to our Prophet, as every prophet has a basin, and it occurs before the weighing of deeds.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the doctrinal importance
The Basin is a real, physical entity in the afterlife, not a metaphor. Understand that this is a matter of faith based on scriptural evidence.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
Notice that the hadith are described as reaching the level of tawatur (mass transmission), ensuring certainty. The specific citation from al-Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) provides a detailed description.
Tawatur means the reports are so numerous that it is impossible they are fabricated.
3
Visualize the attributes from the Sahihayn
Read the hadith: the Basin is a month's journey in size, its water whiter than milk, its scent sweeter than musk, its pitchers more numerous than the stars, and drinking from it quenches thirst forever.
These superlative descriptions emphasize the immense bounty.
4
Understand inclusivity and timing
Dardeer states the correct view that every prophet has a basin, not just Muhammad (peace be upon him). Also, the Basin occurs before the Scale (al-Mizan).
This corrects a potential misconception of exclusivity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحوض أي: حوض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، وورد فيه أحاديث كثيرة بلغت مبلغ التواتر، وفي الصحيحين: 'حوضي مسيرة شهر، وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، من شرب منه لا يظما أبدا'. والصحيح: أن لكل نبي حوضا، فليس من خصوصيات نبينا، وأنه يكون قبل الميزان.
And the Basin: i.e., the Basin of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), and there have come concerning it many hadiths that have reached the level of tawatur, and in the two Sahihs: 'My Basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is sweeter than musk, its pitchers are more numerous than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again.' And the correct view is that every prophet has a basin, so it is not a particularity of our Prophet, and that it will be before the Scale.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the doctrine of the Basin (الحوض) in the afterlife. The author states that the Basin belongs to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and provides textual evidence from many hadith that have reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission), specifically citing the two Sahih collections (Bukhari and Muslim). The hadith describes the Basin's size, water, scent, and the number of its drinking vessels. The author then clarifies that according to the correct view, every prophet has a basin; it is not exclusive to our Prophet, though the famous hadiths emphasize his basin. He also asserts that the Basin occurs before the Scale (الميزان).

Are you seeking the water that truly satisfies, or are you chasing mirages that leave you empty? Pause and identify one worldly craving you can surrender today to focus on your ultimately thirst-quenching destination.
?
Every prophet has a basin for his followers, but you are part of the Ummah of Muhammad. The Prophet specifically described his basin with such detail — it is meant for you. Are you living as someone who truly believes this? If the Prophet appeared before you today, would he welcome you to his basin or turn away? The Basin: Disputed Details and Those Excluded
Dardeer discusses disputed details of the Basin and who is excluded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disputed details of the Basin (Hawd), including its number, location relative to the Sirat, and the categories of people who will be driven away from it.

Core Idea
The Basin is for the faithful, but innovators and open sinners are driven away.

This lesson explores the Prophet's Basin, a promised blessing for his community. Scholars have debated its number and location, and Dardeer explains who will be prevented from drinking from it, including a strong refutation of the Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage covers multiple disputed points.
2
Identify the two opinions on the number of basins
The passage presents two opinions: one basin, or two basins with the second after the Sirat. Some say the second is actually al-Kawthar.
Understand the relationship between the Basin and al-Kawthar.
3
Understand the description of the basin
The basin is a specific body before the Sirat, supplied by two channels from al-Kawthar. Drinking from it quenches thirst forever, but drinking in Paradise is for pleasure.
Note that this clarifies a common misunderstanding.
4
List the categories of those excluded
The passage lists: apostates, innovators of all kinds, open sinners, and oppressive rulers. The Mu'tazila are especially singled out.
These are the people who will be driven away from the Basin.
5
Reflect on the Mu'tazila opposition
Dardeer states that the Mu'tazila disagree and are more worthy of being driven away. Consider why this might be.
This connects to broader theological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل هو حوض واحد، أو حوضان، والثاني بعد الصراط؟ قولان. وقيل: الذي بعد الصراط هو الكوثر، وهو نهر في الجنة لا حوض، وإنما الحوض قبل الصراط، وهو جسم مخصوص يصب فيه ميزابان من ماء الكوثر، ترده أمته عليه الصلاة والسلام، من شرب منه شربة لا يظمأ بعدها أبدا. ويكون الشرب في الجنة، إنما هو على سبيل التلذذ لا العطش، ويطرد عنه من بدل وغير، إما بالارتداد وإما أن يحدث في الدين ما ليس منه، كأهل البدع على اختلاف أنواعهم، وكأهل الكبائر المعلنين بها، وكالظلمة الجائرين في أحكامهم؛ لأن المرتد مخلد في النار. وخالف المعتزلة في ذلك، وهم أحق بالطرد عنه من غيرهم.
And is it one basin or two basins, the second after the Sirat? Two opinions. And it is said: what is after the Sirat is al-Kawthar, which is a river in Paradise not a basin; but the basin is before the Sirat, and it is a particular body into which two channels pour from the water of al-Kawthar; his community (peace and blessings be upon him) will come to it; whoever drinks from it one drink will never thirst after it forever. And drinking in Paradise is only for pleasure, not from thirst. And he will be driven away from it who changes and alters, either through apostasy or through innovating in religion what is not from it, such as the people of innovation of various kinds, and those who commit major sins openly, and the oppressive rulers in their judgments; because the apostate is eternally in Hellfire. And the Mu'tazila disagreed in this, and they are more worthy of being driven away from it than others.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage deals with disputed aspects of the Basin. First, the number: there are two opinions on whether there is one basin or two, with the second after the Sirat (the bridge over Hell). Some say what is after the Sirat is actually al-Kawthar (a river in Paradise), not a basin; the basin itself is before the Sirat, supplied by two channels from al-Kawthar. The author then clarifies that drinking in Paradise is for pleasure only, not due to thirst. Next, he explains who will be excluded from the Basin: those who change and alter the religion, either by apostasy or by introducing innovations (bid'ah) not from the religion. This includes all types of innovators, open sinners, and oppressive rulers. The apostate is permanently in Hell. Interestingly, the author adds that the Mu'tazila oppose this view, and they are even more deserving of being driven away than others.

Misconception: Some believe the Basin is for quenching thirst in Paradise.
Correction: The text clarifies that drinking in Paradise is for pleasure, not because of thirst; the Basin's drink quenches thirst forever before entering Paradise.

Checkpoint

Definition and Seven Layers of Hellfire
Dardeer defines Hellfire and enumerates its seven layers with descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological definition of Hellfire and the names of its seven layers as described by Imam Dardeer, including the textual nuances.

Core Idea
Hellfire is a unique burning entity with seven named layers, each with a door inside the next.

Imam Dardeer provides both a linguistic and theological definition of Hellfire. He clarifies that it is not like earthly fire but a subtle burning body. He then enumerates the seven layers, though the manuscript contains an uncertain term and an apparent extra name. Let's examine the passage carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the unclear word 'وهي ن' at the beginning of the list.
2
Examine the definition of Hellfire
The passage defines 'al-Niran' as a subtle burning body. What does this imply about its nature? Compare to earthly fire.
3
Identify the seven layers
The text states there are seven layers but then lists eight names. Find each name and note the order. Which ones are certain? Which might be a scribal error?
The term 'تخراب' (Takhrib) appears after Jahannam, but it may be a corruption or a different spelling.
4
Reflect on the fuel and supplication
Consider what fuels Hellfire according to Dardeer: humans, jinn, and idols. Why does he end with a supplication?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنيران بكسر النون، جمع نار، وهي: جسم لطيف محرق يميل إلى جهة العلو. والمراد بها دار العقاب الذي أشده النار بجميع طبقاتها السبع، أعلاها جهنم وهي ن، ثم تخرب بعد خروجهم منها، فلظى، فالخطمة، فالسعير، فسقر، لعصاة المؤمنين فالجحيم، فالهاوية. وباب كل منها داخل الأخرى على الاستواء. وحرها هواء محرق، لا جمر لها سوى بني آدم والجن والأحجار المتخذة آلهة من دون الله، نعوذ بالله منها.
And 'al-Niran' (with a kasra on the nun) is the plural of 'nar' (fire), and it is: a subtle, burning body that tends upwards. And what is meant by it is the abode of punishment whose most intense form is the fire with all its seven layers: its highest is Jahannam and it is [?] then Takhrib after their exit from it, then Ladha, then al-Hutama, then al-Sa'ir, then Saqar, for sinful believers then al-Jahim, then al-Hawiya. And the door of each is inside the other on an equal plane. And its heat is a burning air; it has no embers except for the children of Adam and jinn and the stones taken as gods besides God. We seek refuge in God from it.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage defines النيران (the Fires, i.e., Hell) linguistically and theologically. It is a subtle burning body that rises upward. It refers to the abode of punishment with seven layers. The author names each layer in descending order: Jahannam (the highest), then Takhrib, Ladha, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar (which he notes is for sinful believers?), then al-Jahim, and al-Hawiya. Each layer has a door connecting to the next on the same level. The heat of Hell is described as burning air; its fuel consists of humans, jinn, and the idols worshipped besides God. The passage ends with a supplication for refuge from Hell.

?
The doors of each layer are inside the next, meaning sin can drag you deeper and deeper. Think of a sin you struggle with. If left unchecked, where could it lead you? What one step will you take today to stop its progression before it pulls you into the next door?

Who is Prevented from the Prophet's Basin?
Dardeer describes who is prevented from the Basin of the Prophet.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Drinking from the Basin is for pleasure; only those who alter the religion are driven away.

Imam Dardeer clarifies that the Prophet's Basin is a source of pleasure, not thirst, in Paradise. He then specifies that certain people are prevented from it because they have altered the religion. This lesson explores those categories and the disagreement with the Mu'tazila.

The Seven Levels of Hellfire and Its Nature
Dardeer defines Hellfire and enumerates its seven levels with description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Hellfire, the names and order of its seven levels, and the unique nature of its heat and fuel.

Core Idea
Hellfire has seven layers, each with a door, fueled by sinners and idols.

Imam Dardeer begins by giving a precise definition of Hellfire, then lists its seven levels in order from highest to lowest. He also describes how the layers are connected and what fuels them, ending with a prayer for protection. This passage establishes the reality of Hell as a physical place of punishment with distinct levels.

Guided Path
1
Read the linguistic definition
Start by reading the Arabic definition of 'al-niran' as a subtle, burning body that rises upward.
This sets the physical nature of Hellfire as a real substance.
2
Identify the seven levels
Find the list of seven names in order: Jahannam, Ladha, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar, al-Jahim, al-Hawiyah.
Jahannam is the highest; al-Hawiyah is the lowest.
3
Understand the doors and fuel
Notice that each level has a door inside the other, and that the heat is burning air with humans, jinn, and idols as fuel.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why the author provides this detail: to instill fear and a desire for protection from Hell.
The lesson ends with a prayer for refuge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والنيران) بكسر النون، جمع «نار»، وهي: جسم لطيفٌ مُحرِقٌ يميل إلى جهةِ العُلو. والمراد بها دارُ العِقاب الذي أشَدُّه النارُ بجميع طبقاتها السَّبْع، أعلاها جَهَنَّمُ وهي ن، ثُمَّ تُخَرَّبُ بعد خُروجهم منها، فلَظى، فالخُطَمةُ، فالسعيرُ، فَسَقَرُ، فالجحيم، فالهاوية (٢). وبابُ كُلِّ مِنْ داخِل الأخرى على الاستواء (۳). وحرُّها هواءٌ مُحرِقُ، لا جمر لها سوى بني آدمَ والجن والأحجار المتَّخَذَةِ آلهةً مِنْ دون الله، نعوذ بالله منها.
And 'al-niran' (with kasra on the nun) is the plural of 'nar', and it is: a subtle burning body that tends upward. What is meant by it is the abode of punishment, the most intense of which is the Fire with all its seven layers. The highest of them is Jahannam, and it is [...] then it will become ruined after they exit from it, then Ladha, then al-Hutama, then al-Sa'ir, then Saqar, then al-Jahim, then al-Hawiyah. And the door of each is inside the other on the same level. And its heat is burning air, it has no embers except the children of Adam, the jinn, and the stones taken as gods besides Allah. We seek refuge with Allah from it.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'al-niran' and describes Hellfire. It begins by giving the lexicographical definition: 'al-niran' is the plural of 'nar', meaning a subtle, burning body that rises upward. Then it explains that the intended meaning is the abode of punishment, whose most intense form is the Fire with its seven layers. The author names the seven layers in descending order: Jahannam (the highest), then after it becomes ruined when the inmates leave, Ladha, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar, al-Jahim, and al-Hawiyah. He notes that each layer has a door that leads into the next, all on the same level. He then describes the nature of its heat: it is burning air, not embers, and the fuel consists of human beings, jinn, and the stones that were worshipped as gods. The passage ends with a prayer for protection.

Correction: The author specifies that its heat is burning air, not embers, and its fuel consists of human beings, jinn, and the stones worshipped as idols.

?

?
The stones taken as gods are fuel. Do you have any 'stones' in your life—anything you elevate above Allah in your heart? Will you destroy them today before they become your fuel?

Paradise: Linguistic Meaning and Levels
Dardeer defines Paradise linguistically, lists its levels, and presents differing opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic meaning of al-jinan, the various levels of Paradise as listed by scholars, and the debate over whether Paradise is one or many.

Core Idea
Paradise has many levels, with al-Firdaws as the highest.

Before we discuss the theological realities of Paradise, we must first understand what the word 'janna' means and how scholars have described its structure. This passage from Imam Dardeer lays out the linguistic foundation and presents multiple opinions on the levels of Paradise, setting the stage for deeper discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation. Notice the flow: definition first, then enumeration of levels.
The word 'sa' in the Arabic may be incomplete; it likely means 'vast' or 'seven'.
2
Identify the levels listed
The passage lists eight names: al-Firdaws, Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, Jannat al-Na'im, Jannat al-'Adn, Dar al-Salam, Dar al-Jalal. Note that al-Firdaws is called the highest, with the Throne above it.
This is the opinion of Ibn 'Abbas and a group.
3
Compare the three opinions
The passage presents three views: (1) eight levels by Ibn 'Abbas, (2) four levels by the majority based on Surah al-Rahman, (3) a single Paradise with many names. Reflect on why these differences exist.
The author does not choose one; he presents them as valid views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والجنان) جمع «جنّة»، وهي لغة: البستان، والمراد منها دارُ الثواب، وهي سع، أعلاها وأفضَلُها الفِردَوسُ، وفَوقَهَا عَرِشُ الرحمنِ، وَمِنها تَنفَجِرُ أَنهَارُ الْجَنَّةِ، جنة المأوى، فجنَّةُ الخُلْدِ، فجنةُ النّعيم، فجنَّةُ عَدْنٍ، فدار السلام، فدار الجلالِ، هذا ما ذهَبَ إليه ابنُ عبّاس وجماعة. وذهب الجمهورُ إلى أنها أربع بدليل ما في سورة الرحمن). وقيل: الجنَّةُ واحدة، وما تقدّمَ أسماء مُسمَّى واحِدٍ، إذ كُلُّ اسم صالح لها. والجنة والنار موجودتانِ الآنَ)، والجنَّةُ هي التي أُهبِطَ مِنها آدم، خلافًا للمعتزلة الذاهبين إلى أنهما سيُوجَدانِ في الآخرة، وأَنَّ آدَمَ أَهْبِطَ مِنْ بُستانِ على ربوة مِنَ الأرضِ.
And 'al-jinan' is the plural of 'janna', and it is linguistically: the garden, and what is meant by it is the abode of reward, and it is vast, the highest and best of it is al-Firdaws, and above it is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it burst forth the rivers of Paradise, Jannat al-Ma'wa, then Jannat al-Khuld, then Jannat al-Na'im, then Jannat al-'Adn, then Dar al-Salam, then Dar al-Jalal. This is what Ibn 'Abbas and a group held. And the majority held that they are four, by evidence of what is in Surat al-Rahman. And it was said: Paradise is one, and what preceded are names of a single named entity, since every name is suitable for it. And Paradise and the Fire exist now, and Paradise is that from which Adam was caused to descend, contrary to the Mu'tazila who hold that they will be brought into existence in the Hereafter, and that Adam was caused to descend from an orchard on a hill of the earth.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage defines 'al-jinan' and discusses Paradise. It starts with the linguistic meaning: 'jinan' is plural of 'janna', meaning a garden. The intended meaning is the abode of reward. Then it describes the levels: the highest is al-Firdaws, above which is the Throne of the Merciful; from it burst forth the rivers of Paradise. It then lists six further levels: Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, Jannat al-Na'im, Jannat al-'Adn, Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. This is the opinion of Ibn 'Abbas and a group. The majority, however, hold that there are four levels, based on Surat al-Rahman. Another opinion is that Paradise is one, and the different names apply to a single reality. The author then asserts that Paradise and Hell exist now, contrary to the Mu'tazila, who claim they will be created in the Hereafter and that Adam descended from an orchard on a hill, not from the eternal Paradise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the different names of Paradise refer to completely separate, independent places.
Correction: The passage shows that while some scholars distinguish multiple levels, others consider them names for a single reality, and the names are all suitable for Paradise.

Checkpoint

A) Jannat al-Ma'wa
B) Al-Firdaws

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

The Present Existence of Paradise and Hell
Dardeer asserts the present existence of Paradise and Hell, refuting the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, contrary to the Mu'tazila who believe they will be created in the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are already created and exist presently.

A key theological debate concerns whether Paradise and Hell exist now or will be created in the future. The Ash'ari position, affirmed by Imam Dardeer, is that they exist presently, and that Adam was expelled from this same Paradise. This lesson presents the proof and refutes the Mu'tazila view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the brief but significant statement: Paradise and Hell exist now, and Adam was descended from Paradise.
Notice the immediate contrast with the Mu'tazila.
2
Understand the assertion
The author asserts two things: (1) Paradise and Hell exist at present, (2) Paradise is the one from which Adam descended.
3
Identify the refuted view
The Mu'tazila deny both: they say Paradise and Hell will be created in the future, and Adam descended from an earthly orchard.
This shows that the issue is linked to the story of Adam.

The Doctrine of Paradise: Levels and Existence
Dardeer defines Paradise, lists its levels, and affirms its current existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine regarding Paradise: its definition, the differing opinions on the number of its levels, and the Sunni affirmation of its present existence.

Core Idea
Paradise is real, present, and multi-tiered, with al-Firdaws as its highest level.

This passage concisely presents the definition of Paradise, discusses the differing opinions of the early scholars over the number of its levels, and strongly asserts its current existence against the Mu'tazila. It is a foundational text for the sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the full translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the lists of names and the mention of the Mu'tazila.
2
Understand the definition of Paradise
Identify the linguistic and religious definitions given at the beginning of the passage.
The word 'jinan' is plural of 'janna', meaning garden, but the religious meaning is the abode of reward.
3
Examine the lists of levels
Find the list attributed to Ibn Abbas (six names) and contrast it with the majority view (four gardens from Surah al-Rahman). Notice the opinion that Paradise is one entity with multiple names.
Count the names: Firdaws, Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, Jannat al-Na'im, Jannat 'Adn, Dar al-Salam, Dar al-Jalal.
4
Focus on the present existence
Read the last sentence which affirms that Paradise and Hellfire exist now, and that Adam was descended from Paradise.
This is a direct refutation of the Mu'tazila position.
5
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this matter is important for Islamic creed. It relates to the reality of the unseen and the integrity of revelation.
This lesson connects to the broader category of sam'iyyat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والجنان) جمع «جنّة»، وهي لغة: البستان، والمراد منها دارُ الثواب. وهي [سع؟]، أعلاها وأفضَلُها الفِردَوسُ، وفَوقَهَا عَرِشُ الرحمنِ، وَمِنها تَنفَجِرُ أَنهَارُ الْجَنَّةِ، جنة المأوى، فجنَّةُ الخُلْدِ، فجنةُ النّعيم، فجنَّةُ عَدْنٍ، فدار السلام، فدار الجلالِ، هذا ما ذهَبَ إليه ابنُ عبّاس وجماعة. وذهب الجمهورُ إلى أنها أربع بدليل ما في سورة الرحمن. وقيل: الجنَّةُ واحدة، وما تقدّمَ أسماء مُسمَّى واحِدٍ، إذ كُلُّ اسم صالح لها. والجنة والنار موجودتانِ الآنَ، والجنَّةُ هي التي أُهبِطَ مِنها آدم عليه السلام، خلافًا للمعتزلة الذاهبين إلى أنهما سيُوجَدانِ في الآخرة، وأَنَّ آدَمَ أَهْبِطَ مِنْ بُستانِ على ربوة مِنَ الأرضِ.

And it is [seven?]; the highest and most excellent of it is al-Firdaws, and above it is the Throne of the Most Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise gush forth. (It includes) Jannat al-Ma'wa, then Jannat al-Khuld, then Jannat al-Na'im, then Jannat 'Adn, then Dar al-Salam, then Dar al-Jalal. This is what Ibn 'Abbas and a group held. Commentary
This passage defines Paradise (al-jinan) and discusses its levels and current existence. It begins by giving the linguistic meaning of 'jinan' as the plural of 'janna', meaning garden, and then clarifies that in the religious context it means the abode of reward. The author then mentions differing opinions on the number of gardens: Ibn 'Abbas and some others enumerate six or seven, listing specific names such as al-Firdaws, Jannat al-Ma'wa, etc. The majority, however, hold that there are only four gardens, citing Surat al-Rahman. Belief in Jinn
Dardeer defines jinn as subtle fiery bodies with transformative ability.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Jinn are real, subtle fiery bodies that can change form.

Imam Dardeer begins this brief but important passage by affirming the obligation to believe in the existence of jinn. He then provides a concise definition that clarifies their nature: they are not mere spirits but subtle bodies composed of fire, endowed with the power to change their appearance. This definition grounds our belief in a tangible, created being.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the literal meaning.
Notice the concise style of the matn.

Correction: The passage affirms that jinn are actual bodies (ajsād), though subtle and fiery, and are not mere spirits.

Checkpoint
What are jinn made of according to this passage?
A) Air
B) Fire
C) Light
D) Clay

Key Takeaway
Belief in jinn is obligatory; they are real subtle fiery bodies with the ability to transform.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite Surah Al-Falaq and An-Nas seeking protection from jinn and evil. Have you ever truly pondered that these beings are real, subtle fiery bodies that can transform? What does your level of mindfulness in these verses reveal about your depth of belief in the unseen? Starting today, commit to reciting them with the conviction that you are seeking refuge from literal, transformative beings.
?
If jinn are created from fire and can transform, what does that tell you about the power and diversity of Allah's creation? How does this expand your awe of your Creator? Will you let this knowledge transform your salah from routine to a moment of profound awareness of His majesty?
?
The text says it is obligatory to believe in jinn. Have you ever considered that your belief in jinn is not optional but required? Examine your heart: do you truly affirm their existence as a reality that affects your life, or is it merely an intellectual assent? What would change if you lived with constant awareness that you share this world with these beings? Write down one concrete action you will take this week to act on this belief.

Angels: Existence and Nature
Dardeer states the obligation to believe in angels and their infallibility, then defines an angel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to believe in angels, their infallibility, and the classical definition of an angel.

Core Idea
Angels are infallible, luminous beings created to obey Allah.

This passage opens the section on belief in angels by establishing three foundational points: that belief in their existence is obligatory, that they are infallible (ma'sum), and what an angel is. Dardeer anchors his teaching in a Qur'anic verse affirming their perfect obedience, then provides a precise definition that distinguishes angels from other beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse on obedience
Begin by reading verse 66:6 cited by Dardeer. Notice how it establishes the angels' complete submission to Allah's commands. This is the basis for their infallibility.
2
Learn the definition of an angel
Dardeer defines an angel as a subtle, spiritual, luminous body capable of beautiful transformations. Understand each attribute: laṭif (subtle), rūḥānī (spiritual), nūrānī (luminous).
This definition is crucial to distinguish angels from jinn and humans.
3
Understand the two levels of belief
The passage introduces a distinction: general belief (ijmālī) in angels we know in general, and detailed belief (tafṣīlī) in those we know specifically. This lesson focuses on the general obligation.
Detailed belief will be covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(And) [belief] in the existence of (the angels) and their infallibility as well, He said exalted: "And they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded" (Qur'an 66:6). They are the plural of malak, and he is: a subtle, spiritual, luminous body having ability for beautiful transformations. And it is obligatory to believe in them generally regarding whom is known generally, and in detail regarding whom is known in detail: by individual; like Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il, and they are the chiefs of the angels, peace and blessings be upon them all, and Munkar and Nakir, and Ridwan the keeper of Paradise, and Malik the keeper of Hellfire. Or by type, like the bearers of the Throne, and the assistants of sayyid 'Azra'il, and the guardians: angels who are entrusted with guarding humans—even if a child or a disbeliever—from jinn for example, He said exalted: "For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him who guard him by the command of Allah" (Qur'an 13:11), and the writers: and they are angels who write upon the morally responsible all that issues from him of speech, even inner, and action, and belief; they do not leave him except during intercourse, ritual bath, and relieving oneself, and the well-known is that they are two angels, one called ar-Raqib and the second 'Atid, as in Surat Qaf.

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation to believe in angels, their infallibility, and the categories of belief. It begins by stating the obligation to believe in the existence of angels and their 'isma (infallibility), citing Qur'an 66:6 which states they do not disobey Allah. It then provides a definition of an angel (malak): a subtle (laṭif), spiritual (rūḥānī), luminous (nūrānī) body with the power of beautiful transformations. The next part distinguishes two levels of obligatory belief: general belief in those known generally, and detailed belief in those known in detail. Detailed belief is further divided: by individual (bi-l-shakhṣ), listing specific angels like Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il, Munkar, Nakir, Ridwan, and Malik; and by type (bi-l-naw'), giving examples such as the bearers of the Throne, assistants of 'Azra'il, the guardian angels (ḥafaza) who protect humans, citing Qur'an 13:11, and the recording angels (kataba) who write all deeds of every accountable person, with a note about when they leave. It mentions the well-known view that there are two recording angels named Raqib and 'Atid, referencing Surah Qaf.

Belief in Specific Angels: Individuals and Types
Dardeer enumerates the individual angels and types that require detailed belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major individual angels and the types of angels mentioned in revelation, including their roles.

Core Idea
Revelation names specific angels and types, each with a unique role in Allah's creation.

After establishing the general obligation to believe in angels, Dardeer now details the specific angels we must know individually, such as Jibril and Israfil, and the types of angels we must believe in, such as the guardians and recorders. This lesson covers the names and functions of these noble beings, grounding each in Qur'anic proof.

Guided Path
1
List the chief angels by name
Dardeer names Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il, Munkar, Nakir, Ridwan, and Malik. Note that these are the well-known individuals. Understand their roles if known (e.g., Jibril brings revelation, Israfil blows the Trumpet).
The first four are often called the archangels.
2
Understand belief 'by type'
Believing in types means accepting that there are categories like the bearers of the Throne, assistants to 'Azra'il, guardian angels (ḥafaza), and recording angels (kataba).
The passage gives specific details about guardians and recorders.
3
Study the guardian and recording angels
Guardians protect humans from harm, even children and disbelievers, as per Qur'an 13:11. Recording angels write all deeds, never leaving except in specific states; they are two angels named Raqib and 'Atid (Qur'an 50:17-18).
This shows the comprehensive nature of divine accounting.

Belief in Angels: Nature, Categories, and Roles
Dardeer explains the obligation to believe in angels, their nature, and categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in angels, including their nature as luminous spiritual bodies, the obligation to believe in them generally and specifically, and the categories of angels mentioned in revelation.

Core Idea
Angels are luminous spiritual beings created by Allah to execute His commands without disobedience.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's Sharh al-Kharidah establishes the core doctrines regarding angels. It defines their nature, emphasizes the obligation to believe in them, and provides a detailed classification of the angels known to us by name and type. Understanding these categories helps Muslims appreciate the unseen world that interacts with our own.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of an angel
Begin by reading the Arabic definition: angel is a subtle, spiritual, luminous body with power to assume forms. Note the three adjectives: subtle, spiritual, luminous.
This definition is key to distinguishing angels from other beings.
2
Distinguish general vs. specific belief
The passage states we must believe in angels generally and specifically. Identify which angels are known by person and which by type.
3
Explore the roles of guardian and scribe angels
Read the section about the hafaza (guardians) and kataba (scribes). Note their functions: protection and recording deeds.
Guardians protect from jinn; scribes record every action.
4
Consider the recording angels debate
The passage mentions different opinions on whether the two recording angels are fixed or change daily. Understand the dominant view that they are two angels named Raqib and 'Atid.
There is also an opinion that they alternate daily.
5
Summarize the essential belief
Conclude with the 'in summary' part: every human has guardians and scribes in a general sense.
We don't need to know the specifics of location or identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) بوجودِ (الأمْلاكِ) وعِصْمتهم ) أيضًا ، قال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ﴾ (٢)، جمعُ ملَكٍ»، وهو: جسم لطيفٌ رُوحاني نوراني له القدرة على التشكلات الجميلة. ويجب الإيمان بهم إجمالا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم إجمالا، وتفصيلا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم تفصيلا: - بالشخص؛ كجبريل وإسرافيل وميكائيل وعزرائيل، وهُم رؤساء الملائكة عليهم الصلاة والسلام أجمعين، ومُنكر ونكير (۳)، ورضوان خازن الجنان، ومالك خازن النيران. - أو بالنَّوع كحَمَلة العرش (4) ، وأعوان السيّدِ عِزرائيل، والحفظة: ملائكة وهم مُوَكِّلون بحفظ البشَر - ولو صغيرًا وكافرًا - مِنَ الجنّ مَثَلًا، قال تعالى: ﴿لَهُ مُعَقِّبَاتٌ مِّن بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ (٥) أَمْرِ اللهِ )، والكتبة: وهم ملائكة يكتبونَ على المكلف جميع ما صدَرَ منه مِنْ قَولٍ ولو نفْسيًّا وفعل واعتقاد، لا يُفارقونه إلا في حالة الجماع والغُسلِ والخلاء)، والمشهور أنها ملكان (۸) يُسمّى أحدُهُما الرقيب والثاني العتيد، كما في سورة ق. ولكُلِّ يَوم وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصْرِ وصلاة الصبح، وقيل: بل هما تكان فقط لا يتغيّران ما دامَ حيا، وإذا مات جلسا على قبره يستغْفَرانِ له، أي: إن كانَ مُؤمِنًا. ومحلها مِنَ الإنسان عاتقاه (۲) ، وقيل : ذَقَنُه، وقيل: شفَتاه، وقيلَ: عُنقه، وقيل : الناجذان (۳) ، وقيل : إنَّ الكتبة همُ الحفظة. وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده، أنَّ على الإنسان حفظةً وكتبةً على سبيل الإجمال.
And (belief in) the existence of the angels and their infallibility also, He said the Exalted: {They do not disobey Allah what He commands them and they do what they are commanded} (2). The plural of 'malak', which is a subtle spiritual luminous body having the power to assume beautiful forms. And it is obligatory to believe in them in general regarding those known in general, and in detail regarding those known in detail: - by person, such as Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il, and they are the chief angels, peace and blessings be upon them all, and Munkar and Nakir (3), and Ridwan the keeper of Paradise, and Malik the keeper of Hellfire. - Or by type, such as the bearers of the Throne (4), and the assistants of Sayyid 'Azra'il, and the guardians: angels who are entrusted with protecting humans – even a child or a disbeliever – from the jinn for example. He said the Exalted: {For him are successive angels before him and behind him, protecting him from (5) the command of Allah}, and the scribes: they are angels who write upon the morally responsible all that issues from him of speech, even inward, and action and belief; they do not leave him except in the state of sexual intercourse, ritual washing, and relieving oneself, and the well-known view is that they are two angels (8) called one of them Raqib and the other 'Atid, as in Surat Qaf. And for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the 'Asr prayer and the Fajr prayer, and it is said: rather they are two angels only who do not change as long as he lives, and when he dies they sit at his grave seeking forgiveness for him, i.e. if he is a believer. And their place on the human is his shoulders (2), and it is said: his chin, and it is said: his lips, and it is said: his neck, and it is said: the two molars (3), and it is said: the scribes are the guardians. And in summary, what must be believed is that upon the human there are guardians and scribes in a general way.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation to believe in angels and provides details about their nature and categories. It begins by defining an angel as a subtle, spiritual, luminous body capable of assuming beautiful forms. It then states that belief in angels is obligatory both in general (for those known only in general terms) and in detail (for those known by name or specific type). The passage lists angels known by person: Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il (the archangels), along with Munkar and Nakir (the angels of the grave), Ridwan (keeper of Paradise), and Malik (keeper of Hell). It then mentions categories known by type, such as the bearers of the Throne, the assistants of 'Azra'il, the guardian angels (hafaza), who protect humans, and the scribe angels (kataba), who record every speech, action, and belief of the morally responsible. Special attention is given to the recording angels: the dominant view is that they are two types (not individuals) named Raqib and 'Atid. The passage also notes that two angels alternate daily at certain prayers, and when a person dies, they sit at the grave seeking forgiveness. Various opinions are given about the location of these angels on the body. The passage concludes that the essential belief is that every human has guardian and scribe angels in a general sense.

Key Terms
ملائكة
جسم لطيف روحاني نوراني
حفظة
كتبة
رقيب
عتيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two recording angels are fixed individuals that never change throughout a person's life and are the same every day.
Correction: The dominant view names them Raqib and 'Atid, but there is also an opinion that two angels alternate daily at Asr and Fajr prayers. After death, they become the grave angels seeking forgiveness. Their location on the body is also debated. The essential belief is that guardians and scribes exist in general.

Checkpoint

A) They are pure spirits with no bodies.
B) They are luminous spiritual bodies capable of assuming forms.
C) They are physical bodies like humans.
D) They are imaginary beings.

Key Takeaway
Belief in angels is an integral part of Iman, and we affirm their existence as luminous spiritual beings with specific roles including recording and protecting humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have two angels recording every word you speak, even those muttered to yourself. What will you start saying today that you want written in your book of deeds, and what will you stop saying?
?
If you truly believed that guardian angels are constantly protecting you from harm you cannot see, how would your daily worries change? What is one fear you will hand over to Allah after reading this lesson?
?
The passage teaches that angels never disobey Allah. Look at your own obedience: which command of Allah have you been ignoring or delaying? What concrete step will you take within the next hour to begin obeying it fully?

Belief in the Guardian Angels (Hafaza)
Dardeer presents various reports about the recording angels and states the minimal obligatory belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the recording angels is obligatory in general terms, without needing to know specific details about their number, alternation, or location on the body.

Core Idea
Belief in the guardian angels is obligatory in general; details are not required.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary addresses the sam'iyyat (matters known from revelation) regarding the angels who record deeds. While there are various reported opinions about their number, alternation, and location, the author emphasizes that the essential belief is simply that every person has guardians and writers. This lesson will clarify what must be believed and what is left to scholarly discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the literal translation. Notice the different reports mentioned.
Pay attention to the variety of opinions, as the author mentions multiple views before giving the conclusion.
2
Identify the different reports
List the various opinions: alternation at Asr and Fajr, permanence, grave sitting, location on the body, and the identity of writers as guardians.
This shows the range of transmitted reports in the tradition.
3
Find the author's conclusion
The author says 'وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده...' (In summary, the obligatory belief...). This is the key point: general belief without detailed specification.
This reflects the Ash'ari principle of accepting revelation in general terms.
4
Reflect on the principle of 'ijmal
Consider why the author does not require belief in any particular detail. In sam'iyyat, many specifics are not essential for faith.
This helps avoid unnecessary theological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصْرِ وصلاة الصبح، وقيل: بل هما تكان فقط لا يتغيّران ما دامَ حيا، وإذا مات جلسا على قبره يستغْفَرانِ له، أي: إن كانَ مُؤمِنًا. ومحلها مِنَ الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذَقَنُه، وقيل: شفَتاه، وقيلَ: عُنقه، وقيل: الناجذان، وقيل: إنَّ الكتبة همُ الحفظة. وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده، أنَّ على الإنسان حفظةً وكتبةً على سبيل الإجمال.
And for every night two angels alternate at the prayer of Asr and the prayer of Fajr. And it is said: rather they are two permanent ones, not changing as long as one is alive. And when one dies, they sit on his grave seeking forgiveness for him, that is, if he was a believer. And their place in the human is his collarbones; and it is said: his chin; and it is said: his lips; and it is said: his neck; and it is said: the two wisdom teeth. And it is said: the writers are the guardians. And in summary, what must be believed is that there are guardians and writers for a human being in general terms.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage discusses the sam'iyyat (audible matters) concerning the angels who record deeds. Dardeer begins by mentioning a view that two angels alternate for each day and night, coming at Asr and Fajr prayers. Another view holds they are two fixed angels who do not change while the person lives. After death, they sit on the grave and seek forgiveness for a believer. Their location on the human body is disputed: some say on the collarbones (عَاتِقَاه), others on the chin, lips, neck, or wisdom teeth (النَّاجِذَان). Then he reconciles by saying that the writers (الكاتبة) are the guardians (الحفظة). The essential obligatory belief is that there are guardians and writers for every person, but detailed specifics are not required. This reflects the Ash'ari principle of takhsis in matters of sam'iyyat: one must affirm what is established in general and leave details to the revealed texts.

Key Terms
الحفظة
الكتبة
العاتق
الناجذان
السمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that they must know the exact number, names, and physical location of the recording angels as part of their faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the obligatory belief is only the general existence of these angels; the specific details are not required for faith and may be left to scholarly interpretation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the essential belief regarding the angels?
A) That they are exactly two angels per day.
B) That they sit on the grave only after death.
C) That there are guardians and writers for every person in general.
D) That their location is definitely the collarbones.

Key Takeaway
The obligatory belief about the recording angels is that they exist for every person, without requiring knowledge of their specific nature or location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe the guardian angels are with you now, recording your every word and deed. Are there words you have spoken today that you would be ashamed to see in your record? Right now, silently repent for one such word and resolve to speak only what is good for the rest of the day.
?
The angels seek forgiveness for the believer after death. Are you living a life that gives them something to seek forgiveness for? Think of one sin you keep repeating. Make a firm intention to stop, and ask Allah to help you, because your angels are watching.
?
You now know that you do not need to know the details of the angels. Does your heart find peace in that, or does your mind still crave control? Surrender the need to know 'how' and simply act with awareness that you are never alone—let this awareness change one action you are about to do.
