The Three Specific Intercessions of the Prophet
Dardeer enumerates three specific intercessions of the Prophet with details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specific intercessions of the Prophet Muhammad (صلى الله عليه وسلم) – their types, who shares in them, and the example of Abu Talib.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession can lighten punishment even for those who deserved eternal fire.

Dardeer continues his enumeration of the Prophet’s specific intercessions. This lesson covers three more: bringing people out of the Fire, increasing degrees in Paradise, and lightening punishment for those condemned to eternal fire. The last is illustrated by the hadith of Abu Talib, showing that intercession can benefit even a disbelieving relative.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the numbers: fourth, fifth, sixth – these continue a list.
The sixth intercession is supported by a hadith from Sahih.
2
Identify each intercession
List the three intercessions: (4) removing from Fire, (5) increasing degrees, (6) lightening punishment. Note whether each is exclusive to the Prophet or shared.
The fourth is shared with prophets, angels, and righteous believers. The fifth is possibly exclusive. The sixth is shown by the case of Abu Talib.
3
Reflect on the Abu Talib example
Consider that Abu Talib died a disbeliever, yet the Prophet's intercession lessens his punishment. What does this teach about the scope of intercession?
Intercession can benefit those who deserved eternal fire, but not necessarily remove them entirely.
4
Answer the checkpoint quiz
Test your understanding by answering the question about the sixth intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: الشفاعةُ في إخراج قوم مِنَ النارِ، ويُشاركه فيها الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحو المؤمنين.
الخامس : الشفاعةُ في زيادة الدرَجاتِ، وجَوَّزَ النَّوَوِيُّ اختصاصها به عليه الصلاةُ والسلام.
السادس : الشفاعة في تخفيف العذاب عمَّن استَحقَّ الخُلودَ في النار، كما في حق أبي طالب، ففي الصحيح (أنا أوّلُ شافع وأوّلُ مُشفّع، وأنه ذُكِرَ عِندَه عمه أبو طالب فقال: (لعله تنفعه شفاعتي فيُجعَل في ضحضاحِ مِنَ النارِ).
The fourth: intercession in bringing out a people from the Fire, and the prophets, angels, and righteous believers share with him in it. The fifth: intercession in increasing degrees, and al-Nawawi considered it possible that it is specific to him, peace be upon him. The sixth: intercession in lightening the punishment for one who deserved eternal stay in the Fire, as in the case of Abu Talib, for in the Sahih: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted, and that his uncle Abu Talib was mentioned before him, and he said: Perhaps my intercession will benefit him, and he will be placed in a shallow part of the Fire.'
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a classification of three specific types of intercession (shafa'a) of the Prophet Muhammad (صلى الله عليه وسلم). The author lists them as the fourth, fifth, and sixth, indicating this follows a previous enumeration. 

First, the fourth intercession: removing some people from the Fire altogether. The author notes that the prophets, angels, and righteous believers share in this type; it is not exclusive to the Prophet. 

Second, the fifth intercession: increasing degrees or ranks in Paradise. Here, al-Nawawi considered it possible that this type is exclusive to the Prophet, though it is not definitive. 

Third, the sixth intercession: lightening punishment for someone who deserved eternal stay in the Fire. The author gives the example of Abu Talib, the Prophet's uncle, who did not profess Islam. A sahih hadith is cited: the Prophet said he is the first intercessor, and regarding Abu Talib, he said his intercession may benefit him so that he is placed in a shallow part of the Fire (i.e., a less severe punishment). This shows that the Prophet's intercession can alleviate even eternal punishment for certain individuals.

Key Terms
شفاعة
إخراج من النار
تخفيف العذاب
أبو طالب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's intercession only benefits believers.
Correction: The sixth intercession shows that the Prophet can intercede for a disbeliever like Abu Talib, but it only lessens his punishment, not removes him from the Fire.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the sixth intercession mentioned by Dardeer?
A) To increase the degrees of believers in Paradise
B) To remove people from the Fire entirely
C) To lighten the punishment for those who deserved eternal stay in the Fire
D) To grant intercession to other prophets

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession includes lightening punishment for those who deserved eternal fire, as shown by the example of Abu Talib.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does knowing that the Prophet's intercession can lighten punishment even for someone like Abu Talib affect your view of Allah's mercy? Do you take it as a license to sin, or as a reminder of the severity of punishment that has been reduced?
?
This lesson shows that intercession is not only for removal from Fire but also for increasing ranks. Which of these types of intercession do you most desperately need in your own life right now, and what one step can you take today to seek it?
?
The Prophet's intercession for Abu Talib only reduced his punishment, not removed it entirely. Are there people in your life for whom you hope for mercy, yet they persist in turning away from faith? How does this lesson guide you in balancing hope and urgency in your da'wah?

The Dajjal and the Descent of Jesus: Agreed-Upon Signs of the Hour
Dardeer lists the five agreed-upon signs and expounds on the first two: the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major agreed-upon signs of the Hour: the emergence of the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus, and how these events are connected in Islamic eschatology.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's deception and Jesus's descent are two sides of the same prophetic narrative.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's Sharh al-Kharidah introduces the five agreed-upon signs of the Hour, then details the first two: the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus. The Dajjal is the great deceiver who will appear before the end of time, while Jesus will descend from heaven to defeat him. Understanding these signs strengthens faith in the unseen and prepares the believer for the trials of the last days.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the overall structure. Notice that the passage lists five signs, then elaborates on the first two.
The Dajjal sign includes an extended hadith from Jabir.
2
Analyze the Dajjal's name and description
Understand the etymological explanations for 'Masih' and 'Dajjal'. What do these names reveal about his nature?
The author mentions two possible reasons for 'Masih': his swift travels or his wiped eye.
3
Explore the hadith about Dajjal
The hadith from Jabir (Musnad Ahmad) provides vivid details: his appearance, his donkey, his deceptive rivers, and his apparent miracles. Reflect on how these are tests for believers.
The hadith emphasizes that only Makkah and Madinah are protected.
4
Understand the second sign: Jesus's descent
Jesus will descend as a just judge, break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya. Note that this directly counters Dajjal's false claims.
This is from a sahih hadith; no further details are given.
5
Reflect on the purpose of these descriptions
Why does the author include such detailed accounts? Consider the pedagogical goal: to inform and warn believers, strengthening their faith and discernment.
These signs are agreed upon among Sunni scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكشرائط الساعة الخمسة المتفق عليها أي علاماتها، أي: العلامات الدالة على قربها.
أولها: خروج المسيح الدجال - بالحاء المهملة - على الصحيح، سمي مسيحا؛ لمسحه الأرض في أمد يسير، أي: مدة أربعين يوما كما سيأتي في الحديث، وقيل: لأنه ممسوح العين اليسرى. ووصف بالدجال، أي: الكذاب، للفرق بينه وبين المسيح عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام.
و
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
وقيل: لأنه ما مسح على ذي عاهة إلا بَرِئَ بِإِذْنِ اللهِ تعالى، وقيل: لأنه ممسوح بالبركة. وسمي عيسى مسيحا لمسحه الأرض، أي سياحته فيها، وقيل: لأنه ما مسح على [؟].
ثانيها: نزول المسيح عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام من السماء، وقتله للدجال، ففي الصحيح (لينزلن ابن مريم حكما عدلا فليكسرن الصليب، وليقتلن الخنزير، وليضعن الجزية) الحديث.
وفي مسند أحمد من حديث جابر: (يخرج الدجال في خفقة من الدين وإدبار من العلم، وله أربعون ليلة يسيحها في الأرض اليوم منها كالسنة، واليوم كالشهر، واليوم منها كالجمعة، ثم سائر أيامه كأيامكم هذه، وله حمار يركبه، عرض جانب أذنيه أربعون ذراعا، فيقول للناس: أنا ربكم، وهو أعور، وإن ربكم ليس بأعور، مكتوب بين عينيه كافر، يقرؤه كل مؤمن كاتب وغير كاتب، يرد كل ماء ومنهل إلا المدينة ومكة حرمهما الله عليه، وأقامت الملائكة بأبوابها، ومعه جبال من خبز، والناس في جهد إلا من تبعه، ومعه نهران أنا أعلم بهما منه، نهر يقول الجنة ونهر يقول النار، فمن أدخل الذي يسميه الجنة فهو في النار، ومن أدخل الذي يسميه النار فهو في الجنة.
قال: وتبعث معه شياطين تلكم، ومعه فتنة عظيمة، يأمر السماء تمطر فيها يرى الناس، ويقتل نفسا ثم يحييها فيما يرى الناس، فيقول للناس: ...
And among the five agreed-upon conditions of the Hour, i.e., its signs, meaning the signs indicating its proximity. The first of them: the emergence of al-Masih al-Dajjal – with an unpointed ha – according to the correct view; he was called Masih because he travels through the earth in a short period, i.e., a period of forty days as will come in the hadith; and it is said: because his left eye is wiped (mamsuh). And he was described as al-Dajjal, i.e., the liar, to distinguish between him and the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace be upon him. And [continuation from page 166] And it is said: because he did not wipe over a person with a blemish except he was healed by the permission of Allah Almighty; and it is said: because he is wiped with blessing. And Jesus was called Masih because he travels the earth, i.e., his journeying in it; and it is said: because he did not wipe over [؟]. The second of them: the descent of the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace be upon him, from the sky, and his killing of the Dajjal; for in the Sahih: 'Ibn Maryam will surely descend as a just judge, and he will break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya' – the hadith. And in the Musnad of Ahmad from the hadith of Jabir: 'The Dajjal will emerge in a lapse of religion and a turning away from knowledge, and he will have forty nights during which he will travel the earth; one day among them will be like a year, one day like a month, one day like a week, then the rest of his days will be like your days. He will have a donkey on which he rides, the width between its ears being forty cubits. He will say to the people: I am your lord; and he is one-eyed, and your Lord is not one-eyed. Written between his eyes: disbeliever; every believer, literate or illiterate, will read it. He will visit every water and watering-place except Madinah and Makkah, which Allah has forbidden to him; and the angels stand at their gates. He will have mountains of bread, while the people are in hardship except those who follow him. He will have two rivers; I know them better than he: a river that says 'Paradise' and a river that says 'Fire'; whoever enters that which he calls Paradise will be in the Fire, and whoever enters that which he calls Fire will be in Paradise.' He said: 'And devils will be sent with him, and he will have a great tribulation. He will command the sky and it will rain, while the people see it; he will kill a soul then resurrect it while the people see it; then he will say to the people: ...'
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a classification and description of the first two of the five agreed-upon signs of the Hour (ashrat al-sa'a). The author first states that these signs are the well-known markers indicating the proximity of the Day of Judgment.

The first sign is the emergence of al-Masih al-Dajjal. The author explains the etymology of his name: 'Masih' because he traverses the earth quickly in forty days, or because his left eye is wiped (mamsuh). He is called 'Dajjal' meaning liar, to differentiate him from Jesus (the true Messiah).

The text then continues on page 166 with an explanation of why Jesus is called 'Masih' – because he travels the earth or because he heals by wiping. This etymological discussion leads into the second sign.

The second sign is the descent of Jesus from heaven. He will descend as a just judge, break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya, as per a sahih hadith.

Then a long hadith from Musnad Ahmad narrated by Jabir gives extensive details about the Dajjal: his emergence during a time of religious laxity; his extraordinary forty-day period where days vary in length; his one-eyed appearance with 'disbeliever' written on his forehead; his donkey and the rivers that are actually deceptive; his ability to perform apparent miracles like causing rain and reviving the dead; but all are trials. The hadith emphasizes that only Madinah and Makkah are protected from him by angels.

The description ends mid-sentence at the page break, indicating the Dajjal's address to the people.

Key Terms
شرائط الساعة
المسيح الدجال
نزول عيسى
فتنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Dajjal's apparent resurrection of the dead and control over weather are real powers.
Correction: The Dajjal's miracles are deceptive trials; only Allah has true power over life and death. The hadith explicitly states that the river he calls 'Paradise' leads to Hell, emphasizing the deception.

Checkpoint

A) 'This is the Messiah'
B) 'Disbeliever'
C) 'One-eyed'
D) 'Liar'

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's emergence and Jesus's descent are real signs of the Hour; believers must recognize the Dajjal's deception and await Jesus's coming.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were alive during the Dajjal's time and saw him revive a dead person, would your faith in Allah remain firm, or would you be tempted to believe his claim of lordship? What in your heart needs to change now so you would pass that test?
?
The hadith says that the Dajjal will emerge 'in a lapse of religion and a turning away from knowledge.' Look at your own commitment to seeking Islamic knowledge: are you part of the problem or part of the solution? What specific step will you take this week to strengthen your understanding of the signs of the Hour?
?
The Dajjal's deception includes apparent abundance (mountains of bread) while people are in hardship. Are there any false promises of worldly ease that have distracted you from preparing for the Hereafter? What comfort or pleasure do you need to question today?

The Descent of Jesus and the Killing of the Dajjal
Narration of the Dajjal's siege and Jesus' descent to kill him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events at the end of the Dajjal's trial, particularly Jesus' descent and his role in killing the Dajjal.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's siege ends when Jesus descends to kill him.

In this passage, the author narrates the dramatic conclusion of the Dajjal's trial. The believers, besieged on the Mountain of Smoke, are delivered by the descent of Jesus. Jesus leads them to victory, killing the Dajjal, who melts like salt. This account, based on authentic hadith, clarifies Jesus' role as the slayer of the Dajjal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

Notice the vivid description of the Dajjal melting like salt in water.

Identify the key events
List the main events: the siege, Jesus' descent, the dialogue about prayer, the killing of the Dajjal, and the testimony of trees and stones.
3
Consider the significance of Jesus' role

This counters the misconception that Jesus might be passive or co-exist with the Dajjal.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal lesson
Understand that this narrative is based on authentic hadith and reinforces the belief in Jesus' return and victory over falsehood.

.. O people, does anyone do such except the Lord? So the people flee to the Mountain of Smoke in Sham, then he comes to them and besieges them, and his siege becomes severe and he exhausts them greatly. The author concludes that there are authentic hadiths to this effect, and attributes it to al-Suyuti.

The Emergence and Destruction of Gog and Magog
Author details the emergence and destruction of Gog and Magog with hadith and commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of the emergence and destruction of Gog and Magog as a major sign of the Hour, including their origin, the events narrated in the hadith, and key linguistic points.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are a multitude from Adam's lineage, destroyed by God through worms after besieging Jesus.

After the Dajjal is killed, another great sign appears: Gog and Magog. The author describes their origin, their overwhelming force, and their dramatic destruction through divine intervention. This lesson presents the hadith narrative and clarifies key terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the narrative flow before diving into details.
2
Identify the three main parts
The passage has three clear sections: origin of Gog and Magog, the hadith narrative from Muslim, and linguistic commentary on key terms.
Also note the additional hadith from al-Tha'labi at the end.
3
Understand the sequence of events
Trace the steps: Jesus kills Dajjal, God reveals to move to Tur, Gog and Magog pour forth, drink Lake Tiberias, besiege Jesus, worms kill them, birds remove bodies, rain cleanses earth.
This sequence is a core part of eschatological belief.
4
Study the linguistic explanations
The author clarifies terms like 'la yadan' (no power), 'hirz' (refuge), 'al-naghaf' (worm), and 'farsi' (dead). Understanding these helps grasp the hadith precisely.
5
Reflect on the additional hadith
The hadith from Hudhayfah adds details: each tribe size, a man seeing a thousand offspring, and their arrogant arrow-shooting to the sky.
This reinforces the immense scale and punishment.

ثالثها: خُروجُ يأجوج ومأجوج - بالهمز ودونَه-، وهما قبيلتانِ مِنْ وَلَدِ يافث ابنِ نُوحٍ عليه السلام، فهُما مِنْ ذُرِّيةِ آدَمَ عليه السلام مِنْ غَيْرِ خِلافٍ. روى مُسلِمٌ مِنْ حَدِيثِ النُّواس بن سَمْعَانَ: (إِنَّ اللهَ تعالى يوحي إلى عيسى عليه السلام بعْدَ قتلِه الدجّالَ: أني قدْ أَخْرَجتُ عِبادا لي لا يَدانِ لأحَدٍ بقتالهم فحرِّزْ عِبادي إلى الطُّورِ. ويبعث الله يأجوج ومأجوج وهم مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ - أي: مِنْ كُلِّ نَشْرٍ [كذا] - يَمشونَ مُسرعين - فيمُرُّ أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية، فيشربون ماءَها - وهي بالشام، طولها عشرةً أميال - ويمُرُّ آخِرُهم فيقولون: لقد كان بهذا أثر ماء. ويحصرون عيسى وأصحابه حتى يكونَ رأسُ التَّوْرِ لأَحَدِهِم خَيْرًا مِنْ مائة دينار لأحَدِكم، فيرغب نبي الله وأصحابه إلى الله تعالى، فيُرْسِلَ الله عليهم النغَفَ في رقابهم، فيُصبحون فَرْسى كَمَوتِ نفس واحدةٍ، ثُمَّ يهبط نبي الله عيسى وأصحابه في الأرضِ فلا يجدون في الأرضِ مَوَضِعَ شِبرٍ إلا مَلأَتْه زُهومتُهم، فيرغَبُ إِلى اللهِ نبيُّ اللهِ وأَصحابه، فيُرسل الله طَيْرًا كأعناق البُختِ، فتحمِلُهم فتطْرَحُهم حَيثُ شَاءَ اللَّهُ، ثُمَّ يُرْسِلُ الله تعالى مطَرًا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنه بَيتُ مَدَرٍ ولا وَبَرٍ، فيغسِلُ الأَرضَ حتى يتركَهَا كَالزَّلَفَةِ، ثُمَّ يُقالُ للأرضِ : أنبتي ثمَرَكِ). الحديثُ. وقوله «لا يدانِ لأحَدٍ» تثنيةُ يَدِ، ومعناه: لا قدرة ولا طاقة. ومعنى «حرزهم إلى الطور» ضُمَّهم إليه واجعله لهم حِرزًا. وقوله «النغف» - بتحريكِ الغَينِ المعجمة- الدود الذي يكون في أنوف الإبل والغنم. وقوله «فَرْسى» كقتلى زِنَةً ومعنى، واحِدُه «فريس». وفي الثعلبيِّ مِنْ حديث حذيفة، قُلتُ: يا رسول الله، ما يأجوج ومأجوج؟ قال: أُمَمٌ ، كُلُّ أمةٍ أربعمائة ألف، لا يموتُ الرجُلُ حتى يرى ألفَ عَينٍ تطوفُ بَينَ يَدَيهِ مِنْ صُلْبِه، وهم مِنْ وَلَدِ آدمَ، فيسيرونَ إلى خَرابِ الدُّنْيا، فيكونُ مُقَدِّمَتُهم بالشام، وساقَتُهم بالعِراقِ، فيمُرونَ بأنهارِ الدُّنْيا فيشربون الفُراتَ ودجلةَ وبحيرةَ طبرية، حتى يأتوا بيتَ المقدس، فيقولون: قد قتلنا أهْلَ الدُّنْيا، فقاتِلُوا مَنْ في السماء، فيرمون نَشابهم إلى السماء، فيرد الله تعالى نُشّابَهم مُحْمَرًا دمًا.
Third: The emergence of Gog and Magog - with and without hamza - and they are two tribes from the children of Yafith son of Noah, peace be upon him, and they are from the progeny of Adam, peace be upon him, without dispute. Muslim narrated from the hadith of al-Nuwas ibn Sam'an: (Indeed, Allah the Exalted reveals to Jesus, peace be upon him, after he kills the Dajjal: 'I have brought forth servants of Mine whom no one has the power to fight, so move My servants to the Tur. And Allah sends Gog and Magog, and they are from every hillock pouring forth - i.e., from every high place - walking quickly. Their forefront passes by Lake Tiberias and they drink its water - and it is in Sham, its length ten miles - and their last ones pass and say: There was water here. And they besiege Jesus and his companions until the head of a bull becomes better for one of them than one hundred dinars for one of you. So the Prophet of Allah and his companions pray to Allah the Exalted, and Allah sends the worm in their necks, and they become dead like the death of one soul. Then the Prophet of Allah Jesus and his companions descend to the earth and they do not find a handspan of the earth except that it is filled with their stench. So the Prophet of Allah and his companions pray to Allah, and Allah sends birds like the necks of Bactrian camels, which carry them and throw them wherever Allah wills. Then Allah the Exalted sends rain which does not leave a mud-brick house or a tent, and it washes the earth until it leaves it like a smooth surface. Then it is said to the earth: Bring forth your fruit.) The hadith. And His statement 'no power for anyone' is the dual of 'yad', and its meaning is no ability and no capacity. And the meaning of 'move them to the Tur' is 'gather them to it and make it a refuge for them.' And His statement 'al-naghaf' - with the point of the point in the ghayn - is the worm that is in the noses of camels and sheep. And His statement 'farsi' is like 'qutla' in form and meaning, its singular is 'faris'. And in al-Tha'labi from the hadith of Hudhayfah: I said: O Messenger of Allah, what are Gog and Magog? He said: They are nations, each nation four hundred thousand. A man does not die until he sees a thousand eyes from his loins walking before him. And they are from the children of Adam. They will march to the ruin of the world, their vanguard in Sham and their rearguard in Iraq. They pass by the rivers of the world and drink the Euphrates, the Tigris, and Lake Tiberias, until they come to Jerusalem and they say: We have killed the people of the world, so fight those in the sky. They shoot their arrows to the sky, and Allah the Exalted returns their arrows red with blood.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage classifies and explains the third sign of the Hour: the emergence of Gog and Magog. The author first defines them as two tribes from the descendants of Yafith son of Noah, and clarifies that they are from Adam's progeny without dispute. Then he narrates the hadith from Muslim detailing: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, God commands him to move his followers to Mount Tur. God releases Gog and Magog, who come from every hillock. They drink Lake Tiberias dry, then besiege Jesus and his companions so severely that a bull's head is more valuable than 100 dinars. Jesus and his companions pray, and God sends worms in their necks, killing them en masse. Jesus and his companions descend but the land is filled with corpses. They pray again, and God sends birds like Bactrian camels to carry them away. Then God sends rain to cleanse the earth until it becomes like a smooth surface, and then it is commanded to bring forth fruit. The author then provides linguistic commentary: 'la yadan' means no power, 'hirz' means refuge, 'al-naghaf' is the worm in animals' noses, and 'farsi' means dead like slaughtered. Finally, he cites a hadith from al-Tha'labi via Hudhayfah with more details: each tribe has 400,000, a man sees a thousand offspring from his loins, they will march from Iraq to Sham to Jerusalem, drink rivers, and boastfully shoot arrows at the sky which return bloody.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think Gog and Magog are non-human or not from Adam's lineage.
Correction: The author explicitly states they are from the children of Yafith son of Noah, hence from Adam's progeny, without dispute.

Checkpoint
How does God destroy Gog and Magog?
A) Fire from the sky
B) Worms in their necks
C) Jesus kills them
D) They drown

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog are a divinely released multitude from Adam, destroyed by worms and removed by birds, after which the earth is cleansed and restored.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the arrogance of Gog and Magog — who shot arrows at the sky as if to defy the One above — in what areas of your life do you 'shoot arrows' at Allah's commands, acting as if you are beyond His reach or that His decrees do not apply? What will it take for you to humble yourself before Him today?
?
The earth was cleansed only after the believers prayed with desperation. Is there a 'stench' of sin or neglect in your life that you have not yet turned to Allah about with urgency? What would it look like for you to pray as if your very life depends on His mercy right now?
?
Jesus and his companions were besieged and in extreme hardship, yet they did not lose hope in Allah. When you face trials that seem overwhelming, do you turn to Allah with the same certainty that He will respond? What one trial are you carrying today that you need to surrender to Him in prayer, trusting His timing and method?

The Characteristics of Gog and Magog
Hadith from Muslim on Gog and Magog's speed and siege.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of Gog and Magog's movement and the severe siege they impose on Jesus and his companions.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog move swiftly, draining lakes and overwhelming the land.

This lesson presents the opening part of a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing Gog and Magog. It highlights their incredible speed as they pass by the Sea of Tiberias, and the dire situation when they besiege Prophet Jesus and his followers, causing extreme scarcity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage once without analysis. Let the imagery of their swift movement and the siege sink in.
Focus on the contrast between the first and last groups.
2
Identify key actions
Notice the three actions: they walk quickly, drink the lake water, and besiege Jesus. What does this tell you about their nature?
3
Reflect on the hardship
Consider the statement about the head of an ox being better than 100 dinars. What does this imply about the scarcity during the siege?
This shows extreme economic hardship.

القسم الثالث: السمعيات. يمشونَ مُسرعين - فيمُرُّ أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية، فيشربون ماءَها - وهي بالشام، طولها عشرةً أميال - ويمُرُّ آخِرُهم فيقولون: لقد كان بهذا أثر ماء. ويحصرون عيسى وأصحابه حتى يكونَ رأسُ التَّورِ لأَحَدِهِم خَيْرًا مِنْ مائة دينار لأحَدِكم، فيرغب نبي الله وأصحابه إلى الله تعالى، فيُرْسِلَ الله عليهم النغَفَ في رقابهم، فيُصبحون فَرْسَى كَمَوتِ نفس واحدةٍ، ثُمَّ يهبط نبي الله عيسى وأصحابه في الأرضِ فلا يجدون في الأرضَ مَوَضَعَ شِبر إلا مَلأَتْه زُهمتُهم، فيرغَبُ إِلى اللهِ نبيُّ اللهِ وأَصحابه، فيُرسل الله طَيْرًا كأعناق البُختِ، فتحمِلُهم فتطْرَحُهم حَيثُ شَاءَ اللَّهُ، ثُمَّ يُرْسِلُ الله تعالى مطَرًا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنه بَيتُ مدَرٍ ولا وَبَرٍ، فيغسِلُ الأَرضَ حتى يتركَهَا كَالزَّلَفَةِ، ثُمَّ يُقالُ للأرضِ : أنبتي ثمَرَكِ ) (۲). الحديثُ . ه وقوله: «لا يدانِ لأَحَدٍ» تثنيةُ يَدِ، ومعناه: لا قدرة ولا طاقة. ومعنى «حرزهم إلى الطور» ضُمَّهم إليه واجعله لهم حِرزًا. وقوله «النغف» - بتحريكِ الغَينِ المعجمة- الدود الذي يكون في أنوف الإبل والغنم. وقوله «فَرْسَى» كقتلى وزُنًا ومعنى، واحِدُه «فريس». وفي الثعلبيِّ مِنْ حديث حذيفة، قُلتُ: يا رسول الله، ما يأجوج ومأجوج؟ قال: أُمَمٌ ، كُلُّ أمةٍ أربعمائة ألف، لا يموتُ الرجُلُ حتى يرى ألفَ عَين تطوفُ بَينَ يَدَيهِ مِنْ صُلْبِه، وهم مِنْ وَلَدِ آدمَ، فيسيرونَ إلى خَرابِ الدُّنْيا، فيكونُ مُقَدِّمَتُهم بالشام، وسافتهم بالعِراقِ، فيمُرونَ بأنهارِ الدُّنيا فيشربون الفُرات والدجلة وبحيرة طبرية، حتى يأتوا بيت المقدس، فيقولون: قد قتلنا أهْلَ الدُّنيا، فقاتِلُوا مَنْ في السماء، فيرمون نسابهم إلى السماء، فيرد الله تعالى نُشّابَهم مُحْمَرًا دمًا. وقد ورد أنَّ الدجّالَ يقتُلُه عيسى بن مرْيَمَ، فيخرُجُ بعده يأجوج ومأجوج فيقتلون مَنِ اتَّبَعَ الدجّال الذي قتله عيسى، وينحَصِرُ عيسى ومَنْ مَعَه في رؤوس الجبال، فيُسَلَّط الله عليهم داءً في أعناقهم، فيموتون كمَوتِ رجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ. انتهى، ذكَرَ جميعه النفراوي في شرح الرسالة).
The third section: matters of revelation (al-samʿiyyāt). They walk quickly – the first of them pass by the Sea of Tiberias, and drink its water – and it is in Syria, its length ten miles – and the last of them pass and say: 'There used to be water here.' And they besiege Jesus and his companions until the head of an ox among them is better than one hundred dinars for one of you. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God Almighty, and God sends upon them the naghaf (maggots) in their necks, and they become dead like the death of one soul. Then the Prophet of God Jesus and his companions descend to the earth and they do not find any handspan of the earth except that it is filled with their stench. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God, and God sends birds like the necks of Bactrian camels, and they carry them and throw them wherever God wills. Then God Almighty sends rain from which there is no shelter of mud-brick nor of hair, and it washes the earth until it leaves it like a mirror. Then it is said to the earth: 'Produce your fruit.' The hadith. And His saying: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' is the dual of yad, meaning: no ability and no power. And the meaning of 'ḥurzimuhum ilā al-ṭūr' is: gather them to it and make it a refuge for them. And His saying: 'al-naghaf' – with the moving of the dotted ghayn – the worms that are in the noses of camels and sheep. And His saying: 'farsā' like qatlā in form and meaning, its singular is 'farīs'. And in al-Thaʿlabī, from the hadith of Hudhayfa: I said, O Messenger of God, what are Gog and Magog? He said: Nations, each nation four hundred thousand, a man does not die until he sees a thousand eyes circling before him from his own loins, and they are from the children of Adam. They march to the ruin of the world, their vanguard in Syria and their rearguard in Iraq. They pass by the rivers of the world and drink the Euphrates, the Tigris, and the Sea of Tiberias, until they come to Jerusalem and say: 'We have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in heaven.' They shoot their arrows at the sky, and God Almighty returns their arrows dripping with blood. And it has been reported that the Dajjal is killed by Jesus son of Mary, and after him Gog and Magog emerge and kill those who followed the Dajjal whom Jesus killed. Jesus and those with him are besieged on the mountaintops, and God inflicts upon them a disease in their necks, and they die like the death of one man. End. al-Nafrāwi mentioned all of it in his commentary on al-Risāla.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of traditions concerning Gog and Magog (Yājūj wa Mājūj) as part of the third section on samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). It begins with a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing their rapid movement: they pass by the Sea of Tiberias in Syria, the first drinking its water, the last remarking on its traces. They besiege Jesus and his followers until an ox head becomes more valuable than a hundred dinars. In response to prayer, God sends maggots (naghaf) on their necks, killing them en masse. Their corpses' stench fills the earth, so God sends birds to carry them away, then cleansing rain. This is followed by linguistic explanations: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' (no power for anyone), the dual of yad; 'ḥuriz' as refuge; 'al-naghaf' as maggots in animal noses; 'farsā' as plural of farīs (prey). Then a longer tradition from al-Thaʿlabī's commentary via Hudhayfa gives more details: each tribe of Gog and Magog has 400,000; a man sees a thousand descendants; they advance from Iraq to Syria, drink major rivers, and reach Jerusalem. They arrogantly claim to have killed earth's people and shoot arrows at heaven, which return bloodied. The passage concludes with an additional report: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and slay the Dajjal's followers. Jesus and his companions are besieged on mountains, and God destroys them with a neck disease, dying as one man. The author credits al-Nafrāwi for compiling these accounts.

بحيرة طبرية

Checkpoint
What do the last of Gog and Magog say when they pass the Sea of Tiberias?
A) We have conquered the land

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog are described as a multitude so vast that they drink entire lakes and cause extreme scarcity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith says the last of Gog and Magog find only damp ground where there was once a ten-mile lake. How often do you rush through blessings, ignoring the traces of mercy God leaves behind? Will you pause today to acknowledge His provision before it is gone?
?
If the head of an ox becomes more valuable than a hundred dinars during that siege, what does that tell you about the true worth of worldly possessions? Are you holding onto things that will mean nothing in the final hour?
?
Jesus and his companions will be besieged by a multitude that drains entire lakes. When you face trials that seem overwhelming, do you trust that God’s relief is near, or do you panic? How can you strengthen your reliance on Him today?

The Destruction of Gog and Magog
Hadith describing destruction of Gog and Magog with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three stages of divine punishment that destroy Gog and Magog: maggots, birds, and rain.

Core Idea
God destroys Gog and Magog through maggots, birds, and cleansing rain.

After the siege, Prophet Jesus and his followers pray to God. This lesson covers the miraculous destruction that follows: maggots kill them, birds remove their corpses, and rain cleanses the earth, restoring it to purity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full passage from the prayer to the restoration. Notice the sequence of events.
Pay attention to the three acts of God: sending maggots, sending birds, and sending rain.
2
Understand the terms
Review the linguistic explanations for 'naghaf' and 'farsa'. What do they mean conceptually?
These terms highlight the totality and manner of destruction.
3
Contemplate the restoration
Consider how the rain leaves the earth like a mirror. What does this signify?
Complete purification and readiness for new growth.

القسم الثالث: السمعيات. يمشونَ مُسرعين - فيمُرُّ أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية، فيشربون ماءَها - وهي بالشام، طولها عشرةً أميال - ويمُرُّ آخِرُهم فيقولون: لقد كان بهذا أثر ماء. ويحصرون عيسى وأصحابه حتى يكونَ رأسُ التَّورِ لأَحَدِهِم خَيْرًا مِنْ مائة دينار لأحَدِكم، فيرغب نبي الله وأصحابه إلى الله تعالى، فيُرْسِلَ الله عليهم النغَفَ في رقابهم، فيُصبحون فَرْسَى كَمَوتِ نفس واحدةٍ، ثُمَّ يهبط نبي الله عيسى وأصحابه في الأرضِ فلا يجدون في الأرضَ مَوَضَعَ شِبر إلا مَلأَتْه زُهمتُهم، فيرغَبُ إِلى اللهِ نبيُّ اللهِ وأَصحابه، فيُرسل الله طَيْرًا كأعناق البُختِ، فتحمِلُهم فتطْرَحُهم حَيثُ شَاءَ اللَّهُ، ثُمَّ يُرْسِلُ الله تعالى مطَرًا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنه بَيتُ مدَرٍ ولا وَبَرٍ، فيغسِلُ الأَرضَ حتى يتركَهَا كَالزَّلَفَةِ، ثُمَّ يُقالُ للأرضِ : أنبتي ثمَرَكِ ) (۲). الحديثُ . ه وقوله: «لا يدانِ لأَحَدٍ» تثنيةُ يَدِ، ومعناه: لا قدرة ولا طاقة. ومعنى «حرزهم إلى الطور» ضُمَّهم إليه واجعله لهم حِرزًا. وقوله «النغف» - بتحريكِ الغَينِ المعجمة- الدود الذي يكون في أنوف الإبل والغنم. وقوله «فَرْسَى» كقتلى وزُنًا ومعنى، واحِدُه «فريس». وفي الثعلبيِّ مِنْ حديث حذيفة، قُلتُ: يا رسول الله، ما يأجوج ومأجوج؟ قال: أُمَمٌ ، كُلُّ أمةٍ أربعمائة ألف، لا يموتُ الرجُلُ حتى يرى ألفَ عَين تطوفُ بَينَ يَدَيهِ مِنْ صُلْبِه، وهم مِنْ وَلَدِ آدمَ، فيسيرونَ إلى خَرابِ الدُّنْيا، فيكونُ مُقَدِّمَتُهم بالشام، وسافتهم بالعِراقِ، فيمُرونَ بأنهارِ الدُّنيا فيشربون الفُرات والدجلة وبحيرة طبرية، حتى يأتوا بيت المقدس، فيقولون: قد قتلنا أهْلَ الدُّنيا، فقاتِلُوا مَنْ في السماء، فيرمون نسابهم إلى السماء، فيرد الله تعالى نُشّابَهم مُحْمَرًا دمًا. وقد ورد أنَّ الدجّالَ يقتُلُه عيسى بن مرْيَمَ، فيخرُجُ بعده يأجوج ومأجوج فيقتلون مَنِ اتَّبَعَ الدجّال الذي قتله عيسى، وينحَصِرُ عيسى ومَنْ مَعَه في رؤوس الجبال، فيُسَلَّط الله عليهم داءً في أعناقهم، فيموتون كمَوتِ رجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ. انتهى، ذكَرَ جميعه النفراوي في شرح الرسالة).
The third section: matters of revelation (al-samʿiyyāt). They walk quickly – the first of them pass by the Sea of Tiberias, and drink its water – and it is in Syria, its length ten miles – and the last of them pass and say: 'There used to be water here.' And they besiege Jesus and his companions until the head of an ox among them is better than one hundred dinars for one of you. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God Almighty, and God sends upon them the naghaf (maggots) in their necks, and they become dead like the death of one soul. Then the Prophet of God Jesus and his companions descend to the earth and they do not find any handspan of the earth except that it is filled with their stench. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God, and God sends birds like the necks of Bactrian camels, and they carry them and throw them wherever God wills. Then God Almighty sends rain from which there is no shelter of mud-brick nor of hair, and it washes the earth until it leaves it like a mirror. Then it is said to the earth: 'Produce your fruit.' The hadith. And His saying: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' is the dual of yad, meaning: no ability and no power. And the meaning of 'ḥurzimuhum ilā al-ṭūr' is: gather them to it and make it a refuge for them. And His saying: 'al-naghaf' – with the moving of the dotted ghayn – the worms that are in the noses of camels and sheep. And His saying: 'farsā' like qatlā in form and meaning, its singular is 'farīs'. And in al-Thaʿlabī, from the hadith of Hudhayfa: I said, O Messenger of God, what are Gog and Magog? He said: Nations, each nation four hundred thousand, a man does not die until he sees a thousand eyes circling before him from his own loins, and they are from the children of Adam. They march to the ruin of the world, their vanguard in Syria and their rearguard in Iraq. They pass by the rivers of the world and drink the Euphrates, the Tigris, and the Sea of Tiberias, until they come to Jerusalem and say: 'We have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in heaven.' They shoot their arrows at the sky, and God Almighty returns their arrows dripping with blood. And it has been reported that the Dajjal is killed by Jesus son of Mary, and after him Gog and Magog emerge and kill those who followed the Dajjal whom Jesus killed. Jesus and those with him are besieged on the mountaintops, and God inflicts upon them a disease in their necks, and they die like the death of one man. End. al-Nafrāwi mentioned all of it in his commentary on al-Risāla.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of traditions concerning Gog and Magog (Yājūj wa Mājūj) as part of the third section on samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). It begins with a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing their rapid movement: they pass by the Sea of Tiberias in Syria, the first drinking its water, the last remarking on its traces. They besiege Jesus and his followers until an ox head becomes more valuable than a hundred dinars. In response to prayer, God sends maggots (naghaf) on their necks, killing them en masse. Their corpses' stench fills the earth, so God sends birds to carry them away, then cleansing rain. This is followed by linguistic explanations: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' (no power for anyone), the dual of yad; 'ḥuriz' as refuge; 'al-naghaf' as maggots in animal noses; 'farsā' as plural of farīs (prey). Then a longer tradition from al-Thaʿlabī's commentary via Hudhayfa gives more details: each tribe of Gog and Magog has 400,000; a man sees a thousand descendants; they advance from Iraq to Syria, drink major rivers, and reach Jerusalem. They arrogantly claim to have killed earth's people and shoot arrows at heaven, which return bloodied. The passage concludes with an additional report: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and slay the Dajjal's followers. Jesus and his companions are besieged on mountains, and God destroys them with a neck disease, dying as one man. The author credits al-Nafrāwi for compiling these accounts.

Key Terms
النغف
فَرْسَى
الزلفة
لا يدان
حرز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What kills Gog and Magog in the hadith from Muslim?
A) A disease in their necks
B) Maggots (naghaf) sent by God
C) Birds carrying them away
D) Jesus killing them

Key Takeaway
God destroys Gog and Magog through a sequence of three miraculous punishments: maggots, birds, and rain, followed by earth's renewal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that the earth was filled with the stench of corpses and then washed spotless like a mirror, ask yourself: what spiritual filth have you allowed to accumulate in your heart that needs a divine washing today? What specific sin will you beg God to remove this very night?
?
The maggots came as a sudden collective death 'like the death of one soul.' If your life were to end unexpectedly tonight, would you be ready to meet God as one who died in obedience or as one caught in heedlessness? What would you change right now to be among the first?
?
God commanded the earth to produce fruit after its purification. After Allah cleanses a person from major sins through repentance, what fruit of righteousness should be evident in your life? If no fruit is growing, what does that say about the reality of your purification?

Unseen Matters
intermediate

Gog and Magog in the Tradition of Hudhayfa
Additional tradition with details on numbers, rivers, and arrows.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the tradition from Hudhayfa describing Gog and Magog as countless nations with extreme arrogance, including shooting arrows at heaven.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are many huge nations who arrogantly challenge God in heaven.

This lesson presents an additional tradition from al-Tha'labi's commentary, narrated by Hudhayfa. It expands on the description of Gog and Magog: they are many nations, each with 400,000 individuals, who drink rivers and shoot arrows at the sky in blasphemy, only for God to return them bloodied.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the tradition from Hudhayfa. Notice the dialogue and the shocking details about numbers and actions.
Compare with the previous hadith from Muslim.
2
Understand their origin
The Prophet says they are from the children of Adam. What does this imply about their humanity despite their destruction?
They are human beings, not mythical creatures.
3
Analyze their arrogance
They claim to have killed earth's people and then challenge heaven. How does God respond?
The arrows return bloodied, showing divine power.

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of traditions concerning Gog and Magog (Yājūj wa Mājūj) as part of the third section on samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). It begins with a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing their rapid movement: they pass by the Sea of Tiberias in Syria, the first drinking its water, the last remarking on its traces. They besiege Jesus and his followers until an ox head becomes more valuable than a hundred dinars. In response to prayer, God sends maggots (naghaf) on their necks, killing them en masse. Their corpses' stench fills the earth, so God sends birds to carry them away, then cleansing rain. This is followed by linguistic explanations: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' (no power for anyone), the dual of yad; 'ḥuriz' as refuge; 'al-naghaf' as maggots in animal noses; 'farsā' as plural of farīs (prey). Then a longer tradition from al-Thaʿlabī's commentary via Hudhayfa gives more details: each tribe of Gog and Magog has 400,000; a man sees a thousand descendants; they advance from Iraq to Syria, drink major rivers, and reach Jerusalem. They arrogantly claim to have killed earth's people and shoot arrows at heaven, which return bloodied. The passage concludes with an additional report: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and slay the Dajjal's followers. Jesus and his companions are besieged on mountains, and God destroys them with a neck disease, dying as one man. The author credits al-Nafrāwi for compiling these accounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Gog and Magog are a single tribe or non-human beings.
Correction: The hadith clarifies they are many nations (أُمَم) and from the children of Adam (مِنْ وَلَدِ آدمَ), so they are human.

Checkpoint
What do Gog and Magog say when they reach Jerusalem?
A) We have conquered the land of Syria
B) We have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in heaven
C) We are the greatest army
D) Let us rest here

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog are numerous human nations who blasphemously challenge heaven, but God effortlessly humiliates them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In this hadith, Gog and Magog say, 'We have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in heaven.' When you achieve success or power, do you ever feel self-sufficient enough to disregard God's commands? Where in your life today do you need to consciously humble yourself before God, lest you fall into the same arrogance?
?
The man of Gog and Magog sees a thousand descendants from his own loins before he dies. What are you investing your energy in—your lineage, wealth, or status—that will end when you die? How can you instead focus on what will outlast you in the sight of Allah?
?
Gog and Magog drink entire rivers yet cannot contend with God. What 'rivers' have you been chasing—desires, ambitions, distractions—that have consumed your time and attention? What concrete step can you take today to turn back to Allah and prioritize your akhirah over these fleeting pursuits?

beginner

The Final Fate of Gog and Magog after the Dajjal
Report on Dajjal sequence and destruction of Gog and Magog.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events after Jesus kills the Dajjal, including the emergence of Gog and Magog and their destruction by a neck disease.

Core Idea
After Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and are destroyed by a disease in their necks.

This lesson presents the final report in the passage, which details the events after the Dajjal's death. Gog and Magog emerge, kill the Dajjal's followers, and besiege Jesus. Then God inflicts a neck disease on them, causing mass death.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the short passage about the Dajjal sequence. Note the cause and effect.
2
Identify the order of events
List the events: Dajjal killed by Jesus → Gog and Magog emerge → they kill Dajjal's followers → they besiege Jesus → God sends a neck disease → they die.
This is a different account from the hadith in Muslim.
3
Reflect on the mercy of God
Why does Jesus pray? How does God's response show mercy to the believers?
God responds to Jesus' prayer by destroying the enemy.

القسم الثالث: السمعيات. يمشونَ مُسرعين - فيمُرُّ أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية، فيشربون ماءَها - وهي بالشام، طولها عشرةً أميال - ويمُرُّ آخِرُهم فيقولون: لقد كان بهذا أثر ماء. ويحصرون عيسى وأصحابه حتى يكونَ رأسُ التَّورِ لأَحَدِهِم خَيْرًا مِنْ مائة دينار لأحَدِكم، فيرغب نبي الله وأصحابه إلى الله تعالى، فيُرْسِلَ الله عليهم النغَفَ في رقابهم، فيُصبحون فَرْسَى كَمَوتِ نفس واحدةٍ، ثُمَّ يهبط نبي الله عيسى وأصحابه في الأرضِ فلا يجدون في الأرضَ مَوَضَعَ شِبر إلا مَلأَتْه زُهمتُهم، فيرغَبُ إِلى اللهِ نبيُّ اللهِ وأَصحابه، فيُرسل الله طَيْرًا كأعناق البُختِ، فتحمِلُهم فتطْرَحُهم حَيثُ شَاءَ اللَّهُ، ثُمَّ يُرْسِلُ الله تعالى مطَرًا لَمْ يَكُنْ مِنه بَيتُ مدَرٍ ولا وَبَرٍ، فيغسِلُ الأَرضَ حتى يتركَهَا كَالزَّلَفَةِ، ثُمَّ يُقالُ للأرضِ : أنبتي ثمَرَكِ ) (۲). الحديثُ . ه وقوله: «لا يدانِ لأَحَدٍ» تثنيةُ يَدِ، ومعناه: لا قدرة ولا طاقة. ومعنى «حرزهم إلى الطور» ضُمَّهم إليه واجعله لهم حِرزًا. وقوله «النغف» - بتحريكِ الغَينِ المعجمة- الدود الذي يكون في أنوف الإبل والغنم. وقوله «فَرْسَى» كقتلى وزُنًا ومعنى، واحِدُه «فريس». وفي الثعلبيِّ مِنْ حديث حذيفة، قُلتُ: يا رسول الله، ما يأجوج ومأجوج؟ قال: أُمَمٌ ، كُلُّ أمةٍ أربعمائة ألف، لا يموتُ الرجُلُ حتى يرى ألفَ عَين تطوفُ بَينَ يَدَيهِ مِنْ صُلْبِه، وهم مِنْ وَلَدِ آدمَ، فيسيرونَ إلى خَرابِ الدُّنْيا، فيكونُ مُقَدِّمَتُهم بالشام، وسافتهم بالعِراقِ، فيمُرونَ بأنهارِ الدُّنيا فيشربون الفُرات والدجلة وبحيرة طبرية، حتى يأتوا بيت المقدس، فيقولون: قد قتلنا أهْلَ الدُّنيا، فقاتِلُوا مَنْ في السماء، فيرمون نسابهم إلى السماء، فيرد الله تعالى نُشّابَهم مُحْمَرًا دمًا. وقد ورد أنَّ الدجّالَ يقتُلُه عيسى بن مرْيَمَ، فيخرُجُ بعده يأجوج ومأجوج فيقتلون مَنِ اتَّبَعَ الدجّال الذي قتله عيسى، وينحَصِرُ عيسى ومَنْ مَعَه في رؤوس الجبال، فيُسَلَّط الله عليهم داءً في أعناقهم، فيموتون كمَوتِ رجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ. انتهى، ذكَرَ جميعه النفراوي في شرح الرسالة).
The third section: matters of revelation (al-samʿiyyāt). They walk quickly – the first of them pass by the Sea of Tiberias, and drink its water – and it is in Syria, its length ten miles – and the last of them pass and say: 'There used to be water here.' And they besiege Jesus and his companions until the head of an ox among them is better than one hundred dinars for one of you. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God Almighty, and God sends upon them the naghaf (maggots) in their necks, and they become dead like the death of one soul. Then the Prophet of God Jesus and his companions descend to the earth and they do not find any handspan of the earth except that it is filled with their stench. Then the Prophet of God and his companions beseech God, and God sends birds like the necks of Bactrian camels, and they carry them and throw them wherever God wills. Then God Almighty sends rain from which there is no shelter of mud-brick nor of hair, and it washes the earth until it leaves it like a mirror. Then it is said to the earth: 'Produce your fruit.' The hadith. And His saying: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' is the dual of yad, meaning: no ability and no power. And the meaning of 'ḥurzimuhum ilā al-ṭūr' is: gather them to it and make it a refuge for them. And His saying: 'al-naghaf' – with the moving of the dotted ghayn – the worms that are in the noses of camels and sheep. And His saying: 'farsā' like qatlā in form and meaning, its singular is 'farīs'. And in al-Thaʿlabī, from the hadith of Hudhayfa: I said, O Messenger of God, what are Gog and Magog? He said: Nations, each nation four hundred thousand, a man does not die until he sees a thousand eyes circling before him from his own loins, and they are from the children of Adam. They march to the ruin of the world, their vanguard in Syria and their rearguard in Iraq. They pass by the rivers of the world and drink the Euphrates, the Tigris, and the Sea of Tiberias, until they come to Jerusalem and say: 'We have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in heaven.' They shoot their arrows at the sky, and God Almighty returns their arrows dripping with blood. And it has been reported that the Dajjal is killed by Jesus son of Mary, and after him Gog and Magog emerge and kill those who followed the Dajjal whom Jesus killed. Jesus and those with him are besieged on the mountaintops, and God inflicts upon them a disease in their necks, and they die like the death of one man. End. al-Nafrāwi mentioned all of it in his commentary on al-Risāla.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of traditions concerning Gog and Magog (Yājūj wa Mājūj) as part of the third section on samʿiyyāt (matters heard from revelation). It begins with a hadith from Sahih Muslim describing their rapid movement: they pass by the Sea of Tiberias in Syria, the first drinking its water, the last remarking on its traces. They besiege Jesus and his followers until an ox head becomes more valuable than a hundred dinars. In response to prayer, God sends maggots (naghaf) on their necks, killing them en masse. Their corpses' stench fills the earth, so God sends birds to carry them away, then cleansing rain. This is followed by linguistic explanations: 'lā yadān li-aḥad' (no power for anyone), the dual of yad; 'ḥuriz' as refuge; 'al-naghaf' as maggots in animal noses; 'farsā' as plural of farīs (prey). Then a longer tradition from al-Thaʿlabī's commentary via Hudhayfa gives more details: each tribe of Gog and Magog has 400,000; a man sees a thousand descendants; they advance from Iraq to Syria, drink major rivers, and reach Jerusalem. They arrogantly claim to have killed earth's people and shoot arrows at heaven, which return bloodied. The passage concludes with an additional report: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and slay the Dajjal's followers. Jesus and his companions are besieged on mountains, and God destroys them with a neck disease, dying as one man. The author credits al-Nafrāwi for compiling these accounts.

الدجال
عيسى بن مريم
رؤوس الجبال
داء

A) Maggots in their necks

Key Takeaway
After the Dajjal's death, Gog and Magog are destroyed by a divine neck disease that kills them all at once.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Jesus and his companions were besieged on the mountaintops and prayed to God for deliverance. When you face trials that seem inescapable, do you turn to God with the same intensity, or do you rely on your own plans? What one step can you take today to strengthen your reliance on Allah in hardship?
?
Gog and Magog were destroyed by a disease in their necks, dying all at once as one man. This shows that God's punishment can come suddenly and collectively. Is there any sin or indulgence in your life that you are delaying repentance for, assuming you have more time? What is holding you back from turning to Allah now?
?
The Dajjal's followers perished after his death. How much do you invest in learning about the major signs of the Hour, including the Dajjal, so that you are not deceived? What specific action can you take this week to increase your knowledge of these events and strengthen your faith?

The Beast of the Earth: Emergence and Speech
Describes the beast's emergence, speeches, and physical characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of the emergence of the Beast of the Earth as a major eschatological sign, including its speech, place of emergence, and the three stages of its appearance.

Core Idea
The Beast of the Earth speaks to people, emerges in three stages, and is a key sign of the Hour.

This passage explores the fourth major sign of the Hour: the emergence of the Beast of the Earth. Based on Quran and hadith, it describes the beast's speech, its place of emergence from the Sacred Mosque, and three distinct appearances culminating in a dramatic scene during the time of Jesus. Understanding these details helps believers recognize the enormity of this sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its interpretation
Start with the verse (Quran 27:82) and the explanation of 'when the word falls upon them' meaning the approach of resurrection and punishment.
2
Understand the beast's speech
Note the three opinions about what the beast says: nullifying other religions, identifying individuals' destinies, or reproaching disbelief.
The beast does not speak physically like humans; it communicates meaning.
3
Learn the place of emergence
The Prophet said it emerges from the greatest mosque in sanctity—the Sacred Mosque (al-Masjid al-Ḥaram).
4
Examine the three emergences
The hadith mentions three distinct emergences: first in Yemen, second near Mecca, and third when Jesus is at the Kaaba.
The first emergence does not reach Mecca; the second reaches both desert and Mecca.
5
Visualize the final emergence
The beast's head emerges from al-Ṣafā as the earth shakes; it is enormous—a horse runs three days for only a third of it. Its head touches clouds, and it is called al-Jassāsa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعُها: خُروجُ الدابَّةِ التي تُكَلِّمُ الناسَ آخِرَ الزمانِ، المشار إليها بقوله تعالى: وَإِذَا وَقَعَ الْقَوْلُ عَلَيْهِم أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُمْ دَابَّةٌ مِّنَ الْأَرْضِ تُكَلِّمُهُمْ ﴾ (۲) أَيْ: وإذا قرُبَ وقوع معنى القول عليهم، وهو ما وُعِدوا به مِنَ البَعْثِ والعذابِ، أَخْرَجْنا لهم دابَّةٌ مِنَ الأرضِ تُكلّمُهم قيلَ : تُكَلِّمُهم بيُطلانِ الأديان إلا دين الإسلام. وقيل: تقول: يا فُلانُ أَنتَ مِنْ أهل الجنّة، ويا فُلانُ أَنتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ النارِ. وقيل: تقولُ : إِنَّ النَّاسَ كانوا بآياتِنا لا يوقنون. وروي أنه سُئل عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ عنْ يَخْرجها فقالَ: مِنْ أَعظَمِ المساجدِ حُرمةً على الله تعالى، يعني المسجد الحرام. وروي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلامُ أنَّ لها ثلاثَ حَرَجاتِ: خَرْجَةٌ بأقصى اليمن، فيفشو ذِكْرُها في البادية، ولا يدخُلُ ذِكْرُها مكةَ، ثُمَّ تَمْكُثُ رَمَنَّا طويلًا. وخرْجةً قريبةٌ مِنْ مكَّةَ، فيفشو ذكرها بالبادية وبمكة، وخرجة بينما عيسى ابن مريمَ اللهُ بالبَيتِ ومعه المسلمون، إذ تهتز الأرضُ تحتهم، وينشقُ الصَّفا مما يلي المشعَرَ، فتخرُجُ رأسُ الدابَّةِ مِنَ الصَّفا، تجري الفرَسُ ثلاثة أيام، وما خرَج ثُلثها، وبعدَ خُروجها يمس رأسها السحاب، وتُسَمّى الجساسة.
The fourth of them: the emergence of the beast (al-dābba) that speaks to people at the end of time, alluded to in His statement: {And when the word falls upon them, We will bring forth for them a beast from the earth speaking to them} [Quran 27:82]. That is: when the meaning of the word, which is what they were promised of resurrection and punishment, is about to occur, We brought forth for them a beast from the earth speaking to them. It is said: it speaks to them about the nullification of religions except the religion of Islam. And it is said: it says, 'O so-and-so, you are from the people of Paradise, and O so-and-so, you are from the people of the Fire.' And it is said: it says, 'The people were not certain of Our signs.' And it is narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, was asked about its place of emergence, so he said: 'From the greatest of mosques in sanctity to God Almighty,' meaning the Sacred Mosque (al-Masjid al-Ḥarām). And it is narrated from him, peace and blessings be upon him, that it has three emergences: an emergence in the farthest part of Yemen, so its mention spreads in the desert, but its mention does not enter Mecca, then it remains for a long time. And an emergence near Mecca, so its mention spreads in the desert and in Mecca. And an emergence while Jesus son of Mary is at the House (Kaaba) and the Muslims with him, when the earth shakes beneath them, and al-Ṣafā splits from the side facing al-Mashʿar, and the beast's head emerges from al-Ṣafā. A horse runs for three days, yet only a third of it has emerged. After its emergence, its head touches the clouds, and it is called al-Jassāsa.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage describes the fourth major eschatological sign: the emergence of the Beast (dābba) that speaks to people. It begins by quoting Quran 27:82 and explains its interpretation: when the promised resurrection and punishment are near, God brings forth this beast. Several opinions are given regarding what the beast says: some say it declares the falsehood of all religions except Islam; others say it addresses individuals by name, telling them whether they are destined for Paradise or Hell; yet another opinion says it reproaches people for not believing in God's signs. The Prophet was asked about the beast's place of emergence, and he replied that it emerges from the most sacred mosque, i.e., the Sacred Mosque in Mecca. The passage then narrates that the beast has three emergences: first in the far reaches of Yemen, where its mention spreads in the countryside but not in Mecca; after a long interval, a second emergence near Mecca, where its mention spreads both in the countryside and in Mecca; finally, a third emergence at the time when Jesus son of Mary is at the Kaaba with the Muslims. At that moment, the ground shakes, al-Ṣafā splits, and the beast's head emerges from that hill. It is so enormous that a horse could run for three days and still only a third of the beast's body would have emerged. After its full emergence, its head touches the clouds. This beast is also known as al-Jassāsa (the spy).

Key Terms
الدابة
تكلّم الناس
آخر الزمان
المسجد الحرام
الصفا
الجساسة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Beast of the Earth only appears once.
Correction: The hadith specifies three distinct emergences at different times and places: first in Yemen, second near Mecca, and third during the time of Jesus.

Checkpoint
Where does the beast first emerge according to the narration?
A) In Mecca
B) In the farthest part of Yemen
C) Near the Sea of Tiberias
D) In Jerusalem

Key Takeaway
The Beast of the Earth emerges in three stages, speaks to people, and reminds us of the certainty of the Hour.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the beast will address individuals by name and tell them their eternal destination, do you feel secure in your own standing? What specific action will you take today to ensure you are among those who hear 'you are from the people of Paradise'?
?
The beast emerges from the most sacred place on earth, the Sacred Mosque. How does this challenge your sense of spiritual complacency? Are you treating the symbols of Islam with the reverence they demand, knowing they may be the very sites of the Hour's signs?
?
The beast will declare the falsehood of all religions except Islam. If you were to face that declaration right now, would your faith be proven genuine? What one doubt or compromise do you need to abandon this week to stand firm in the truth?

The Beast (Dabbah) – Emergence and Speech
Presents the fourth major eschatological sign: the Beast's emergence and three interpretations of its speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth major sign of the Hour: the emergence of the Beast, and the three interpretations of its speech based on the Qur'an and transmitted reports.

Core Idea
The Beast's speech has three transmitted interpretations—all point to the end of times.

This lesson introduces the fourth eschatological sign from the Samiyyat section: the emergence of the Beast (Dabbah). The author cites the Qur'anic verse and then presents three different explanations of what the Beast will say to people. These interpretations are not mutually exclusive but represent varying traditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation once to get the overall meaning.
Notice the Qur'anic quote and the three 'qīla' statements.
2
Identify the three interpretations
List the three interpretations of the Beast's speech as given in the text.
They are: nullification of religions except Islam, addressing individuals by name, and stating lack of certainty in signs.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why the author presents multiple interpretations without choosing one.
This shows the richness of transmitted traditions and avoids over-specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعها: خُرُوجُ الدَّابَّةِ الَّتِي تُكَلِّمُ النَّاسَ آخِرَ الزَّمَانِ، المُشَارُ إِلَيْهَا بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَإِذَا وَقَعَ الْقَوْلُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُمْ دَابَّةً مِنَ الْأَرْضِ تُكَلِّمُهُمْ﴾ أَيْ: وَإِذَا قَرُبَ وُقُوعُ مَعْنَى الْقَوْلِ عَلَيْهِمْ، وَهُوَ مَا وُعِدُوا بِهِ مِنَ الْبَعْثِ وَالْعَذَابِ، أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُمْ دَابَّةً مِنَ الْأَرْضِ تُكَلِّمُهُمْ. قِيلَ: تُكَلِّمُهُمْ بِبُطْلَانِ الْأَدْيَانِ إِلَّا دِينَ الْإِسْلَامِ. وَقِيلَ: تَقُولُ: يَا فُلَانُ أَنْتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ، وَيَا فُلَانُ أَنْتَ مِنْ أَهْلِ النَّارِ. وَقِيلَ: تَقُولُ: إِنَّ النَّاسَ كَانُوا بِآيَاتِنَا لَا يُوقِنُونَ.
The fourth of them: the emergence of the Beast that speaks to people at the end of time, referred to in His saying, Exalted is He: {And when the word falls upon them, We will bring forth for them a beast from the earth speaking to them}. Meaning: when the occurrence of the meaning of the word draws near upon them, which is what they were promised of resurrection and punishment, We bring forth for them a beast from the earth speaking to them. It is said: it speaks to them of the nullification of religions except the religion of Islam. And it is said: it says: O so-and-so, you are from the people of Paradise, and O so-and-so, you are from the people of Hellfire. And it is said: it says: Indeed the people were not certain of Our signs.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the fourth major eschatological sign: the emergence of the Beast (Dabbah). It begins by quoting the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-Naml 27:82) that mentions the Beast, then explains the meaning of 'when the word falls upon them' as the approach of resurrection and punishment. The passage then presents three different interpretations of what the Beast will say: (1) it declares the falsehood of all religions except Islam, (2) it addresses individuals directly telling them whether they are destined for Paradise or Hell, or (3) it states that people were not certain of God's signs. The author does not choose one interpretation but reports them as possibilities.

Key Terms
دابَّة (dābbah, beast)
آخر الزمان (ākhir al-zamān, end of time)
بطلان الأديان (buṭlān al-adyān, nullification of religions)
آيات (āyāt, signs)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Beast speaks only one specific statement.
Correction: The text presents three equally transmitted interpretations without preferring one, indicating that the exact wording is not fixed beyond what is transmitted.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many interpretations are given for the speech of the Beast?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Beast's emergence is a major end-time sign, and its speech is understood through three transmitted interpretations, all emphasizing the decisive separation of truth and falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Beast may address you by name, telling you your eternal destiny today. If you knew that moment was now, what single change would you make in your life before hearing your name? Will you wait until then, or act now?
?
The Beast will declare the nullification of all religions except Islam. Are there any beliefs, habits, or attachments in your heart that compete with the purity of your Islam—things you treat as 'almost true'? What would the Beast's declaration expose about your actual certainty?

The Beast (Dabbah): Emergences and Description in Hadith
Hadith narrations on the Beast's emergences and composite physical description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith narrations about the Beast's three emergences and its composite physical description.

Core Idea
The Beast emerges three times, each with distinct locations, and has a form composed from various animals.

This lesson presents hadith details about the Beast (Dabbah), one of the major signs of the Hour. The Prophet ﷺ described its three emergences, and companions provided a composite physical description. Understanding these narrations helps us grasp the transmitted signs of the end times.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith on emergence locations
Read the opening narration where the Prophet is asked about the Beast's emergence and he specifies the Sacred Mosque. Then note the three distinct emergences described.
The first two emergences are in Yemen and near Mecca, with the third being during Jesus' time.
2
Examine the third emergence in detail
Focus on the third emergence: the earth shakes, al-Safa splits, the Beast's head emerges, and it is called al-Jassasah. Observe the cosmic signs accompanying it.
The description emphasizes the Beast's enormous size: a horse runs three days but only a third of its body emerges.
3
Study the physical description
Read the hadith about the Beast's length (sixty), four legs, down, feathers, two wings, and its swiftness. Then read Ka'b al-Ahbar's composite description with parts from various animals.
The composite description uses familiar animals to convey the Beast's fearsome and unique appearance.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why these details are important in Islamic eschatology. The Beast is a confirmed sign that will appear after specific conditions, and its description underscores its extraordinary nature.
This passage is part of the Sam'iyyat (transmitted matters) that must be accepted on faith.

وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهُ سُئِلَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ عَنْ [مَخْرَجِهَا؟] فَقَالَ: مِنْ أَعْظَمِ الْمَسَاجِدِ حُرْمَةً عَلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى، يَعْنِي الْمَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامَ. وَرُوِيَ عَنْهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ أَنَّ لَهَا ثَلَاثَ خَرَجَاتٍ: خَرْجَةٌ بِأَقْصَى الْيَمَنِ، فَيَفْشُو ذِكْرُهَا فِي الْبَادِيَةِ، وَلَا يَدْخُلُ ذِكْرُهَا مَكَّةَ، ثُمَّ تَمْكُثُ زَمَنًا طَوِيلًا. وَخَرْجَةٌ قَرِيبَةٌ مِنْ مَكَّةَ، فَيَفْشُو ذِكْرُهَا بِالْبَادِيَةِ وَبِمَكَّةَ. وَخَرْجَةٌ بَيْنَمَا عِيسَى ابْنُ مَرْيَمَ [عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ] بِالْبَيْتِ وَمَعَهُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ، إِذِ اهْتَزَّتِ الْأَرْضُ تَحْتَهُمْ، وَانْشَقَّ الصَّفَا مِمَّا يَلِي الْمَشْعَرَ، فَتَخْرُجُ رَأْسُ الدَّابَّةِ مِنَ الصَّفَا، تَجْرِي الْفَرَسُ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ، وَمَا خَرَجَ ثُلْثُهَا، وَبَعْدَ خُرُوجِهَا يَمَسُّ رَأْسُهَا السَّحَابَ، وَتُسَمَّى الْجَسَّاسَةَ. الْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ: السَّمْعِيَّاتُ. وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ: أَنَّ طُولَهَا سِتُّونَ، وَلَهَا أَرْبَعُ قَوَائِمَ وَزَغَبٌ وَرِيشٌ وَجَنَاحَانِ، لَا يَفُوتُهَا هَارِبٌ وَلَا يُدْرِكُهَا طَالِبٌ. وَعَنْ كَعْبٍ: صُورَتُهَا صُورَةُ حِمَارٍ، قِيلَ: لَهَا رَأْسُ ثَوْرٍ، وَعَيْنُ خِنْزِيرٍ، وَأُذُنُ إِبِلٍ، وَعُنُقُ نَعَامَةٍ، وَصَدْرُ أَسَدٍ، وَلَوْنُ نِمِرٍّ، وَخَاصِرَةُ هِرٍّ، وَذَنَبُ كَبْشٍ، وَخُفُّ بِعِيرٍ.
And it was narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, was asked about [its place of emergence?] and he said: From the greatest of mosques in sanctity to Allah Almighty, meaning the Sacred Mosque. And it was narrated from him, peace and blessings be upon him, that it has three emergences: an emergence in the furthest part of Yemen, and its mention spreads in the desert, but its mention does not enter Mecca, then it stays for a long time. And an emergence near Mecca, and its mention spreads in the desert and in Mecca. And an emergence while Jesus son of Mary [peace and blessings be upon him] is at the House with the Muslims, when the earth trembles beneath them, and al-Safa splits from the side of al-Mash'ar, and the head of the Beast emerges from al-Safa, the horse runs for three days, and only a third of it has emerged, and after its emergence its head touches the clouds, and it is called al-Jassasah. The third section: the Sam'iyyat. And in the hadith: its length is sixty, and it has four legs, down, feathers, and two wings, no fleeing person escapes it and no seeker catches it. And from Ka'b: its image is the image of a donkey; it is said: it has the head of an ox, the eye of a pig, the ear of a camel, the neck of an ostrich, the chest of a lion, the color of a leopard, the flank of a cat, the tail of a ram, and the hoof of a camel.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith narrations and reports about the Beast (Dabbah). It begins by answering a question about the Beast's place of emergence: the Sacred Mosque. Then it describes three emergences (kharajāt): the first in Yemen, the second near Mecca, and the third at the time of Jesus when the Beast emerges from al-Safa. After this, the section header 'The third section: the Sam'iyyat' appears, indicating the start of the section on transmitted matters. The passage then provides a hadith describing the Beast's length (sixty), its four legs, down, feathers, and two wings, emphasizing its swiftness. Finally, it reports a description from Ka'b al-Ahbar giving a composite form: body of a donkey, with parts from various animals—head of an ox, eye of a pig, ear of a camel, neck of an ostrich, chest of a lion, color of a leopard, flank of a cat, tail of a ram, and hoof of a camel.

Key Terms
حرجات (kharajāt, emergences)
الجساسة (al-Jassāsah, the spy)
زغب (zaghab, down)
ريش (rīsh, feathers)
ثلاث خرجات (thalāth kharajāt, three emergences)
الصفا (al-Ṣafā)
الْمَشْعَر (al-Mash'ar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Beast emerges only once.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states that the Beast has three separate emergences (ثلاث حرجات).

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Beast will emerge three times, with the final emergence coinciding with the time of Jesus, and it has a fearsome composite form described in hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Beast emerges and no one can escape it, are you truly prepared for that day? What change do you need to make in your life today so that when that sign comes, you are found among the believers with Jesus at the Kaaba?
?
The Beast's composite form demonstrates Allah's absolute power to combine disparate creatures. Do you live with awe of His power, or do you take His signs lightly? What would it take for you to truly fear and love Him as He deserves?
?
The hadith mentions that the Beast's mention spreads first in the desert, then in Mecca. Are you among those who hear and heed the signs before they become unavoidable? What is preventing you from taking the Hereafter seriously right now?
