The Fifth Major Sign: Sun Rising from the West and Closing of Repentance
Describes the fifth major sign and debates on repentance closure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the fifth major sign (the sun rising from the west), the scholarly disagreements about its duration, and the nuanced rulings regarding the closing of repentance, including exceptions for those who are not discerning.

Core Idea
The sun rising from the west closes the door of repentance, but not for everyone.

The fifth major sign is among the most dramatic events foreshadowing the Day of Resurrection. But what exactly happens when the sun rises from the west? And does repentance truly become impossible for all? This passage from Imam Dardir's commentary explores these questions, presenting various scholarly opinions and qualifications that nuance the general ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation side by side. Let the author's own words set the stage before diving into analysis.
2
Understand the sign and its duration
Notice the description of the sign: the sun rises from the west, there is disagreement whether it lasts one or three days, and then it returns to normal until the Day of Resurrection.
3
Identify the main ruling on repentance
The passage states that at that time, the door of repentance is closed upon both the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. Then it presents an opinion that it is specific to the disbeliever, citing a Quranic verse.
4
Examine the scope and continuity
Note the questions: Is the closing specific to the accountable person (mukallaf) or general? Does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? The passage notes al-Laqani's view and then asserts the truth based on a hadith that no one's repentance is accepted from that day onward.
5
Explore the exceptions
Finally, see al-Ajhuri's correction: the non-acceptance applies only to a discerning person (mumayyiz) who witnesses the rising. Those who are non-discerning (due to childhood or insanity) and later become discerning, or are born after, have repentance accepted. Also note Ibn Abbas's view on a child disbeliever.
This shows that the ruling is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خَامِسُهَا: طُلُوعُ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِهَا، وَاخْتُلِفَ فِي ذَلِكَ، هَلْ هُوَ فِي يَوْمٍ وَاحِدٍ، أَوْ فِي ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ، ثُمَّ تَطْلُعُ مِنَ الْمَشْرِقِ عَلَى عَادَتِهَا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ، وَإِذَا طَلَعَتْ مِنَ الْمَغْرِبِ غَرَبَتْ فِي الْمَشْرِقِ، وَعِنْدَ ذَلِكَ يُغْلَقُ بَابُ التَّوْبَةِ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِ الْعَاصِي وَالْكَافِرِ، وَقِيلَ: هُوَ خَاصٌّ بِالْكَافِرِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنْفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِنْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا﴾. هَلْ ذَلِكَ خَاصٌّ بِالْمُكَلَّفِ أَوْ عَامٌّ، وَهَلْ يَسْتَمِرُّ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ؟ وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ قَوْلِ الْبُرْهَانِ اللَّقَانِيِّ فِي شَرْحِ جَوْهَرَتِهِ. الْحَقُّ أَنَّ مِنْ يَوْمِ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِهَا إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ لَا تُقْبَلُ تَوْبَةُ أَحَدٍ، كَمَا فِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ. لَكِنْ صَحَّحَ الْأَجْهُورِيُّ فِي حَاشِيَتِهِ عَلَى الرِّسَالَةِ: أَنَّ عَدَمَ قَبُولِهَا مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِ وَالْكَافِرِ خَاصٌّ بِمَنْ شَاهَدَ الطُّلُوعَ وَهُوَ مُمَيِّزٌ، أَمَّا غَيْرُ الْمُمَيِّزِ – لِصِبًا أَوْ جُنُونٍ – ثُمَّ حَصَلَ لَهُ التَّمْيِيزُ، أَوْ وُلِدَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَإِنَّهُ تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ التَّوْبَةُ. وَقَالَ فِي شَرْحِهِ عَلَى الْمُخْتَصَرِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ لَا تُقْبَلُ تَوْبَةُ الْكَافِرِ إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ صَغِيرًا، ثُمَّ أَسْلَمَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَإِنَّهَا تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ، وَأَمَّا الْمُؤْمِنُ الْمُذْنِبُ فَتُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ تَوْبَتُهُ.
The fifth of them: the rising of the sun from its west, and there is disagreement concerning that, whether it is in one day or in three days, then it rises from the east as is its custom until the Day of Resurrection, and when it rises from the west it sets in the east, and at that time the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, and it is said: it is specific to the disbeliever because of His saying, Exalted is He: {The day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith}. Is that specific to the accountable person or general, and does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? That is the apparent meaning of the saying of al-Burhan al-Laqani in his commentary on his Jawharah. The truth is that from the day of the rising of the sun from its west until the Day of Resurrection, the repentance of no one is accepted, as in the hadith of Ibn Umar. But al-Ajhuri corrected in his gloss on al-Risalah: that the non-acceptance of it from the believer and the disbeliever is specific to one who witnesses the rising while being discerning, but as for the non-discerning – due to childhood or insanity – then he becomes discerning, or is born after that, then repentance is accepted from him. And he said in his commentary on al-Mukhtasar: from Ibn Abbas, the repentance of the disbeliever is not accepted unless he was a child, then he becomes Muslim after that, then it is accepted from him, and as for the sinful believer, his repentance is accepted from him.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the fifth major eschatological sign: the sun rising from the west. It first notes a disagreement about whether this occurs in one day or three days, after which the sun returns to its normal course until the Day of Resurrection, but when it rises from the west it sets in the east. At that time, the door of repentance is closed for both the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, though some say it is only for the disbeliever, citing the Qur'anic verse that on the day of certain signs, faith after seeing them is of no benefit. The passage then raises two questions: whether the closing of repentance is specific to the accountable (mukallaf) or general, and whether it continues until the Day of Resurrection. It states that al-Laqani's apparent view is that it continues. The author asserts the truth as per the hadith of Ibn Umar that no one's repentance is accepted from that day until the Day of Resurrection. However, al-Ajhuri qualifies this: the non-acceptance applies only to a discerning (mumayyiz) person who witnesses the rising; a non-discerning person (due to childhood or insanity) who later becomes discerning, or a child born after that, can have repentance accepted. Al-Ajhuri also reports from Ibn Abbas that a disbeliever's repentance is not accepted unless he was a child who later becomes Muslim, while a sinful believer's repentance is always accepted.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس من مغربها (ṭulūʿ al-shams min maghribihā)
باب التوبة (bāb al-tawbah)
مميز (mumayyiz)
مكلف (mukallaf)
صبا (ṣibā)
جنون (junūn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that after the sun rises from the west, repentance is absolutely impossible for everyone without exception.
Correction: The passage shows that the closing of repentance applies specifically to those who witness the sign while being discerning (mumayyiz). Non-discerning individuals (due to childhood or insanity) and those born after can still have their repentance accepted.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ajhuri's correction, who is excepted from the general closing of repentance after the sun rises from the west?
A) Those who are not accountable
B) Those who are not discerning at the time of the rising
C) Only disbelievers
D) All believers

Key Takeaway
The sun rising from the west is a definitive sign that repentance is generally closed, but scholars made exceptions for those who were not discerning at the time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sun were to rise from the west tomorrow, would you be among those whose repentance is no longer accepted because you are discerning and accountable? What does your current state of faith and repentance say about your readiness for that moment?
?
Are there sins you are delaying to repent from, assuming you have time before the major signs? How does the knowledge that the door of repentance could close at any moment—especially after witnessing the sign—press you to turn back to Allah right now, without delay?
?
The sign of the sun rising from the west closes repentance only for those who witness it while being discerning. But what about those who have already died before the sign? Do you know for certain that you will still be alive to see it? If you died tonight, would your repentance be accepted—or have you been putting it off, relying on a future that is not guaranteed?

The Beast of the Earth: A Major Sign of the Hour
Describes the Beast of the Earth as a major sign of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the Beast of the Earth as a major eschatological sign, based on transmitted hadith and reports.

Core Idea
The Beast of the Earth is a fearsome creature whose description inspires awe of the Last Day.

In this lesson, we examine one of the major signs of the Hour: the Beast of the Earth (dābbat al-arḍ). The passage presents two complementary descriptions: a concise hadith and a more elaborate composite portrayal from Ka‘b al-Aḥbār. Together, they convey the extraordinary and terrifying nature of this creature, reminding believers of the reality of the Hour and the importance of faith in the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its rhythm, then read the literal translation. Notice how the hadith gives a brief overview while Ka‘b’s report adds vivid details.
The passage is from the section on transmitted matters (sam‘iyyāt).
2
Compare the two descriptions
Identify what the hadith mentions (length, legs, fur, wings, speed) and what Ka‘b adds (parts from various animals). Ask yourself why both are included.
Ka‘b’s description is not meant to be a literal animal but a symbolic composite.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why scholars transmit such descriptions. They serve to emphasize the power and awe of the Last Day, reinforcing the need for belief and preparation.
Such descriptions are common in eschatological reports to make the unseen tangible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات. وفي الحديث: أن طولها ستون، ولها أربعة قوائم وزغب وريس وجناحان، لا يفوتها هاربٌ ولا يُدْرِكُها طالبٌ. وعن كعب: صورتها صورة حمار، قيل: لها رأسُ ثَورِ، وَعَينُ خِنْزِيرٍ، وَأَذَنُ إِبِلِ، وعنق نعامة، وصدرُ أسَدٍ، وَلَونُ نِمرٍ، وخاصرةُ هِر، وذنبُ كَبِشِ، وَخُفٌ بِعِيرِ.
The third section: the transmitted matters. And in the hadith: that its length is sixty, and it has four legs, and fur, and feathers, and two wings; no fleeing one escapes it, nor does any pursuer overtake it. And from Ka'b: its form is the form of a donkey; it is said: it has the head of an ox, the eye of a pig, the ear of a camel, the neck of an ostrich, the chest of a lion, the color of a leopard, the flank of a cat, the tail of a ram, and the hoof of a camel.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage describes the beast of the earth (dābbat al-arḍ) as one of the major signs of the Hour under the section of transmitted matters (sam'iyyāt). It begins by citing a hadith that gives its length as sixty (likely cubits or arms), its four legs, fur, feathers, and two wings, emphasizing that it cannot be escaped nor overtaken, highlighting its fearsome speed. Then it reports from Ka'b al-Aḥbār a more detailed composite description: its form is like a donkey, but its parts come from various animals—head of an ox, eye of a pig, ear of a camel, neck of an ostrich, chest of a lion, color of a leopard, flank of a cat, tail of a ram, and hoof of a camel. This enumeration of different animal parts is not meant to be taken literally in a zoological sense but rather to convey its extraordinary and terrifying appearance, as is common in descriptions of eschatological signs.

Key Terms
دابة الأرض
السمعيات
أشراط الساعة
حديث
كعب الأحبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the description is a literal animal that can be found in nature.
Correction: The composite description is a symbolic depiction meant to convey awe and fear, not a zoological classification.

Checkpoint

B) Fifty
C) Sixty

Key Takeaway
The Beast of the Earth is described in transmitted reports with extraordinary features that underscore its role as a terrifying sign of the Last Day.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Beast is described as inescapable—no one can flee from it. Is there something in your faith that you have been trying to outrun or avoid? What would it take to stop running and face it?
?
The composite parts of the Beast combine fearsome qualities from many animals. What fears about the Day of Judgment do you habitually push aside? How can you begin to truly prepare your heart for that encounter starting tonight?

The Sun Rising from the West and the Closure of Repentance
Describes the sign and the debate over repentance closure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the sign of the sun rising from the west and the condition of repentance after it, including differing scholarly views and exceptions.

Core Idea
The sign of the sun rising from the west closes repentance, but the closure is nuanced and not absolute.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer explains the fifth major sign of the Hour: the sun rising from the west. He presents different opinions about its duration and, most importantly, the effect on repentance. This teaching clarifies a common misunderstanding and provides a detailed ruling based on hadith and scholarly commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the sign
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the description of the sun rising from the west and the initial disagreement about its duration.
Focus on the phrasing: 'خامسها: طلوع الشمسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِها'.
2
Understand the general closure of repentance
The passage states that when the sun rises from the west, the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, citing Quran 6:158. Reflect on why this sign is so significant.
Note the verse is used as evidence.
3
Explore the scholarly opinions
The author presents al-Laqani's view that the closure is general until the Day of Resurrection, then the correct view from hadith, and finally al-Ajhuri's correction that it applies only to discerning witnesses.
Al-Ajhuri's exception is key: non-discerning (youth, insane) can repent later.
4
Apply the nuance to real cases
Consider the examples given: a young child who later reaches discernment, an insane person who recovers, or a person born after the sign. According to al-Ajhuri, their repentance is accepted.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
5
Synthesize the final ruling
Summarize the position: repentance is not accepted from those who witness the sign while discerning (mumayyiz), but is accepted from others, including the disobedient believer who repents after the sign.
This is the nuanced understanding.

خامسها: طلوع الشمسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِها، واختُلِفَ في ذلك، هل هو في يوم واحد، أو في ثلاثةِ أَيَّامٍ، ثُمَّ تَطْلُعُ مِنَ الْمَشْرِقِ على عادتها إلى يَومِ القيامةِ، وإذا طَلَعَتْ مِنَ الْمَغْرِبِ غَرَبتْ في المشرق، وعِندَ ذلك يُغلَقُ باب التوبة على المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل: وخاص بالكافِرِ لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ءَايَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْساً إِيمَانَهَا لَم تَكُنْ ءَامَنَتْ مِن قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْراً﴾. وهل ذلك خاص بالمكلف أو عام، وهل يستمِرُّ إلى يوم القيامةِ؟ وهو ظاهرُ قَولِ البرهان اللقاني في شَرحِ جَوهَرَتِه. الحقُّ أَنَّ مِنْ يَومِ طُلوعِ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِها إِلى يَومِ القيامةِ لا تُقبَلُ تَوبةُ أَحَدٍ، كما في حديث ابنِ عُمَرَ. لكن صحَّحَ الأجهوري في حاشيته على الرسالة: أَنَّ عَدَمَ قَبولِها مِنَ المُؤمِنِ والكافر خاص بمَنْ شاهَدَ الطَّلوع وهو مميز، أما غَيرُ المُميّز - لصباً أو جُنون - ثُمَّ حصل له التمييز، أو وُلِدَ بعْدَ ذلك فإنه تُقبَلُ مِنه التَّوبة، وقالَ فِي شَرْحِه على المختصر (٣): عن ابن عبّاس لا تُقبل توبة الكافر إلا إذا كانَ صغيرًا، ثُمَّ أَسْلَمَ بعد ذلك فإنَّها تُقبَلُ منه، وأما المؤمنُ المذنب فتقبلُ منه تَوبتُه.
Its fifth: the rising of the sun from its west, and there is disagreement concerning that: is it in one day or in three days, then it rises from the east as usual until the Day of Resurrection? And when it rises from the west, it sets in the east, and at that time the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. And it is said: it is specific to the disbeliever due to His saying, exalted: 'On the day when some signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good through its faith.' And is that specific to the accountable person or general? And does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? That is apparent from the statement of al-Burhān al-Laqānī in his commentary on his Jawhara. The truth is that from the day of the sun's rising from its west until the Day of Resurrection, no one's repentance is accepted, as in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. But al-Ajhūrī corrected in his gloss on al-Risāla: that the non-acceptance of it from the believer and the disbeliever is specific to the one who witnessed the rising while discerning (mumayyiz). As for the non-discerning – due to youth or insanity – then later discernment occurs, or one is born after that, then repentance is accepted from him. And he said in his commentary on al-Mukhtaṣar (3): from Ibn 'Abbās: the repentance of the disbeliever is not accepted unless he was young, then he embraced Islam after that, then it is accepted from him. As for the disobedient believer, his repentance is accepted from him.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth major sign of the Hour: the sun rising from the west. It begins by noting disagreement about whether this happens in one day or three days, after which the sun returns to rising from the east as usual until the Day of Resurrection. When it rises from the west, it sets in the east. At that time, the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. Some hold it is specific to the disbeliever, citing the verse (6:158) that mentions that when some signs come, faith does not benefit those who had not previously believed. The author then raises questions: is the closure specific to the accountable person or general, and does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? The apparent view of al-Burhān al-Laqānī in his commentary on al-Jawhara is that it is general. The correct view (al-ḥaqq) is that from the day of the sun's rising from the west until the Day of Resurrection, no one's repentance is accepted, as in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. However, al-Ajhūrī corrects this in his gloss on al-Risāla, explaining that the non-acceptance is specific to those who witness the rising while being discerning (mumayyiz, i.e., of sound mind and age). As for the non-discerning—due to youth or insanity—then later attain discernment, or are born after that sign, their repentance is accepted. He further reports from Ibn 'Abbās in his commentary on al-Mukhtaṣar that the repentance of a disbeliever is not accepted unless he was young (i.e., before the sign) and then embraced Islam after the sign, then it is accepted. As for the disobedient believer, his repentance is accepted (even after the sign). Thus, the passage resolves the apparent contradiction between the absolute closure of repentance and the possibility of acceptance for those who were not accountable at the time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Repentance is absolutely closed for everyone after the sun rises from the west.
Correction: Al-Ajhūrī clarifies that the closure applies only to those who witness the sign while being discerning (mumayyiz); others, such as the insane, children, or those born after, may still have their repentance accepted.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ajhūrī, for whom is repentance not accepted after the sun rises from the west?
A) All believers and disbelievers
B) Only disbelievers
C) The one who sees it while being discerning (mumayyiz)
D) Only believers who are disobedient

Key Takeaway
The closure of repentance after the sun rises from the west is not absolute; it applies to those who witness it while discerning, but others may still repent, and the disobedient believer's repentance is always accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sun were to rise from the west tomorrow, would you be among those who are discerning and thus have their repentance closed? What would that mean for the sins you are currently indulging in? How does this realization shake you out of complacency about your own repentance right now?
?
You claim to be a believer, but are you truly repenting from your sins now, while the door is still wide open? What if you delay repentance, only to die before the sign, or worse, witness the sign while still stained with sin? How does this lesson confront your assumption that you have unlimited time to turn back to Allah?
?
The passage mentions that the closure is not absolute; even after the sign, those who were not discerning (e.g., children) can still repent. But you are not a child. You are responsible and accountable. How does this knowledge make your current negligence in repentance more blameworthy? What will you change today?
